The Four Witnesses and the Explicit Word 'Zina'
Ruling on the requirement of four witnesses testifying with the word 'zina'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for proving zina through testimony and explain why the word 'zina' is mandatory.

Core Idea
Zina is proven only by four male witnesses who explicitly say 'zina' in a unified session.

This lesson unpacks the strict procedural conditions for proving zina in a Hanafi court. The testimony must meet exacting standards: four men, using the specific word 'zina', in one session. Beyond the technical rules, we explore the wisdom behind concealment and when speaking out becomes obligatory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its Quranic basis
Read the first part of the passage that states zina is established by four witnesses with the word 'zina'. Note the Quranic references (4:15 and 24:4) and the hadith about the man who accused his wife.
The imperative 'fastashhidu' indicates obligation in Hanafi usul.
2
Recognize the requirement of four male witnesses
The text explicitly requires four men; women's testimony is not accepted in hadd cases. The phrase 'أربعة من الرجال' is derived from the Quranic 'أربعة منكم' and the inclusion of the feminine tā' in the number indicates male witnesses.
Hanafi: women cannot testify in zina cases, unlike financial transactions.
3
Understand why only the word 'zina' is accepted
The author stipulates 'بالزنا لا بالوطء والجماع'. The word 'zina' clearly denotes unlawful intercourse. Synonyms like 'wat' (coitus) or 'jima' (intercourse) are ambiguous because they can apply to lawful relations.
The language is precise to avoid false accusations.
4
Distinguish between concealment and obligation
The passage explains that testifying is generally against better practice (makruh tanzih) to uphold concealment. However, if zina becomes open and brazen, testifying becomes wajib to enforce the hadd and cleanse society.
This is a crucial nuance: the ruling changes with context.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( ويثبت بشهادة أربعة بالزنا لا بالوطء والجماع) أي يثبت الزنا عند الحاكم ظاهراً بشهادة أربعة من الرجال يشهدون بلفظ الزنا لا بلفظ الوطء والجماع لقوله تعالى فاستشهدوا عليهن أربعة منكم [النساء : ١٥] وقال تعالى ثم لم يأتوا بأربعة شهداء [النور: ٤] وقال عليه السلام للذي قذف امرأته : انت بأربعة يشهدون على صدق مقالتك. ولأن في اشتراط الأربع تحقيق معنى الستر وهو مندوب إليه بقوله عليه السلام «من ستر مسلماً ستره الله في الدنيا والآخرة» (۱) والإشاعة ضده. فعلى هذا فالشهادة بالزنا خلاف الأولى التي مرجعها إلى كراهة التنزية لأنها في رتبة الندب في جانب الفعل وكراهته التنزية في جانب الترك، ويجب أن يكون بالنسبة إلى من لم يعتد بالزنا ولم يتهتك به، أما إذا وصل الحال إلى إشاعته والتهتك به بل بعضهم ربما افتخر به فيجب كون الشهادة أولى من تركها لأن مطلوب الشارع إخلاء الأرض عن المعاصي والفواحش وذلك يتحقق بالتوبة من الغافلين وبالزجر لهم، فإذا أظهر حال الشره في الزنا مثلاً والشرب وعدم مبالاته فإخلاء الأرض حينئذ بالحدود، وعلى هذا ذكره في غير مجلس القاضي. وأداء الشهادة بمنزلة الغيبة فيه يحرم منه ما يحرم منها ويحل منه ما يحل منها وسيأتي في الشهادات أنه لا بد من الذكورة في الشهود لإدخال التاء في العدد في المنصوص. وأطلقهم فشمل ما إذا كان الزوج أحدهم خلافاً للشافعي، هو يقول هو متهم، ونحن نقول التهمة ما توجب جر نفع والزوج مدخل على نفسه بهذه الشهادة لحوق العار وخلو الفراش خصوصاً إذا كان له منها أولاد وقيده في الظهيرية بأن لا يكون الزوج قذفها فلو كان قد قذفها وشهد بالزنا ومعه ثلاثة حد الثلاثة للقذف وعلى الزوج اللعان لأن شهادة الزوج لم تقبل لمكان التهمة لأنه بشهادته يسعى في دفع اللعان عن نفسه اهـ. فعلى هذا لو قال بعض الشهود إن فلاناً قد زنى أو قال له زنيت ثم جاء وشهد عند القاضي لا تقبل شهادته لما ذكر في الزوج. وفي المحيط ولو شهدوا على المرأة أحدهم زوجها بالزنا بابن زوجها مطاوعة لا تجوز شهادة الزوج، دخل بها أو لم يدخل لوجود التهمة لأنه ربما يريد إسقاط المهر قبل الدخول وإسقاط النفقة بعد الدخول ويحد الثلاثة ولا يحد الزوج اهـ. ولا بد من اتحاد المجلس لصحة الشهادة حتى لو شهدوا متفرقين لا تقبل شهادتهم لقول عمر رضي الله عنه: لو جاؤوا مثل ربيعة ومضر فرادى الجلدتهم. وفي الظهيرية : لو جاؤوا متفرقين يحدون حد القذف ولو جاؤوا فرادى وقعدوا مقعد الشهود وقام إلى القاضي واحد بعد واحد قبلت شهادتهم وإن كان خارج المسجد حدوا جميعاً ا وإنما اشترط لفظ الزنا الدال على فعل الحرام لا لفظ الوطء والجماع، وظاهر كلام المصنف أنه لا لفظ يقوم مقام لفظ الزنا.
His statement: (And it is established by the testimony of four [witnesses] with [the word] 'zina', not with 'wat' or 'jima') i.e., zina is established before the judge apparently by the testimony of four men who testify with the word 'zina', not with the word 'wat' or 'jima', due to His statement 'And seek testimony of four witnesses from among you' [Quran 4:15] and His statement 'Then they did not bring four witnesses' [Quran 24:4] and his statement, peace be upon him, to the one who accused his wife: 'You [need] four witnesses to testify to the truth of your statement.' And because in requiring the four, there is realization of the meaning of concealment, which is recommended by his statement, peace be upon him: 'Whoever conceals a Muslim, Allah will conceal him in this world and the Hereafter,' and spreading it is its opposite. On this basis, bearing witness to zina is against the better practice, which goes back to dislike of tanzih, because it is in the rank of recommendation on the side of action and its dislike of tanzih on the side of abandonment, and it must be in relation to one who is not accustomed to zina and not brazen about it. However, if the situation reaches the point of its becoming widespread and brazen, and some may even boast about it, then bearing witness becomes more important than abstaining from it, because the intent of the Lawgiver is to empty the earth of sins and immoralities, and that is achieved through repentance of the heedless and deterrence for them. If a person shows the state of greed in zina, for example, and drinking, and carelessness, then emptying the earth at that time is through the prescribed punishments. This is mentioned regarding [testimony] outside the court of the judge. And performing testimony is like ghaybah (backbiting): what is forbidden in it is forbidden, and what is permitted in it is permitted. It will come in the chapter of testimonies that it is necessary for the witnesses to be male due to the inclusion of the feminine [tā] in the number in the revealed text. And they [the jurists] stated it generally, so it includes if the husband is among them, contrary to al-Shafi'i. He says he is suspect, but we say: suspicion is what causes drawing of benefit, and the husband brings upon himself through this testimony the befalling of disgrace and emptying of the bed, especially if he has children from her. And it is restricted in al-Zahiriyyah to the husband not having accused her [of zina]. If he had accused her and then testified to zina along with three others, the three are flogged for slander, and the husband must undergo li'an, because his testimony is not accepted due to suspicion, as by his testimony he seeks to ward off li'an from himself. On this basis, if one of the witnesses says 'So-and-so has committed zina' or says 'You committed zina' and then comes and testifies before the judge, his testimony is not accepted, due to what was mentioned regarding the husband. And in al-Muhit: If they testify against a woman, one of them being her husband, for zina with her [step-]son willingly, the husband's testimony is not permissible, whether he has consummated or not, due to the presence of suspicion, because he may want to drop the mahr before consummation or drop the maintenance after consummation; the three are flogged and the husband is not flogged. And it is necessary that the session be unified for the validity of the testimony, such that if they testify separately, their testimony is not accepted, because of the statement of 'Umar, may Allah be pleased with him: 'If they came like Rabi'a and Mudar one by one, I would flog them.' And in al-Zahiriyyah: If they come separately, they are flogged with the slander punishment; if they come individually and sit in the place of witnesses and get up to the judge one after another, their testimony is accepted, and if they were outside the mosque, they are all flogged. And the word 'zina' indicating the forbidden act is stipulated, not the words 'wat' and 'jima'. And the apparent meaning of the author's statement is that no word can stand in place of the word 'zina'.
Source pages p. 7

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the matn condition that zina must be proven by the testimony of four male witnesses who explicitly use the word 'zina'. The author cites Quranic verses (4:15, 24:4) and the hadith about slander. The rationale is to promote concealment of sins, as recommended by hadith. However, the ruling differs for habitual sinners: if zina is open and brazen, testifying becomes better than silence to deter evil. The passage also addresses nuances: the husband can be a witness unless there is conflict of interest (e.g., he previously accused her). The witnesses must come together in one session; if they come separately, their testimony is rejected and they may be flogged for slander. The key point is that only the word 'zina' suffices; 'wat' or 'jima' are not acceptable.

Key Terms
الزنا (al-zina): Sexual intercourse between a man and a woman who are not married to each other, and without a valid shubhat nikah.
شهادة (shahada): Testimony given in court; for zina, requires four male witnesses.
التهمة (al-tuhma): Suspicion of bias or interest that disqualifies a witness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because only 'zina' explicitly denotes unlawful intercourse; other words can apply to lawful acts.
C) Because 'wat' and 'jima' are not Arabic words.
D) Because the Quran uses 'zina' exclusively.

Key Takeaway
The testimony for zina requires four male witnesses, the explicit word 'zina', and a unified session; testifying is generally avoided but becomes obligatory when sin is open.

Testifying to Zina: When Is It Disliked and When Obligatory?
Explains the wisdom behind four witnesses and the ruling on testifying.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on testifying to zina and explain when it becomes wajib instead of makruh tanzihi.

Core Idea
Testifying to zina is normally makruh tanzihi; it becomes wajib only when the sinner is flagrant.

This lesson explores the wisdom behind the requirement of four witnesses for zina and the Hanafi ruling on testifying. You will learn why testifying is normally considered contrary to the recommended act of concealment (sitr), and when it becomes obligatory to enforce the hudud punishment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
The act is bearing witness to zina. The default ruling in the Hanafi school is makruh tanzihi (slightly disliked) because it contradicts the recommended act of concealment.
The ruling is based on the hadith encouraging concealment of faults.
2
Understand the wisdom behind the four-witness requirement
Requiring four witnesses promotes sitr (concealment) by making it difficult to prove zina. This aligns with the Shari'ah's preference for covering faults.
The hadith: 'Whoever covers a Muslim, Allah will cover him in this world and the next.'
3
Recognize the condition that changes the ruling
If the accused is flagrant—openly committing zina, boasting, and showing no shame—then the purpose shifts to deterrence, and testifying becomes wajib to uphold the hadd punishment.
Flagrancy nullifies the recommendation of concealment.
4
Apply the ruling to different scenarios
Practice distinguishing between a private sinner (testifying is disliked) and a flagrant sinner (testifying is obligatory) using the criteria from the text.
The text also compares testimony to backbiting: what is prohibited in backbiting is prohibited in testimony.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عليه السلام للذي قذف امرأته : انت بأربعة يشهدون على صدق مقالتك. ولأن في اشتراط الأربع تحقيق معنى الستر وهو مندوب إليه بقوله عليه السلام «من ستر مسلماً ستره الله في الدنيا والآخرة» والإشاعة ضده. فعلى هذا فالشهادة بالزنا خلاف الأولى التي مرجعها إلى كراهة التنزية لأنها في رتبة الندب في جانب الفعل وكراهته التنزية في جانب الترك، ويجب أن يكون بالنسبة إلى من لم يعتد بالزنا ولم يتهتك به، أما إذا وصل الحال إلى إشاعته والتهتك به بل بعضهم ربما افتخر به فيجب كون الشهادة أولى من تركها لأن مطلوب الشارع إخلاء الأرض عن المعاصي والفواحش وذلك يتحقق بالتوبة من الغافلين وبالزجر لهم، فإذا أظهر حال الشره في الزنا مثلاً والشرب وعدم مبالاته فإخلاء الأرض حينئذ بالحدود، وعلى هذا ذكره في غير مجلس القاضي. وأداء الشهادة بمنزلة الغيبة فيه يحرم منه ما يحرم منها ويحل منه ما يحل منها وسيأتي في الشهادات أنه لا بد من الذكورة في الشهود لإدخال التاء في العدد في المنصوص.
Peace be upon him to the one who accused his wife: 'You must bring four witnesses to testify to the truth of your statement.' And because in requiring four there is the realization of the meaning of concealment (sitr), which is recommended by his saying (peace be upon him): 'Whoever covers (the fault of) a Muslim, Allah will cover him in the world and the Hereafter,' and spreading (the news) is its opposite. Based on this, testifying to zina is khilaf al-awla, which amounts to makruh tanzihi, because it is on the level of recommendation in the aspect of action and its dislike (tanzihi) in the aspect of abandonment. And it is required that this applies to one who is not accustomed to zina and not openly flagrant. However, if the situation reaches the point of spreading it and being flagrant, and some even boast about it, then testifying becomes more meritorious than leaving it, because the Lawgiver's objective is to clear the earth of sins and immoralities, and that is achieved by repentance of the heedless and by deterring them. So when a person displays the state of being voracious in zina, for example, and drinking and lack of concern, then clearing the earth at that time is through the prescribed punishments. And on this basis, he mentioned it outside the court. And performing testimony is like backbiting: what is prohibited in backbiting is prohibited in it, and what is permissible in it is permissible. And it will come in the chapter on testimonies that masculinity is required in the witnesses, because the feminine 'ta' enters into the number in the text.
Source pages p. 8

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq begins by citing the hadith that the one who accuses his wife must bring four witnesses to confirm his statement. The author then explains the wisdom behind requiring four witnesses: it promotes the virtue of covering faults (sitr), which is recommended by the hadith 'Whoever covers a Muslim, Allah will cover him.' Spreading accusations is contrary to this virtue. Therefore, testifying to zina is normally considered khilaf al-awla (contrary to what is better), meaning it is makruh tanzihi (disliked but not sinful). This is because the act of testifying is on the level of a recommended act, and its abandonment is on the level of a disliked (tanzihi) act. However, this ruling applies only when the accused is not habitual or flagrant in sin. If a person openly commits zina, boasts about it, and shows no concern, then testifying becomes more meritorious than remaining silent, because the Shari'ah aims to eliminate sin from the earth through repentance and deterrence. In such cases, the prescribed punishments serve as a deterrent. The author also equates bearing witness to zina with backbiting (ghiba) in terms of what is permitted and prohibited, and notes that masculinity is a condition for witnesses, as indicated by the masculine plural form in the Quranic text.

Key Terms
خلاف الأولى (khilaf al-awla): An act that is contrary to what is better; in Hanafi fiqh it amounts to makruh tanzihi.
الستر (al-sitr): Concealing the faults of others, a recommended act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the default ruling for testifying to zina in the Hanafi school?
A) Wajib because zina is a major sin.
B) Makruh tanzih because it contradicts the recommended act of concealment.
C) Sunnah because it helps enforce the hadd.
D) Haram because it spreads immorality.

Key Takeaway
Testifying to zina is normally makruh tanzihi; it becomes wajib only when the sinner is flagrant, as determined by the Shari'ah's objective of deterrence.

Husband as Witness for Zina: Hanafi Conditions and the Shafi'i Dispute
Ruling and conditions for husband's testimony in zina, with Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the husband as a witness for zina, identify the conditions for his testimony, and state the requirement of unity of session for all four witnesses.

Core Idea
The husband's testimony is valid in Hanafi law because he gains no benefit, but is void if he has already accused his wife.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses two critical conditions for testimony in zina cases: whether the husband can be among the four witnesses, and the necessity of all witnesses testifying in the same session. The Hanafi school allows the husband with a condition, while Imam al-Shafi'i rejects it entirely. Understanding this dispute reveals the Hanafi definition of tuhma (self-interest) and the strict procedural safeguards for hadd punishments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and opposing positions
The author states the general rule that four witnesses are required for zina, and then notes that the husband can be one of them, contrary to Shafi'i. Identify the core question: Is the husband eligible to testify against his wife?
Shafi'i considers the husband mutaham (accused of self-interest).
2
Analyze the Hanafi definition of tuhma
The Hanafi response is that tuhma only applies when the witness stands to gain a benefit. The husband brings disgrace and an empty bed upon himself, especially if he has children. Thus, he is not benefiting.
This is a rational (aqli) argument focusing on the nature of benefit.
3
Note the exception from al-Zahiriyyah
If the husband has already accused his wife of zina (qadhf), his later testimony is rejected because he seeks to avoid li'an. The condition is that the husband must not be a qadhif.
This exception prevents the husband from using testimony to escape the consequences of his own accusation.
4
Understand the unity of session condition
The passage quotes Umar's statement that if witnesses come individually, they would be flogged. All four must testify in the same session (ittihad al-majlis). However, if they come separately but sit in the witness seat and approach the judge one by one, it is still considered one session.
The key is the presence of all witnesses at the same time, even if they testify sequentially.
5
Apply to cases from the text
The text gives an example where the husband testifies that his wife committed zina with her son. His testimony is invalid because he might want to drop mahr or maintenance. In another example, if some witnesses say 'So-and-so committed zina' and then testify, their testimony is not accepted due to tuhma.
Compare these with the condition that the husband has not qadhf'd.

And he (the author) made it general, so it includes when the husband is one of them, contrary to al-Shafi'i, who says he is accused (mutaham). We say: 'Tuhma' (accusation of self-interest) is what brings benefit. The husband brings upon himself disgrace and an empty bed by this testimony, especially if he has children from her. And al-Zahiriyyah restricted it to the case where the husband has not already accused her of zina (qadhf). If he had accused her and then testified with three others, the three are punished for qadhf, and the husband must perform li'an, because his testimony is not accepted due to tuhma, as he seeks to avert li'an from himself. Based on this, if some witnesses say 'So-and-so committed zina' or 'he said you committed zina' and then they come and testify before the judge, their testimony is not accepted for the reason mentioned concerning the husband. And in al-Muhit: If they testify against a woman, one of them being her husband, that she committed zina with her son willingly, the husband's testimony is not valid, whether he has consummated or not, because of tuhma: he might want to drop the mahr before consummation or drop maintenance after consummation. The three are punished with hadd for qadhf, and the husband is not punished. And unity of the session is necessary for the validity of testimony; even if they testify separately, their testimony is not accepted, due to the saying of Umar (may Allah be pleased with him): 'If they came like Rabi'ah and Mudar individually, I would flog them.' And in al-Zahiriyyah: If they come separately, they are punished with the hadd of qadhf. And if they come individually and sit in the witness seat and approach the judge one by one, their testimony is accepted, even if they are outside the mosque, they are all punished.
Source pages p. 8

Commentary
This passage discusses two conditions for the testimony of zina: (1) the husband cannot be among the four witnesses, and (2) the four must testify in a single session. The author first mentions that the general rule of requiring four witnesses includes the husband, but Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, considering the husband an interested party (mutaham). The Hanafi response is that 'tuhma' applies only when the witness stands to gain a benefit. The husband, by testifying, brings disgrace and an empty bed upon himself, especially if he has children, so he is not gaining a benefit. However, al-Zahiriyyah qualifies this: if the husband has already accused his wife of zina (qadhf), then his subsequent testimony is rejected because he is trying to avoid li'an. The text then cites a case from al-Muhit where the husband testifies that his wife committed zina with her son; his testimony is invalid due to tuhma (he might want to avoid mahr or maintenance). The second condition is unity of the majlis (session). The hadith of Umar states that if witnesses come individually, they would be flogged (for qadhf). However, if they come one after another but sit in the witness seat and the judge calls them one by one, their testimony is accepted. The key is that they must all be present in the same session.

Key Terms
التهمة (al-tuhma): Accusation of self-interest that disqualifies a witness.
اتحاد المجلس (ittihad al-majlis): The condition that all four witnesses must testify in the same session.
قذف (qadhf): False accusation of zina that triggers hadd punishment.

B) Because he brings disgrace and an empty bed upon himself.
C) Because the wife's consent is not required.
D) Because the husband is the guardian.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school allows the husband as a witness for zina unless he has already accused his wife, and requires all four witnesses to testify in one session.

Required Wording and Judge's Inquiry in Zina Testimony
Required Wording and Judge's Inquiry in Zina Testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi requirement for the wording of zina testimony and explain why the judge must investigate details and conduct secret tazkiya.

Core Idea
The word 'zina' or an explicit description is required; the judge must probe every detail to prevent error in hadd.

In hadd cases, the stakes are high—the penalty of death by stoning. The Hanafi school therefore imposes strict procedural safeguards. This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies that the word 'zina' must be used or the act described so explicitly that no doubt remains. Moreover, the judge cannot rely on a witness's apparent integrity; he must secretly verify it. These rules aim to avert the hadd in cases of doubt (shubha).

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested wording
The passage explains that the word 'zina' is required, not general terms like 'wati'' or 'jima''. But note: if witnesses explain the act in detail (e.g., 'like a stick in a kohl container'), that suffices. So the requirement is for an unambiguous description of the forbidden act.
2
Understand the judge's investigative duty
The judge must ask about the nature, manner, place, time, and the woman (mazanniyya). Why? To rule out any possibility that the act was halal (e.g., if she is his wife). This is a wajib (obligatory) part of the procedure.
3
Grasp the tazkiya requirement
The judge must not accept mere apparent integrity (zahir al-adala). He must conduct secret tazkiya: sending a paper with the witnesses' names to discreetly inquire about their reliability. This is a precaution to avoid executing the hadd on flawed testimony.
4
Note the effect of explanations
The witnesses' explanation of the manner ('like a stick...') is an additional description to ensure clarity. The text says it is 'an additional explanation to avoid (the hadd)'—meaning it helps ensure accuracy. If they only say 'zina' without details, the judge may still require more.
5
Contrast with other cases
In other rights (financial etc.), the judge may rely on apparent integrity. But in hadd, secret tazkiya is required per Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (Sahibayn). This shows the heightened caution for hudud.

Source pages p. 9

Commentary
This passage addresses two interrelated points: the required wording in zina testimony and the judge's investigative duty. The author of the sharh first comments on the matn's stipulation that the word 'zina' must be used, not general terms like 'wati'' (intercourse) or 'jima'' (copulation). However, if witnesses explain the act with sufficient detail (e.g., 'like a stick in a kohl container'), that explanation stands in place of the word 'zina' and the testimony is accepted. The judge must also question the witnesses about the nature, manner, place, time, and the woman (mazanniyya) to eliminate any possibility of doubt (shubha) that could avert the hadd. The text notes that the judge should not rely on the apparent integrity of the witnesses merely by stating they are Muslims not apparently corrupt; rather, a more thorough investigation is required, which includes secret inquiries (tazkiya sirran). The procedure for secret tazkiya involves the judge sending a paper with the witnesses' names to gather information about their uprightness. This is a precautionary measure to avoid executing the hadd if there is any doubt.

Key Terms
المزنية (al-mazanniyya): The woman with whom zina was allegedly committed.
التعديل سراً (al-ta'dil sirran): Secret verification of witnesses' integrity by the judge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) He asks the accused about the witnesses.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi hudud, the testimony must be explicit, and the judge must thoroughly investigate and verify witnesses secretly to avoid unjust punishment.

Conditions for Zina Testimony and Witness Verification
Explaining the requirement of specificity in zina testimony and the procedure for tazkiyah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi requirements for zina testimony and apply the principle of dar' al-hadd to determine when the hadd is averted.

Core Idea
Zina testimony demands extreme specificity—every doubt must be exhausted before the hadd can be applied.

Zina (unlawful sexual intercourse) is a crime punishable by severe hadd (flogging or stoning). However, the Hanafi school, following the principle of 'ward off the hadd by doubts' (dar' al-hadd bi al-shubuhat), requires extraordinary specificity in testimony. This lesson unpacks the five areas the judge must investigate and the procedure for verifying witnesses (tazkiyah). These rules ensure that no one is punished unless the act is proven beyond any plausible doubt.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five areas of specificity
The passage lists five elements the judge must ask about: mahiyyah (essence, i.e., insertion), kayfiyyah (modality, willing or forced), makan (place, to exclude dar al-harb), zaman (time, to exclude childhood or staleness), and al-mazniyyah (identity of the woman, to exclude ownership). Each area addresses a distinct potential doubt.
The graphic phrase 'like a kohl stick in a kohl container' clarifies the required level of detail.
2
Understand the rationale: dar' al-hadd bi al-shubuhat
The entire procedure is a mechanism to avert the hadd. Every question probes for a possible doubt (shubha). If any doubt exists, the hadd is averted. This is derived from the hadith that 'the eyes commit zina' – witnesses might mean only looking, not intercourse.
This approach distinguishes Hanafis from schools that accept general testimony.
3
Apply to incomplete testimony scenarios
The passage gives cases: if witnesses merely say 'they committed zina' without specifics, the accused is not hadded, and the witnesses are not punished for qadhf (false accusation) unless they clearly lie. If the woman is unknown, no hadd; even if witnesses later name her, still no hadd because they were suspect.
Confession is treated differently: one who confesses to zina with an unknown woman is hadded because he knows his own act.
4
Note the tazkiyah requirement
Even after specifics, witnesses must be verified (ta'dil). This is done secretly (by sending a paper to a reliable person) or openly. The judge must not rely on his own knowledge of probity in zina cases, to maximize caution.
In non-hadd cases, the judge may rely on apparent probity; here he must investigate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And the woman with whom zina is committed, if they explain and say: 'We saw him having intercourse with her like a kohl stick in a kohl container, and they modify (the witnesses) secretly and openly, then (the hadd) is executed. (This) stands in place of the word 'zina'. For if they testified that he committed zina by unlawful intercourse, it is not established (for hadd). And he indicated by his saying 'by zina' that if two men testified that he committed zina and two others that he confessed to zina, then he is not to be hadded. It is said in al-Zahiriyya: The witnesses are also not hadded. And if three testified to zina and the fourth testified to a confession of zina, then the three are hadded (for qadhf). He said the judge asks the witnesses about its essence i.e. its reality, which is insertion of the penis into the vagina, because it is possible they meant something other than the act in the vagina, as the Prophet ﷺ said: 'The eyes commit zina, and their zina is looking.' The hadith. Some people think every unlawful intercourse is zina that necessitates hadd, but the apparent meaning of their words is that the intended essence is not the legal definition as we explained. The modality is compulsion or willingness. And about the place because of the possibility that it was zina in dar al-harb, so no hadd. And about the time because of the possibility that the covenant is old, and the possibility that it was zina during his childhood. And about the woman because of the possibility that she was his son's slave girl or his mukatab's slave girl. So the judge should investigate that as a means to ward off the hadd. In Fath al-Qadir: By analogy, in testimony about a woman's zina, he should ask them who the man was, because there is also the mentioned possibility and an additional one, which is the possibility that he was a child or insane, that she enabled one of them, in which case there is no hadd on her according to Imam Abu Hanifa. They said: And the witnesses are also not hadded, because they testified to zina and their qadhf is not established because they did not mention anything that negates what they mentioned being zina, so their qadhf is not apparent. Unlike if they described it other than its description, then they are hadded. And if three testified and one did not add to (the word) zina, he is not hadded. And what occurred in the original of al-Mabsut, that if the fourth said: 'I testify that he is a fornicator' and was asked about its description and did not describe it, that he is hadded, is to be understood as he said it to the judge in a session other than the session in which the three testified. It is said in al-Muhit: He is not hadded, even if he said 'She is not my wife'. And if he confessed to zina with a woman he does not know, he is hadded, because he is not accused in confession against himself, as he knows his own situation, unlike the witness because he is accused. In al-Khaniyya: They testified that he committed zina with a woman they do not know, then they said it was so-and-so: neither the man nor the witnesses are hadded. End. His statement: 'If they explain and say: We saw him having intercourse with her like a kohl stick in a kohl container, and they modify secretly and openly, then he is executed because the truth is evident and it is obligatory for the judge to execute it.' Al-mikhala is with damma on the mim and ha. Their saying 'having intercourse with her like a kohl stick in a kohl container' refers to explaining the modality, and it is an additional explanation as a means to ward off (hadd); otherwise the question about its essence is sufficient, although the apparent meaning of their words is that the judgment depends on its explanation. And here he is not content with apparent probity by agreement, that it be said 'He is a Muslim, not outwardly sinful', as a means to ward off, unlike other rights according to Imam Abu Hanifa. And the explanation of modification secretly and openly will come, if Allah wills. And the summary of modification secretly is that the judge sends a paper with their names and the names of their locality in a way that each one is distinguished from them by one who knows him, and he writes under his name: 'He is just, acceptable of testimony.'
Source pages p. 9

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding the establishment of the hadd for zina through testimony. The author, al-Marghinani, explains that witnesses must specify the act in detail: the essence (insertion), the modality (willing or compelled), the place (to rule out dar al-harb), the time (to rule out childhood or old accusation), and the identity of the woman (to rule out ownership). This meticulousness is a deliberate means to avert the hadd (dar' al-hadd), based on the principle of avoiding punishment in cases of doubt. The text then discusses cases where witnesses fail to specify: if they merely say 'they committed zina', the accused is not punished, and the witnesses themselves are not punished for qadhf unless their testimony is clearly false. A hypothetical is given where three testify to zina and one to confession: the three are hadded because the fourth's testimony is insufficient to establish zina, leaving the three as qadhf. The passage also addresses when the woman is unknown: the accused is not hadded, and even if the witnesses later name her, the hadd falls. This is because the witnesses are considered suspect (mutamah), unlike the accused who confesses to a known act. The commentary then explains the phrase 'like a kohl stick in a kohl container' as a graphic description emphasizing full penetration. It also details the procedure for tazkiyah (verification of witnesses' probity): secretly by sending a sealed paper with names to a reliable person, and openly by bringing the witness and the modifier together. A notable ruling from Fath al-Qadir is that if the judge personally knows the witnesses' probity, he need not ask, as his own knowledge is stronger than a modifier's statement. However, because the law disregards the judge's personal knowledge for zina (to avoid his testimony?), the rule differs. This difference reflects the Hanafi emphasis on procedural caution in hadd cases.

Key Terms
الزنا (al-zina): Sexual intercourse between a man and a woman who are not married to each other, with full penetration (like a kohl stick in a kohl container).
الماهية (al-mahiyyah): The essence of the act, which here is defined as insertion of the male organ into the female organ (إدخال الفرج في الفرج).
التعديل (al-ta'dil): Verification of the witnesses' probity ('adalah) by the judge through secret or open means.
الدرء (al-dar'): Warding off the hadd punishment by any legitimate doubt (shubuha).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If four witnesses testify that a man committed zina but cannot identify the woman, what is the ruling according to the text?
A) The man is hadded for zina.
B) The man is not hadded, but the witnesses are hadded for qadhf.
C) The man is not hadded, nor are the witnesses hadded.
D) The testimony is considered insufficient, and the case is postponed until the woman is identified.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires exhaustive investigation in zina testimony to maximize the chance of averting the hadd through doubt.

Conditions for Zina Confession: Explicitness and Physical Possibility
Ruling with proof on conditions for zina confession

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two core conditions for a valid zina confession in the Hanafi school and explain why a deaf-mute's confession is invalid based on the principle of dar' al-hadd.

Core Idea
A valid zina confession requires explicit speech and physical possibility; otherwise, the hadd is averted by doubt.

Confession is one of the two main proofs for zina, but the Hanafi school imposes strict conditions to protect the accused from wrongful punishment. In this passage, the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains two key conditions: the confession must be explicit (sarih) and not contradicted by physical reality. These conditions flow from the overarching principle that hudud are averted by doubts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Conditions
Locate in the text the two conditions stated for a valid zina confession: (1) it must be explicit (sarih), and (2) it must not appear false (i.e., no physical impossibility).
The first condition excludes non-verbal communication; the second excludes cases like castration or imperforation.
2
Understand the Reason for Each Condition
For the first condition, the doubt arises from lack of explicitness—a deaf-mute's gesture might be misconstrued. For the second, physical impossibility shows the confession is false, creating a doubt that averts the hadd.
Both conditions are rooted in the maxim 'al-hudud tudra'u bi al-shubhat'.
3
Apply to the Deaf-Mute Case
The text explicitly says a deaf-mute's confession by writing or gesture is invalid. Consider why: the lack of speech introduces uncertainty about intent.
This is contrasted with a blind person, whose confession is valid because he can speak.
4
Examine the Inter-Madhhab Dispute
The hanafi_position_box and madhhab_dispute_map show that other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may accept a deaf-mute's written confession. Understand the basis of the dispute: different weight given to writing as communication.
The Hanafi position is based on the need for absolute certainty in hadd cases.

وأسماء محلتهم على وجه يتميز كل منهم لمن يعرفه فيكتب تحت اسمه هو عدل مقبول الشهادة. وحاصل التعديل علانية أن يجمع القاضي بين المزكي والشاهد فيقول هذا هو الذي زكيته. وفي فتح القدير : واعلم أن القاضي لو كان يعلم عدالة الشهود لا يجب عليه السؤال عن عدالتهم لأن علمه يغنيه عن ذلك وهو أقوى من الحاصل له من تعديل المزكي، ولولا ما ثبت من إهدار الشرع علمه بالزنا في إقامة الحد بالسمع الذي ذكرناه لكان يحده بعلمه لكن ثبت ذلك هناك ولم يثبت هنا قالوا ويحبسه هنا حتى يسأل عن الشهود كيلا يهرب ولا وجه لأخذ الكفيل منه لأن أخذ الكفيل نوع احتياط فلا يكون مشروعاً فيما ينبني على الدرء وليس حبسه للاحتياط بل للتهمة بطريق التعزير بخلاف الديون لا يحبس فيها قبل ظهور العدالة لأن الحبس أقصى عقوبة فيها فلا يجوز أن يفعله قبل الثبوت بخلاف الحدود فإنه فيها عقوبة أخرى

ولا بالتقادم هكذا في الفتح وفيه مخالفة لما مر من قوله في علة سؤالهم عن الزمان لجواز تقادم العهد، ولما يأتي أيضاً قريباً ويأتي متناً في باب الشهادة على الزنا أنها تسقط بالتقادم، ولم أر من نبه على هذا المحل، ثم رأيت الرملي نبه عليه في حاشية المنح حيث وقع فيها كما هنا فقال: المقرر أن التقادم يمنعها دون الفرار وكما يمنع التقادم قبول الشهادة في الابتداء فكذا يمنع الإقامة بعد القضاء فتأمل. قوله : (ولو أقر أنه زنى بخرساء أو هي أقرت الخ قال في النهر : قيل يشكل عليه ما لو أقر أنه زنى بغائبة حد استحساناً لأن انتظار حضورها لاحتمال أن تذكر مسقطاً عنه وعنها، ولا يجوز
And (zina is established) by his confession four times in his four sessions. Every time he confesses, the judge rejects him and asks him as previously mentioned. If he explains (the details), he is hadded; if he retracts... And the names of their (the witnesses') locality in a way that each one is distinguished from them by one who knows him, and he writes under his name: 'He is just, acceptable of testimony.' The summary of modification openly is that the judge gathers the modifier and the witness and says: 'This is the one you have verified.' In Fath al-Qadir: 'Know that if the judge knows the probity of the witnesses, he is not obligated to ask about their probity, because his knowledge suffices him and it is stronger than what is obtained from the modifier's verification. And were it not for what is established that the Law disregards his knowledge of zina in executing the hadd based on hearing (as we mentioned), he would have hadded the accused based on his knowledge. But that is established there (for zina) and not established here (for other rights). They said: He should imprison the accused here until he asks about the witnesses, lest he flee. And there is no way to take a surety from him, because taking a surety is a kind of precaution, so it is not legislated in matters based on warding off. And his imprisonment is not for precaution, but for accusation by way of ta'zir. Unlike debts: in debts, he is not imprisoned before probity appears, because imprisonment is the severest penalty in them, so it is not permissible to do it before proof. Unlike hadd punishments, where there is another penalty more severe than it.' His statement: 'And by his confession four times in his four sessions, each time he confesses the judge rejects him' is conjoined to 'by evidence'. That is, zina is established by his confession. And he gave precedence to establishment by evidence over it because it is mentioned in the Qur'an, and because what is established by it is stronger: the hadd is not repelled by flight nor by lapse of time, and because it is a transitive proof while confession is limited. And confession has two conditions: one is that it be explicit. So if a deaf-mute confesses to zina by writing or gesture, he is not hadded due to the doubt of lack of explicitness. Similarly, testimony against a deaf-mute is not accepted because he might claim a doubt, like if they testify against an insane person that he committed zina during his lucidity. Unlike a blind person: his confession and testimony against him are valid. Similarly, a eunuch and an impotent person. Based on this, the definition of zina that necessitates hadd should have added after 'mukallaf, speaking': because you know that a deaf-mute is not hadded, neither by his confession nor by evidence. Second condition: that his confession not appear false. So if he confessed and then he is found to be castrated, or she confessed and then she is found to be sealed (imperforate), and that is when women inform that she is sealed before the hadd, because their informing about the sealing creates a doubt in the testimony of the witnesses, and by doubt the hadd is averted. And if he confessed that he committed zina with a deaf-mute woman, or she confessed with a deaf-mute man, neither one is hadded. As in Fath al-Qadir. And his confession must be in a state... The author's statement is explicit that they (deaf-mute and sealed) do not stand in place of zina, as is not hidden. His statement: 'So that the hadd is not repelled by flight nor by lapse of time.' This is how it is in al-Fath, and there is contradiction with what previously passed in his statement regarding the reason for asking about time (due to the possibility of old covenant), and also with what will come shortly, and what will come in the text of the chapter on testimony about zina that it is nullified by lapse of time. I have not seen anyone who alerted to this issue. Then I saw al-Ramli alert to it in his Hashiyat al-Minhaj, where it occurred as here, and he said: 'The established rule is that lapse of time prevents it but not flight, and just as lapse of time prevents acceptance of testimony initially, similarly it prevents execution after judgment, so reflect.' His statement: 'And if he confessed that he committed zina with a deaf-mute, or she confessed...' He said in al-Nahr: 'It could be objected that if he confessed to zina with an absent woman, he is hadded by istihsan, because waiting for her presence (on the possibility that she might mention something that nullifies the hadd for him and her) is not permitted.'
Source pages p. 10

Commentary
This passage discusses the establishment of zina through confession (iqrar). The author explains that confession must be made four times in four separate sessions, with the judge rejecting and questioning the confessor each time to ensure it is not a result of duress or confusion. This mirrors the four witnesses requirement. The passage then returns to the topic of witness verification (tazkiyah) from the previous page, reiterating the procedure and noting that if the judge personally knows the witnesses' probity, he may dispense with formal tazkiyah, except in zina cases where personal knowledge is disregarded to uphold the principle of ward. The author then contrasts this with debt cases, where imprisonment before proof of probity is not allowed. Returning to confession, two conditions are given: (1) it must be explicit (sarih) — hence a deaf-mute's confession by writing or gesture is not valid due to lack of explicitness, creating a doubt; similarly, testimony against a deaf-mute is not accepted. A blind person, however, can confess and be testified against because he can speak. (2) The confession must not be contradicted by physical reality — if the confessor is found to be castrated (majbub) or the woman imperforate (ratqa'), the hadd falls because the confession is false, creating a doubt. The text also addresses confession involving a deaf-mute partner: no hadd on either. A problematic statement in Fath al-Qadir regarding flight and lapse of time is noted: the earlier text said time lapse is a reason to ask (to avoid old accusations), but later it says lapse of time does not repel the hadd in confession. The commentator (possibly al-Ramli) clarifies that lapse of time prevents acceptance of testimony from the start, and even after judgment, it prevents execution; but flight does not prevent. The passage ends with a discussion of confession to zina with an absent woman: by istihsan the confessor is hadded immediately without waiting for her presence, because waiting might allow her to mention something that nullifies the hadd, which is not allowed — contrast with the case of a deaf-mute where the partner's status creates a doubt.

Key Terms
الإقرار (al-iqrar): Confession by the accused of committing zina, made four times in four separate sessions.
الأخرس (al-abras): A person who is mute (cannot speak). Their confession by writing or gesture is invalid for hadd due to lack of explicitness.
المجبوب (al-majbub): A man who is castrated (has no male organ or is impotent). If he confesses and then is found to be majbub, the hadd falls due to falsehood of confession.
الرتقاء (al-ratqa'): A woman who is imperforate (sealed), making intercourse impossible. If she confesses and is found to be ratqa', the hadd falls.
التقادم (al-taqadum): Lapse of time (prescription). In hadd cases, it prevents the acceptance of testimony from the start and also prevents execution after judgment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is a deaf-mute's confession to zina not accepted according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because they cannot speak, so they cannot satisfy the requirement of a 'speaking' confession.
B) Because they might not understand the legal consequences.
C) Because they can only write, but writing is not considered a valid form of confession in any case.
D) Because of the doubt that they might be claiming a legal doubt (shubha) that would avert the hadd.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school imposes two strict conditions on zina confession—explicitness and physical possibility—to uphold the principle that hudud are averted by doubts.

Proving Zina by Confession: Conditions and Proof in Hanafi Law
Explains conditions for proving zina by confession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four conditions for a valid confession of zina in Hanafi law and apply them to determine whether the hadd punishment is incurred.

Core Idea
Zina by confession requires four explicit confessions in separate sittings; any ambiguity (shubha) wards off the hadd.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq expands on Kanz al-Daqaiq's ruling on hudud. The commentator, Ibn Nujaym, details the stringent requirements for a confession of zina to be valid, drawing from the hadith of Ma'iz. Understanding these conditions is crucial to appreciate the Hanafi principle of warding off hadd punishments through shubha.

Guided Path
1
Identify the method of proof
Recognize that zina can be proven either by four eyewitnesses (bayyinah) or by the accused's confession (iqrar). The passage explains that confession is a weaker proof than witness testimony.
Confession is a limited proof (hujja qasira) that only affects the confessor.
2
List the conditions for a valid confession
From the passage, extract the two stated conditions: (1) explicit wording (sarih), and (2) that the confession does not appear false. Also note implied conditions: sobriety, repeat four times, separate sittings.
The mute's confession by gesture is invalid due to shubha.
3
Understand the fourfold repetition requirement
The hadith of Ma'iz shows the Prophet delayed punishment until four confessions in four sittings. The passage emphasizes that all four must be in separate sittings (majalis mutafarriqa) to avoid doubt.
Muhammad defined 'separate' as the confessor leaving the judge's sight.
4
Analyze the effect of contradiction by the other party
If a man confesses and the woman denies, the hadd is dropped from the man. If a woman confesses and the man denies, Abu Hanifa drops the hadd from her; the Sahibayn disagree.
The disagreement hinges on whether the denial creates sufficient shubha.
5
Apply the rule to edge cases
Consider cases like the drunkard's confession (invalid), the slave's confession (valid), or if the confessor later retracts (not covered directly but implied). The passage shows that shubha overrides the hadd.
Shubha includes physical conditions like castration or virginity.

وبإقراره أربعاً في مجالسه الأربعة كلما أقر رده وسأله كما مر فإن بينه حد فإن رجع

الصحو لما في المحيط : السكران إذا سرق أو زنى في حال سكره يحد ولو أقر بالزنا أو بالسرقة لا يحد لأن الإنشاء لا يحتمل الكذب والإقرار يحتمل الكذب فاعتبر هذا الاحتمال في حال سكره في الإقرار بالحد لا غير .اهـ. ولا بد من أن لا يكذبه الآخر فإن أقر الرجل بالزنا بفلانة فكذبته درئ الحد عن الرجل، سواء قالت إنه تزوجني أو لا أعرفه أصلاً، ويقضى بالمهر عليه إن ادعته المرأة، وإن أقرت المرأة بالزنا بفلان وكذبها الرجل فلا حد عليها أيضاً عند الإمام خلافاً لهما في المسألتين؛ كذا في الظهيرية. وفي المحيط : أصله أن الحد متى لم يجب على المرأة أصلاً أو تعذر استيفاؤه عليها لا يجب على الرجل بالإجماع، ومتى لم يجب على الرجل أصلاً لم يجب على المرأة بالإجماع وإن انعقد فعله موجباً للحد لكن بطل الحد عنه لمعنى عارض لا يمنع الوجوب على المرأة عنده خلافاً لهما .اهـ. ولم يشترط المصنف بلوغ المقر وعقله كما في الهداية لأنهما شرطاً لكل تكليف وليس من شرطه الحرية فصح إقرار العبد بالزنا أو بغيره مما يوجب الحد وإن كان مولاه غائباً، وكذا القطع والقصاص، وفرق أبو حنيفة ومحمد بين حجة البينة وحجة
الإقرار ولو قال العبد بعد ما أعتق زنيت وأنا عبد لزمه حد العبيد؛ كذا في الظهيرية وإنما شرطنا تكرار الإقرار أربعاً لحديث ماعز أنه عليه السلام أخر إقامة الحد عليه إلى أن تم إقراره أربع مرات في أربع مجالس فلهذا قلنا لا المجالس لأن لاتحاده أثراً في جمع المتفرقات فعنده يتحقق شبهة الاتحاد فيه والعبرة لمجلس المقر لأنه قائم به دون مجلس القاضي. وفسر محمد المجالس المتفرقة أن يذهب المقر بحيث يتوارى القاضي وينبغي للإمام أن يزجره عن الإقرار ويظهر له الكراهية من ذلك ويأمر عن بصر بإبعاده عن مجلسه في كل مرة لأنه عليه السلام فعل كذلك وفي الظهيرية : ولو أقر كل يوم

بد من
اختلاف
التأخير بهذا الاحتمال فيحتاج إلى الفرق .اهـ. وفي حاشية أبي السعود قال شيخنا تغمده الله برحمته : الزيلعي في الباب الآتي بالفرق حيث قال : بخلاف ما إذا أقرأنه زنى بغائبة أو شهد عليه بذلك حيث يحد وإن احتمل أن ينكر الغائب الزنا أو يدعي النكاح لأنه لو حضر وأنكر الزنا أو ادعى النكاح يكون شبهة، واحتمال ذلك يكون شبهة الشبهة فالشبهة هي المعتبرة دون شبهة الشبهة اهـ . قال : ثم ظهر لي أنه لا يصلح فارقاً لما أن شبهة الشبهة ثابتة في المسألتين إذ دعوى الخرساء على فرض نطقها ما يسقط الحد هو الشبهة وجواز أنها لو تكلمت أبدته شبهة الشبهة فكان الاحتياج إلى إبداء الفرق باقياً اهـ بلفظه وذكر في الجوهرة أن القياس عدم الحد الجواز أن تحضر فتجحد فتدعي حد القذف أو نكاحاً فتطلب المهر وفي حده إبطال حقها والاستحسان أن يحد لحديث ماعز أنه تدعي غيبة المرأة وتمامه فيه وحاصله أنه ترك القياس للدليل فلا يقاس عليه ما لو زنا بخرساء حد
مع
لوروده على خلاف القياس، وبه يندفع الإشكال والله تعالى أعلم قوله : ( ومتى لم يجب على الرجل أصلاً لم يجب على المرأة سيأتي عند قول المصنف وبزنا صبي أو مجنون أنه منقوض بزنا المكره بالمطاوعة والمستأمن بالذمية والمسلمة .اهـ لكن احترز هنا عن الأول بقوله «وإن انعقد الخ» تأمل.
Book of Hudud: And by his confession four times in his four sittings, whenever he confessed he rejected him and asked him as previously, then if he clarified, he is flogged, and if he retracted, ... and the names of their places in a way that each of them is distinguished for one who knows him, so he writes under his name: 'He is just, acceptable of testimony.' And the summary of public verification is that the judge gathers the verifier and the witness and says: 'This is the one you verified.' And in Fath al-Qadir: Know that if the judge knows the justice of witnesses, he is not required to ask about their justice because his knowledge suffices him, and it is stronger than what he obtains from the verifier's verification. Were it not for the established fact that the Shari'ah disregards his knowledge of zina in establishing the hadd by hearing that we mentioned, he would flog them by his knowledge, but it is established there and not established here. They said: He imprisons him here until he asks about the witnesses so that he does not flee, and there is no justification for taking a guarantor from him because taking a guarantor is a type of precaution, so it is not legislated in what is based on [the principle of] warding off. And his imprisonment is not for precaution but for suspicion by way of ta'zir, unlike debts where he is not imprisoned before the appearance of justice because imprisonment is the maximum punishment in them, so it is not permissible for him to do it before proof, unlike hudud where there is another punishment more severe than it. His statement: (And by his confession four times in his four sittings, whenever he confessed he rejected him) is conjoined to 'by evidence' meaning that zina is proven by his confession. And he gave precedence to proof by evidence over it because it is mentioned in the Qur'an and because what is proven by it is stronger, such that the hadd is not repelled by flight or by passage of time, and because it is a transmissible proof while confession is limited. And confession has two conditions: one is that it be explicit; if a mute confesses to zina by writing or gesture, he is not flogged due to ambiguity because it is not explicit. Similarly, testimony against a mute is not accepted due to the possibility that he claims an ambiguity, as if they testify against a madman that he committed zina while sane, unlike the blind, for his confession and testimony against him are valid, and likewise the eunuch and the impotent. Based on this, the definition of zina that necessitates the hadd is augmented after his saying 'accountable, speaking' because you know that the mute has no hadd upon him, neither by his confession nor by evidence. The second condition is that his confession not appear to be false; if he confesses and then appears to be castrated, or she confesses and appears to be closed (virgin), by women informing that she is closed before the hadd, because their informing about the closedness causes ambiguity in the testimony of witnesses, and by ambiguity the hadd is warded off. And if he confesses that he committed zina with a mute woman, or she confesses with a mute, there is no hadd on either of them. Thus in Fath al-Qadir. And it is necessary that his confession be in a state of sobriety. In al-Muhit: The drunkard, if he steals or commits zina while drunk, he is flogged; but if he confesses to zina or theft, he is not flogged because an action (creating a legal effect) does not admit falsehood while confession admits falsehood, so this possibility is considered in his drunken state in confession regarding the hadd only. And it is necessary that the other person not contradict him. If a man confesses to zina with a certain woman and she contradicts him, the hadd is warded off from the man, whether she says he married me or I do not know him at all, and the dowry is adjudged against him if the woman claims it. If a woman confesses to zina with a certain man and he contradicts her, there is no hadd on her either according to Imam Abu Hanifa, contrary to the two companions in both issues. Thus in al-Zahiriyya. And in al-Muhit: The principle is that if the hadd is not obligatory on the woman at all, or its execution upon her is impossible, it is not obligatory on the man by consensus. And if it is not obligatory on the man at all, it is not obligatory on the woman by consensus. But if his action was such that it made the hadd obligatory but the hadd was nullified due to an incidental reason, that does not prevent obligation on the woman according to him, contrary to the two companions. He did not stipulate the confessor's majority and sanity, as in al-Hidaya, because they are conditions for every assignment of responsibility, and freedom is not a condition, so the confession of a slave regarding zina or anything else that necessitates the hadd is valid even if his master is absent, and likewise amputation and retaliation. And Abu Hanifa and Muhammad distinguished between the proof of evidence and the proof of confession. And if the slave after being freed says 'I committed zina while I was a slave', the hadd of slaves is imposed on him. Thus in al-Zahiriyya. And we stipulated the repetition of confession four times because of the hadith of Ma'iz that he (peace be upon him) delayed the execution of the hadd upon him until his confession was completed four times in four sittings. Therefore we say: not [in one session] because unity has an effect in gathering scattered [confessions]; then the ambiguity of unity is realized in it, and consideration is given to the session of the confessor because it is attached to him, not the session of the judge. And Muhammad interpreted the separate sessions as the confessor going such that the judge loses sight of him. And the Imam should dissuade him from confessing and show dislike for that and order the guard to remove him from his session each time, because he (peace be upon him) did likewise. And in al-Zahiriyya: And if he confesses every day... (the rest of the text discusses differences and the case of confessing to zina with an absent woman, and the distinction between shubha and shubhat al-shubha, and the hadith of Ma'iz as a proof overriding qiyas.)
Source pages p. 10

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq is an expansion on the matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq regarding the proof of zina by confession. The commentator, Ibn Nujaym, begins by explaining that zina can be established either by four male witnesses (bayyinah) or by the accused's own confession made four times in four separate sittings (majalis). The priority of bayyinah over confession is due to its mention in the Qur'an (Surah al-Nisa, 4:15) and its strength: the hadd is not dropped by the accused's flight or by lapse of time when proven by witnesses, whereas confession is weaker and confined to the confessor. The author then outlines two essential conditions for a valid confession: (1) it must be explicit (sarih), so a mute's confession by writing or gesture is not accepted due to ambiguity (shubha), and similarly, testimony against a mute is inadmissible because he might claim a valid excuse; however, a blind person's confession and testimony are valid. This leads to an addition to the definition of zina that incurs the hadd: the offender must be a legally responsible (mukallaf) speaking person (natiq). (2) The confession must not be contradicted by reality: if the confessor is found to be castrated (majbub) or the woman found to be a virgin (ratqa'), the hadd is dropped. The passage then addresses the scenario of a drunkard: if he commits zina while drunk, he is flogged, but if he merely confesses while drunk, the confession is not accepted because it might be false. Another key rule is that if one party confesses and the other denies, the hadd is waived from the confessor; for instance, if a man confesses to zina with a woman and she denies it, the hadd is dropped from the man (and he may be liable for mahr if she claims it). The same applies if a woman confesses and the man denies—Abu Hanifa drops the hadd from her, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) disagree. The text then explains that the hadd is not imposed on either party if it is not obligatory on one of them from the start. Regarding the confessor's capacity, the commentator notes that majority (bulugh) and sanity ('aql) are conditions for all legal responsibilities, so they are not repeated here, but freedom is not required; thus a slave's confession of zina is valid, and if he confesses after being freed to an act done while a slave, he receives the slave's punishment (half of a free person's). The requirement of four confessions in four separate sittings is derived from the hadith of Ma'iz (may Allah be pleased with him), where the Prophet (peace be upon him) kept delaying the punishment until Ma'iz had confessed four times in four different gatherings. The commentator notes that the confessions must be in separate sittings, not one session, because if all four are made in one session, there is an ambiguity (shubha) that the confessor might be confused. The imam is also encouraged to dissuade the confessor and show disapproval. Finally, the passage discusses a controversial issue: if someone confesses to zina with an absent woman, he is flogged (by istihsan) despite the possibility that the absent woman might deny it or claim marriage, because the hadith of Ma'iz serves as a proof overriding qiyas. The lesson concludes with a note on a later passage regarding the effect of the hadd being nullified for one party and the other.

Key Terms
إقرار (iqrar): A legal confession made by the accused, which in the context of zina must be repeated four times in four separate sittings.
شبهة (shubha): An ambiguity or doubt that prevents application of the hadd punishment.
مجالس متفرقة (majalis mutafarriqa): Separate sittings; the confessor must leave the judge's presence between each confession.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is a condition for a valid confession of zina that incurs the hadd?
A) The confessor must be free.
B) The confession must be made in the presence of the other party.
C) The confession must be repeated four times in four separate sittings.
D) The confession must be witnessed by two men.

Key Takeaway
A confession of zina is valid only if explicit, truthful, sober, repeated four times in separate sittings, and not contradicted by the other party; any ambiguity (shubha) drops the hadd.

Drunkard's Action vs. Confession in Hadd Penalties
Ruling that drunkard is punished for action but not for confession

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the drunkard's liability for hadd and explain the distinction between action (inshā') and confession (iqrār) based on certainty.

Core Idea
Actions are certain; confessions are doubtful — thus a drunkard's act incurs hadd, but his confession does not.

In Hanafi fiqh, the enforcement of fixed penalties (hudud) requires a high level of certainty. This passage from al-Bahr al-Rā’iq clarifies a unique ruling: a person who commits a hadd offense while intoxicated is still liable because the act itself is undeniable. However, a confession made while drunk is not accepted because verbal statements can be false, and intoxication increases that possibility. This lesson unpacks the rationale behind this distinction and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage presents two situations: (1) a drunkard actually steals or commits zina, and (2) a drunkard confesses to such acts. Note the different outcomes.
2
State the ruling for each scenario
For the action: the drunkard is punished with hadd. For the confession: he is not punished. This is the core ruling.
The ruling applies only to hadd penalties, not to other legal matters.
3
Extract the rationale (ta'lil)
The author explains: action (inshā') does not admit falsehood (lā yahtamil al-kadhib), whereas confession (iqrār) admits falsehood. Therefore, the possibility of falsehood is considered in the state of drunkenness for confession only.
This is a key principle: actions are objective, statements are subjective.
4
Apply the rationale to the drunkard's state
Intoxication does not change the certainty of the action, but it increases the likelihood of falsehood in speech. Hence, the confession is rejected due to this heightened doubt.
The same reasoning would apply if the person was coerced or insane? Not directly; this is specific to intoxication.
5
Generalize the Hanafi principle
The Hanafi school requires a high degree of certainty (yaqīn) for hudud. Any evidence open to doubt is insufficient. Action is certain; confession by a drunk person is doubtful.
This principle is also seen in other areas, e.g., requiring multiple witnesses for zina.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الصحو لما في المحيط : السكران إذا سرق أو زنى في حال سكره يحد ولو أقر بالزنا أو بالسرقة لا يحد لأن الإنشاء لا يحتمل الكذب والإقرار يحتمل الكذب فاعتبر هذا الاحتمال في حال سكره في الإقرار بالحد لا غير .اهـ.
Drunkenness? According to what is in al-Muhit: A drunk person, if he steals or commits zina while in a state of drunkenness, he is punished with hadd. But if he confesses to zina or theft, he is not punished, because an action does not admit falsehood, but confession admits falsehood. So this possibility is considered in his state of drunkenness regarding confession of hadd only. End quote.
Source pages p. 11

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq cites al-Muhit to explain a key distinction: a drunk person is legally responsible for his actions (zina or theft) and thus liable for the hadd penalty, because actions are objective and cannot be false. However, his confession to such acts while drunk is not accepted because confession is a statement that could be false, and in a state of intoxication, this possibility is given weight. The ruling is specific to hadd penalties. This shows that the Hanafi school requires certainty in evidence for hadd, and a confession from an intoxicated person lacks that certainty.

Key Terms
الإنشاء (al-inshā'): The actual commission of the act (zina or theft), as opposed to a verbal confession.
الإقرار (al-iqrār): A verbal confession admitting guilt for a hadd offense.
الحد (al-ḥadd): The fixed penalty prescribed by Shariah for specific crimes like zina and theft.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is a drunk person's confession for theft not accepted?
A) Because he is not sane.
B) Because confession is open to falsehood.
C) Because the hadd has already been applied.
D) Because the theft was not proven.

Key Takeaway
A drunkard's action is sufficient for hadd, but his confession is invalid due to the potential for falsehood.

Effect of Denial in Zina Confession: Abu Hanifa vs Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on denial in zina confession

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the effect of denial by the accused party in a confession of zina and explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Denial by the alleged partner creates a doubt that averts the hadd from the confessor, but the Sahibayn disagree when the confessor is a woman.

When a person confesses to zina, the hadd penalty is typically applied. However, if the alleged partner denies the act, a doubt (shubha) arises that may avert the punishment. This lesson unpacks an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the denial protects both parties, while the two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue that if the confessor is a woman, she still faces hadd. Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens your grasp of how shubha operates in hudud law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage presents two scenarios: (1) a man confesses and the woman denies; (2) a woman confesses and the man denies. In both, the hadd is averted from the confessor according to Imam Abu Hanifa, but the Sahibayn differ in the second scenario.
The denial can be expressed as 'he married me' or 'I do not know him' – both create doubt.
2
State the principle from al-Muhit
The text cites a principle: if hadd is never obligatory on one party originally, it is not obligatory on the other by consensus. However, if hadd was originally obligatory but is nullified by an incidental factor (like denial), the obligation may remain on the other party according to Abu Hanifa, but not according to the Sahibayn.
Key distinction: 'originally not obligatory' vs 'obligatory but nullified by an incidental factor'.
3
Analyze the point of disagreement
The dispute hinges on whether the denial is merely an incidental factor that removes hadd from the confessor only, or whether it creates a shubha that removes hadd from both. Abu Hanifa sees the denial as creating a shubha for both; the Sahibayn see it as only affecting the confessor.
The practical consequence: if a woman confesses and the man denies, Abu Hanifa says no hadd on her; Sahibayn say she is punished.
4
Determine the mufta bihi position
The text implies that the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Imam Abu Hanifa, as the passage states 'at the Imam' and contrasts 'contrary to them' without further debate.
Later Hanafi fatwa works generally follow Abu Hanifa in this matter.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا بد من أن لا يكذبه الآخر فإن أقر الرجل بالزنا بفلانة فكذبته درئ الحد عن الرجل، سواء قالت إنه تزوجني أو لا أعرفه أصلاً، ويقضى بالمهر عليه إن ادعته المرأة، وإن أقرت المرأة بالزنا بفلان وكذبها الرجل فلا حد عليها أيضاً عند الإمام خلافاً لهما في المسألتين؛ كذا في الظهيرية. وفي المحيط : أصله أن الحد متى لم يجب على المرأة أصلاً أو تعذر استيفاؤه عليها لا يجب على الرجل بالإجماع، ومتى لم يجب على الرجل أصلاً لم يجب على المرأة بالإجماع وإن انعقد فعله موجباً للحد لكن بطل الحد عنه لمعنى عارض لا يمنع الوجوب على المرأة عنده خلافاً لهما .اهـ.
And it is necessary that the other does not deny him. For if a man confesses to zina with a certain woman and she denies him, the hadd is averted from the man, whether she says 'he married me' or 'I do not know him at all.' And the dowry is adjudged against him if the woman claims it. And if a woman confesses to zina with a certain man and the man denies her, then there is no hadd on her according to Imam [Abu Hanifa], contrary to them [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad] in both matters. This is in al-Zahiriyyah. And in al-Muhit: The principle is that whenever the hadd is not obligatory on the woman originally or its enforcement upon her becomes impossible, it is not obligatory on the man by consensus; and whenever it is not obligatory on the man originally, it is not obligatory on the woman by consensus. However, if his act is such that it entails hadd but the hadd is nullified from him due to an incidental factor, that does not prevent obligation on the woman according to him, contrary to them. End quote.
Source pages p. 11

Commentary
This passage discusses a scenario where a person confesses to zina but the alleged partner denies it. The denial creates a shubha (doubt) that prevents the hadd from being enforced on the confessor. The Hanafi position distinguishes between two cases: if the confessor is a man and the woman denies, the hadd is dropped from the man regardless of her reason, and he must pay the dower if she claims it. If the confessor is a woman and the man denies, Imam Abu Hanifa holds that no hadd is on her, but the two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree. The text then cites a general principle from al-Muhit: the obligation of hadd is reciprocal between the two parties. If it is not obligatory on one originally, it is not on the other. But if the hadd is nullified from one due to an incidental factor (like denial), it does not necessarily remove it from the other according to Abu Hanifa, while the Sahibayn say it does. This is an important intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Key Terms
الشبهة (al-shubha): A doubt or ambiguity that prevents the application of a hadd penalty.
المهر (al-mahr): The dower or bridal gift that a husband must pay to his wife upon marriage.
درئ (duri'a): Averted or dropped, referring to the hadd penalty being lifted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if a woman confesses to zina with a man and the man denies, what is the ruling?
A) She is punished with hadd.
B) She is not punished.
C) Both are punished.
D) The man is punished.

Key Takeaway
In hanafi fiqh, the denial of the alleged partner in a zina confession creates a doubt that averts the hadd from the confessor, but the Sahibayn disagree when the confessor is a woman; the mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view protecting the woman.

Conditions for Acceptance of Confession in Hadd Offenses
Ruling on the conditions for accepting confession in hadd offenses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for the acceptance of a confession in hadd cases and identify whether freedom is a requirement.

Core Idea
A confession to a hadd offense is valid even from a slave, as long as the confessor is adult and sane.

In Hanafi fiqh, a confession (iqrar) is a powerful form of evidence in hadd cases. This lesson clarifies that while maturity and sanity are essential conditions for any legal responsibility (taklif), freedom is not. Thus, a slave’s confession is fully valid, even if the master is absent. We also explore a special case: a freed slave confessing to an act committed while in bondage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general conditions for taklif
Maturity (bulugh) and sanity ('aql) are required for any legal responsibility. The author did not restate them because they are already established as conditions for all Shariah obligations.
2
Determine the conditions specific to confession
Freedom is not a condition. The passage emphatically states that a slave's confession is valid, even if his master is absent.
3
Apply the ruling to a slave's confession
A slave's confession to zina, theft (cutting), or murder (retaliation) is accepted. The hadd penalty applies accordingly.
4
Distinguish between bayyinah and iqrar
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad differentiated between testimony (bayyinah) and confession (iqrar). Testimony requires additional conditions (e.g., justice of witnesses), while confession does not.
5
Handle the special case of a freed slave
If a freed slave confesses to an offense committed while still a slave, the hadd of slaves (e.g., half the free penalty) is applied, not the free penalty.
This is recorded in al-Zahiriyyah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولم يشترط المصنف بلوغ المقر وعقله كما في الهداية لأنهما شرطاً لكل تكليف وليس من شرطه الحرية فصح إقرار العبد بالزنا أو بغيره مما يوجب الحد وإن كان مولاه غائباً، وكذا القطع والقصاص، وفرق أبو حنيفة ومحمد بين حجة البينة وحجة الإقرار ولو قال العبد بعد ما أعتق زنيت وأنا عبد لزمه حد العبيد؛ كذا في الظهيرية
And the author did not stipulate the confessor's being adult and sane, as in al-Hidayah, because they are conditions for every legal responsibility. And freedom is not a condition for confession, so the confession of a slave for zina or other acts entailing hadd is valid, even if his master is absent, and similarly for amputation and retaliation. And Abu Hanifa and Muhammad distinguished between the evidence of testimony and the evidence of confession. And if a slave says after being freed, 'I committed zina while I was a slave,' the hadd of slaves is incumbent on him. This is in al-Zahiriyyah.
Source pages p. 11

Commentary
This passage clarifies the conditions for a valid confession in hadd cases. The author of Kanz al-Daqaiq did not need to mention maturity and sanity because they are already required for taklif (legal responsibility) generally. However, freedom is not a condition. Thus, a slave's confession to zina or other hadd offenses is valid, even if his master is absent. The same applies to amputation (for theft) and retaliation (for murder). There is a distinction between testimony (bayyinah) and confession (iqrar): testimony requires additional conditions like justice of witnesses, but confession does not. Additionally, if a freed slave confesses to an offense committed while he was a slave, the penalty is that of a slave (e.g., half the hadd of a free person).

Key Terms
التكليف (al-taklif): Legal responsibility; capacity to be bound by Shariah rulings.
العبد (al-'abd): A slave; a person in legal bondage.
القصاص (al-qisas): Retaliation; the penalty for murder or intentional injury.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) Only if his master is present.
D) Only if the theft amount is large.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, confession to a hadd offense is accepted from any mukallaf, regardless of freedom status.
