Four Separate Confessions Required for Hadd of Zina
Ruling that confession must be repeated four times in separate sessions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi requirement for accepting a confession of zina and derive it from the prophetic practice with Ma'iz.

Core Idea
A confession for zina is only accepted if repeated four times in distinct sessions.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains why the Hanafi school requires a confession of zina to be made four times in separate sessions. The ruling is derived from the Prophet's treatment of Ma'iz, who confessed repeatedly before the hadd was applied. Understanding this condition prevents hasty punishment and ensures the confession is voluntary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The passage states that the confession must be repeated four times. This is a condition for the hadd punishment to be enforced.
2
Locate the dalil
The evidence is the hadith of Ma'iz: the Prophet delayed the hadd until Ma'iz had confessed four times in four separate sessions.
The hadith is narrated in multiple collections.
3
Analyze the istidlal
The Prophet's action of delaying indicates that multiple confessions are required. The Hanafi school takes this as a binding precedent (sunnah).
The imperative to follow the Prophet's practice establishes the wujub of this condition.
4
Define separate sessions
Separate sessions are defined as the confessor leaving the judge's presence such that the judge loses sight of him.
This ensures each confession is made independently and voluntarily.
5
Note ancillary rulings
The judge should discourage the confession and order the person removed each time. Confessing once per day or month still counts as separate sessions.
These rules are based on the Prophet's practice with Ma'iz.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإنما شرطنا تكرار الإقرار أربعاً لحديث ماعز أنه عليه السلام أخر إقامة الحد عليه إلى أن تم إقراره أربع مرات في أربع مجالس فلهذا قلنا لا المجالس لأن لاتحاده أثراً في جمع المتفرقات فعنده يتحقق شبهة الاتحاد فيه والعبرة لمجلس المقر لأنه قائم به دون مجلس القاضي. وفسر محمد المجالس المتفرقة أن يذهب المقر بحيث يتوارى القاضي وينبغي للإمام أن يزجره عن الإقرار ويظهر له الكراهية من ذلك ويأمر عن بصر بإبعاده عن مجلسه في كل مرة لأنه عليه السلام فعل كذلك وفي الظهيرية : ولو أقر كل يوم مرة أو كل شهر مرة فإنه يحد .اهـ.
And we required the repetition of confession four times based on the hadith of Ma'iz that the Prophet, peace be upon him, delayed the execution of the hadd upon him until his confession was completed four times in four separate sessions. So we said: sessions, because union has an effect in gathering scattered things, and thus a suspicion of unity occurs. And the consideration is for the session of the confessor because it is associated with him, not the session of the judge. And Muhammad interpreted separate sessions as the confessor going away such that the judge disappears from sight. And it is recommended for the imam to discourage him from confessing and to show dislike for that, and to order someone to remove him from his session each time, because the Prophet did so. And in al-Zahiriyyah: If he confesses once every day or once every month, he is punished. End quote.
Source pages p. 11

Commentary
This passage establishes a key requirement for the acceptance of a confession in zina cases: it must be repeated four times in separate sessions. This is derived from the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) in the case of Ma'iz, who confessed four times before the Prophet ordered the hadd. Separate sessions are defined by the confessor leaving the judge's presence so that the judge loses sight of him. This is to ensure that the confession is voluntary and not coerced. The judge is also encouraged to discourage the confession, showing the gravity of the matter. If the confessor confesses once a day or once a month, that is considered separate sessions and the confession is valid.

Key Terms
المجالس (al-majālis): Sessions; separate occasions for the confession to be made.
ماعز (Mā'iz): The companion who confessed to zina and was stoned by order of the Prophet.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many times must a confession of zina be repeated to be accepted?
A) Once
B) Twice
C) Three times
D) Four times

Key Takeaway
A valid confession for zina must be made four times in truly separate sessions, as established by the Prophet's practice with Ma'iz.

The Judge's Questioning and Rejection of Testimony on Confession
Ruling with proof: judge's questioning and rejection of testimony on confession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school requires the judge to question a confessor of zina about the time and the woman, and state that testimony on a confession is never accepted.

Core Idea
Confession must be clear and before the judge; testimony on confession is never accepted.

In hadd cases, a confession is a serious matter. The judge must verify the confession thoroughly to avoid punishing the innocent. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the procedure: the judge asks about five specific matters, especially the time and the woman, to rule out possibilities like the act occurring during childhood. It also clarifies that witnesses who heard the confession cannot testify to it, because the confessor may retract or the confession is unnecessary if admitted.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling on the Judge's Questioning
Recognize that the judge is required to ask the confessor about five matters (time, woman, etc.) to ensure the confession is valid. The hadd is not imposed unless the confessor answers clearly.
The five matters were mentioned previously in the text, not in this passage.
2
Understand the Reasons for Questioning
Consider the possibilities: the act might have occurred during childhood (invalidating hadd) or with a legally forbidden relative (like a son's slave woman). The benefit of asking about time is not only prescription but also minority.
The passage gives two examples: childhood and a son's slave woman.
3
Analyze the Istihsan Exception
If the confessor confesses to zina with a specific woman who is absent, he is still punished by istihsan (juristic preference), unlike if the woman denies it (then he is not punished). This shows the flexibility of Hanafi methodology.
Istihsan overrides the normal qiyas that would require her confirmation.
4
Determine Why Testimony on Confession is Rejected
Testimony (bayyinah) on a confession is not accepted because if the person denies it, his retraction is accepted; if he admits, the testimony is superfluous. The confession must be made directly before the judge, not elsewhere.
Even if the confession was made four times elsewhere, testimony about it is not considered.
5
Summarize the Mufta Bihi Position
The operative ruling is that confession must be before the judge, who must question the confessor. Evidence (testimony) on a confession is never accepted. This is the relied-upon Hanafi position.
The passage confirms it is the 'most correct' (al-asahh) opinion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وسأله كما فإن بينه حد) أي سأل الحاكم المقر عن الأشياء الخمسة المتقدمة للاحتمالات المذكورة فإن بين المسؤول عنه وجب الحد وظاهر كلامه أنه يسأله عن الزمان والمزني بها وهذا هو الأصح لاحتمال أنه زنى في صباه أو زنى بجارية ابنه وهو يعلمها . وليس فائدة السؤال عن الزمان منحصرة في احتمال التقادم وهو مضر في الشهادة دون الإقرار لأن له فائدة أخرى وهو احتمال وجوده في زمن الصبا. ولو سئل عن المزني بها فقال لا أعرفها قدمنا أنه يحد، وكذا إذا أقر بالزنا بفلانة وهي غائبة فإنه يحد استحساناً بخلاف ما إذا كذبته لما قدمناه. وأشار بسؤال الإمام إلى أنه لا يعتبر إقراره عند غير الحاكم لأنه لا ولاية له في إقامة الحدود ولو كان أربع مرات حتى لا تقبل الشهادة بذلك عليه لأنه إن كان منكراً رجع، ، وإن كان مقراً لا تعتبر الشهادة مع الإقرار ؛ كذا في التبيين. وبهذا علم أن البينة على الإقرار لا تقبل أصلاً
He said: (And he asks him, as if he clarifies the hadd?) i.e., the judge asks the confessor about the five things mentioned previously for the mentioned possibilities. If he explains what is asked, the hadd becomes obligatory. The apparent meaning of his speech is that he asks about the time and the woman with whom he committed zina, and this is the most correct opinion because of the possibility that he committed zina in his childhood or with his son's slave woman while knowing her. And the benefit of asking about the time is not limited to the possibility of prescription, which is harmful in testimony but not in confession, because there is another benefit: the possibility of it occurring during childhood. And if he is asked about the woman with whom he committed zina and says, 'I do not know her,' we have stated that he is punished. Similarly, if he confesses to zina with a certain woman who is absent, he is punished by istihsan, unlike the case where she denies him, as we mentioned. And by the judge's questioning, it is indicated that his confession is not considered before anyone other than the judge because the judge has jurisdiction to execute the hadd penalties, even if it was four times, so that testimony about it is not accepted against him because if he denies it, he retracts, and if he admits, testimony with confession is not considered. This is in al-Tabyin. And by this it is known that testimony on confession is not accepted at all.
Source pages p. 11

Commentary
This passage explains the procedure when a person confesses to zina. The judge must question the confessor about five specific matters (likely time, place, person, etc.) to rule out possibilities such as the act having occurred during childhood or with a legally forbidden relative. The questioning about time is crucial because it may reveal that the act occurred during minority, which would nullify the hadd. If the confessor does not know the woman, he is still punished. If he confesses about a woman who is absent, he is punished by istihsan (juristic preference). Importantly, the confession must be made before the judge; it is not valid before others. Furthermore, if someone testifies that they heard the confession, that testimony is not accepted because if the person denies it, his retraction is considered, and if he admits, the testimony is superfluous. Thus, evidence (bayyinah) on a confession is not accepted.

Key Terms
الاستحسان (al-istihsān): Juristic preference; departure from qiyas for a stronger reason.
البينة (al-bayyinah): Evidence, specifically testimony of witnesses.
الإقرار (al-iqrār): Confession, admission of guilt.
الحد (al-ḥadd): Fixed corporal punishment prescribed by Islamic law for specific crimes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, always.
B) No, not at all.
C) Yes, if the confessor does not retract.
D) Only if the confession was made in front of the judge.

Key Takeaway
Testimony on a confession is never accepted in Hanafi hadd cases; the confession must be made directly to the judge and verified through questioning.

Retraction of Confession in Pure Hadd Penalties
Ruling that retraction of confession is valid for pure hadd penalties

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on retraction of confession in pure hadd penalties and distinguish it from cases involving the right of a person.

Core Idea
Retraction of confession in pure hadd penalties creates doubt and averts the punishment.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains a fundamental rule in Hanafi criminal law: a person who confesses to a hadd crime (like theft or zina) may retract that confession before or even during the punishment, and the penalty is dropped. The reasoning is that retraction is a statement that could be true, and since no one denies it, a doubt (shubha) arises, and the hadd is averted. However, this mercy does not apply when the penalty involves a personal right, such as in qisas or the hadd of qadhf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Ruling
State clearly: retraction of confession is valid for pure hadd penalties (exclusive rights of Allah) and the accused is released.
This applies to penalties like hudud for zina, drinking, theft, etc.
2
Analyze the Legal Proof (Talil)
The proof is that retraction is a report that may be true, like the original confession. Since no one contradicts it, a doubt arises, and hadd is averted by doubts.
This is based on the principle that doubts avert hadd penalties.
3
Distinguish Cases with Personal Rights
Identify that retraction is not accepted for qisas (retaliation) or the hadd of qadhf (false accusation) because the victim or heirs can deny the retraction – there is a personal right involved.
In qadhf, the accused person's right to clear their name is involved.
4
Examine the Scope of Retraction
Retraction can be by word (verbal denial) or by action (e.g., running away). But if the hadd is proven by testimony (not confession), running away does not stop the punishment.
Also, retraction is valid even if it involves the condition of ihsan (being married) because that condition is part of the hadd right of Allah.
5
Apply to Specific Hadd Penalties
List pure hadd penalties: theft (sariqa), drinking (shurb), zina (when proven by confession). For each, retraction is valid. For qisas and qadhf, retraction is invalid.
Be careful: theft also involves a victim's right to property, but the hadd itself is a right of Allah; retraction averts the hadd but the victim may still claim the stolen property through civil means.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (فإن رجع عن إقراره قبل الحد أو في وسطه خلى سبيله) لأن الرجوع خبر محتمل للصدق كالإقرار وليس أحد يكذبه فيه فتحقق الشبهة بالإقرار بخلاف ما فيه حق العبد وهو القصاص وحد القذف لوجود من يكذبه ولا كذلك ما هو خالص حق الشرع. أطلق في الرجوع فشمل الرجوع بالقول أو بالفعل كما إذا هرب كما في الحاوي . وقيد بالإقرار لأنه لو ثبت الزنا بالبينة فهرب في حال الرجم اتبع بالحجارة حتى يقضى عليه؛ في الحاوي. وإنكار الإقرار رجوع كإنكار الردة توبة قال في الخانية: رجل أقر عند القاضي بالزنا أربع مرات فأمر القاضي برجمه فقال والله ما أقررت بشيء يدرأ عند الحد اهـ . وكذا يصح الرجوع عن الإقرار بالإحصان لأنه لما صار شرطاً للحد صار حق الله تعالى فصح الرجوع عنه لعدم المكذب ؛ كذا في الكشف الكبير من بحث العلامة. وقد ظهر بما ذكرنا أنه يصح الرجوع عن الإقرار بالحدود الخالصة كحد الشرب والسرقة .
He said: (If he retracts his confession before or during the hadd, he is released) because retraction is a report that may be true, like the confession, and there is no one to deny it, so a doubt occurs regarding the confession. This is unlike cases involving the right of a person, such as retaliation and the hadd of qadhf, where there is someone to deny him. And it is not like that which is purely the right of Allah. The retraction is unrestricted, so it includes retraction by word or by action, such as running away, as in al-Hawi. And it is restricted to confession because if zina is established by testimony and he runs away during stoning, he is followed with stones until it is carried out, as in al-Hawi. And denial of the confession is a retraction, just as denial of apostasy is repentance. It is stated in al-Khaniyyah: A man confessed to the judge four times, and the judge ordered his stoning. He said, 'By Allah, I did not confess anything,' so it averts the hadd. Similarly, retraction of confession regarding ihsan (being married) is valid because when it becomes a condition for the hadd, it becomes a right of Allah, so retraction is valid because there is no one to deny it. This is in al-Kashf al-Kabir from the research of the commentator. And it is clear from what we have mentioned that retraction of confession for pure hadd penalties, such as the hadd of drinking and theft, is valid.
Source pages p. 12

Commentary
This passage explains that retraction of a confession before or during the execution of the hadd penalty is accepted, because retraction is a statement that could be true, and there is no one to contradict it, thus creating a doubt (shubha). This applies to penalties that are purely the right of Allah (huquq Allah), such as the hadd for zina, drinking, and theft. However, in cases involving the rights of people (e.g., qisas for murder or the hadd for qadhf), retraction is not accepted because the victim or his heirs can deny the retraction. Retraction can be by word or by action (like running away). But if the hadd is proven by testimony rather than confession, running away does not stop it. Additionally, denying the confession is considered retraction. The passage also states that retraction of confession regarding ihsan (being married, which is a condition for stoning) is valid because ihsan becomes a right of Allah.

Key Terms
الرجوع (al-rujū'): Retraction; taking back a confession.
القذف (al-qadhf): False accusation of zina; its hadd is 80 lashes.
الإحصان (al-iḥṣān): The state of being married (and having consummated) which subjects the adulterer to stoning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, retraction of confession is NOT accepted for which of the following?
A) Hadd of theft (sariqa)
B) Hadd of drinking (shurb)
C) Hadd of qadhf (false accusation)
D) Hadd of zina (when based on confession)

Key Takeaway
Retraction of confession is accepted in pure hadd penalties (huquq Allah) because it creates a doubt, but not when a personal right is involved.

Proof of Zina: Testimony or Confession, Not Judge's Knowledge
Ruling on proof of zina and intra-Hanafi dispute on mixed evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two acceptable proofs for zina in Hanafi law, explain why the judge's personal knowledge is insufficient, and apply the ruling on conflicting evidence (four sinful witnesses plus one confession) according to the positions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.

Core Idea
Zina is proven only by four upright witnesses or confession; doubt (shubha) averts the hadd.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies a foundational principle in Hanafi hudud law: the fixed punishment for zina cannot be imposed based on the judge's private knowledge. Instead, the law requires clear external evidence—either four male witnesses or a voluntary confession. The author then examines a contested scenario where imperfect evidence from both sources exists, illustrating how Hanafi imams differ on whether the hadd can still be applied.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two exclusive means of proof
The text explicitly limits proof of zina to bayyinah (testimony) and iqrar (confession). Recognize that no other method—such as the judge's personal observation or circumstantial evidence—is acceptable.
This exclusion is a distinctive feature of Hanafi hudud law, grounded in the principle of dar' al-hudud bi al-shubuhat (avert hadd punishments by doubts).
2
Understand the prohibition of combining evidence
Confession and testimony cannot be combined to establish zina. The author cites the case of four sinful witnesses plus a single confession to demonstrate this: both are deficient, so the hadd is not imposed.
The reasoning: each piece of evidence is incomplete on its own (witnesses are fasiq, confession is only once), so together they create a shubha that blocks the hadd.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Compare the positions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. Abu Yusuf holds that the hadd is not imposed due to the combined doubt, while Muhammad holds that the hadd is imposed because the accused's own confession (even once) removes the doubt from the fasiq witnesses.
Sarakhsi adopts Muhammad's view. The text does not explicitly choose a mufta bihi, indicating that this ikhtilaf remains relevant for later fatwa.
4
Apply the principle to analogous cases
Consider other hudud (e.g., theft, drinking) or mixed evidence scenarios. The same logic applies: any doubt arising from deficient evidence will prevent the hadd.
The principle is general: 'al-hudud tudra' bi al-shubuhat' (hudud are averted by doubts).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحدود عن إقراره قبل الحد أو في وسطه خلى سبيله وندب تلقينه بلعلك قبلت أو لمست أو مرة أو كل شهر مرة فإنه يحد .اهـ. وأشار المصنف باقتصاره على البيئة والإقرار إلى أن الزنا لا يثبت بعلم القاضي وكذلك سائر الحدود الخالصة كذا في الذخيرة. وإلى أن الإقرار والشهادة لا يجتمعان فلذا قال في الظهيرية والذخيرة : أربعة فسقة شهدوا على رجل بالزنا وأقر هو مرة واحدة لا يحد. ولو كان الشهود عدولاً. ذكر شمس الأئمة السرخسي أنه يحد وذكر غيره من المشايخ أن على قول محمد يحد وعلى قول أبي يوسف لا يحد اهـ.
Book of Hudud: Regarding his confession before the hadd or during it, he is released, and it is recommended to prompt him with 'Perhaps you kissed or touched or once or every month?' Then he is punished. End. The author indicated by limiting to testimony and confession that zina is not established by the judge's knowledge, and similarly all pure hudud, as in al-Dhakhira. And that confession and testimony do not combine, hence he said in al-Zahiriyya and al-Dhakhira: Four sinful people testified against a man for zina and he confessed once, he is not punished. Even if the witnesses were upright. Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi said he is punished, and other mashayikh said that according to Muhammad he is punished, and according to Abu Yusuf he is not punished. End.
Source pages p. 12

Commentary
This passage begins a discussion on the proof of zina in Hanafi law. The author states that if a person confesses before the hadd punishment is carried out, or during it, he is to be released, and it is recommended (mandub) to prompt him to retract by suggesting he might have kissed or touched, etc. The author then indicates two important points by limiting the proof of zina to testimony (bayyinah) and confession (iqrar): first, zina cannot be established by the judge's private knowledge; second, confession and testimony cannot be combined to establish the offense. A specific case is cited: if four sinful witnesses testify against a man for zina, and he also confesses once, he is not punished. Even if the witnesses are upright (udul), there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: according to Imam Muhammad, he is punished; according to Abu Yusuf, he is not. Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi holds the view that he is punished. The passage thus clarifies the evidentiary rules for hudud, emphasizing the preference for sparing the accused whenever possible (dar' al-hudud bi al-shubuhat).

Key Terms
حد (hadd): The fixed corporal punishment prescribed by Shari'ah for certain crimes (zina, theft, etc.).
إقرار (iqrar): Confession of a crime or liability, especially in hudud cases.
بينة (bayyinah): Proof or testimony; in hudud, specifically four male witnesses for zina.
شبهة (shubha): Doubt that averts the hadd punishment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He is punished (hadd is imposed).
B) He is not punished.
C) He is imprisoned until further evidence.
D) The testimony is accepted and he is stoned.

Key Takeaway
Zina is proven only by four upright witnesses or a fourfold confession; the judge's personal knowledge is invalid, and imperfect evidence from both sources combined still averts the hadd due to doubt.

Judge's Interrogation of the Zina Confessor
Ruling on judge's interrogation of a zina confessor

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the procedure for a judge's interrogation of a confessor to zina and identify when the hadd becomes wajib.

Core Idea
The judge must actively seek doubts by questioning — only a confession that withstands scrutiny triggers the hadd.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq explains the judge's duty to ask the confessor about time and woman. This is not a formality; it is a substantive safeguard to avert the hadd if any doubt appears. Understanding this procedure reveals the Hanafi commitment to protecting the accused.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling
The judge must ask the confessor about five specific matters (time, woman, etc.) to uncover possible doubts.
The five matters are mentioned earlier in the text.
2
Recognize the two key questions
The author emphasizes asking about the time and the identity of the woman, as these are most likely to reveal a doubt.
3
Understand the underlying reasons
The questioning aims to uncover if the act occurred during childhood or if the confessor mistakenly believed the woman was permissible (e.g., his son's slave-girl).
These doubts would prevent the hadd.
4
Apply to special cases
If the woman is absent and does not deny, the confessor is still punished by istihsan. If she denies, the hadd is averted.
Istihsan departs from strict analogy to avoid a miscarriage of justice.
5
Note the principle of jurisdiction
Confession is only valid before a judge with authority to implement hudud. Testimony on confession is not accepted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وسأله كما فإن بينه حد) أي سأل الحاكم المقر عن الأشياء الخمسة المتقدمة للاحتمالات المذكورة فإن بين المسؤول عنه وجب الحد وظاهر كلامه أنه يسأله عن الزمان والمزني بها وهذا هو الأصح لاحتمال أنه زنى في صباه أو زنى بجارية ابنه وهو يعلمها . وليس فائدة السؤال عن الزمان منحصرة في احتمال التقادم وهو مضر في الشهادة دون الإقرار لأن له فائدة أخرى وهو احتمال وجوده في زمن الصبا. ولو سئل عن المزني بها فقال لا أعرفها قدمنا أنه يحد، وكذا إذا أقر بالزنا بفلانة وهي غائبة فإنه يحد استحساناً بخلاف ما إذا كذبته لما قدمناه. وأشار بسؤال الإمام إلى أنه لا يعتبر إقراره عند غير الحاكم لأنه لا ولاية له في إقامة الحدود ولو كان أربع مرات حتى لا تقبل الشهادة بذلك عليه لأنه إن كان منكراً رجع، ، وإن كان مقراً لا تعتبر الشهادة مع الإقرار ؛ كذا في التبيين. وبهذا علم أن البينة على الإقرار لا تقبل أصلاً
His saying: (And ask him, as it clarifies the hadd): That is, the judge asks the confessor about the five things previously mentioned for the possibilities mentioned. If he clarifies what was asked, the hadd becomes obligatory. The apparent meaning of his statement is that he asks him about the time and the woman with whom he committed zina, and this is the most correct view, due to the possibility that he committed zina in his childhood or with his son's slave-girl thinking she was his own. The benefit of asking about time is not limited to the possibility of prescription, which is harmful in testimony but not in confession, because it has another benefit: the possibility that it occurred during childhood. If he is asked about the woman and says 'I do not know her', we previously stated that he is punished. Similarly, if he confesses to zina with a certain woman who is absent, he is punished by istihsan, unlike if she denies it, as we have mentioned. The author indicated by the judge's questioning that his confession is not considered before other than the judge, because they have no authority to establish hadd even if it is four times, so that testimony against him is not accepted. If he denies, he retracts; if he confesses, testimony is not considered with confession; as in al-Tabyin. And by this it is known that testimony based on confession is not accepted at all.
Source pages p. 12

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the base text's statement: 'And ask him, as it clarifies the hadd.' It explains that the judge must interrogate the confessor about five specific matters to uncover possible doubts. The author says the correct view is that the judge asks about the time and the identity of the woman, because the confession might be about an act committed during childhood (when one is not legally responsible) or with a woman he mistakenly believed was permissible (e.g., his son's slave-girl). The purpose of asking about time is not just to check for prescription (which affects testimony but not confession), but also to catch the possibility that the act occurred under age. If the confessor says he doesn't know the woman, he is still punished (hadd applied). If he confesses to zina with a specific absent woman, he is punished by istihsan (juristic preference), unless the woman denies it, in which case the hadd is averted. The text also clarifies that confession is only valid before a judge who has jurisdiction to enforce hudud. Testimony based on a confession is not accepted, because the confession itself suffices and testimony would create a conflict. Thus, testimony on confession is never admissible.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; a method of departing from strict analogy for a more equitable outcome.
تقادم (taqadum): Prescription; the lapse of a long period of time affecting the admissibility of testimony.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a person confesses to zina with a specific absent woman, and she does not deny it?
A) He is not punished because she is absent.
B) He is punished by istihsan.
C) He is punished only if she confirms it.
D) He is given a discretionary punishment.

Key Takeaway
The judge must actively seek doubts in a confession; only after thorough questioning can the hadd be applied.

Retraction of Confession in Pure Hudud
Ruling on retraction of confession in pure hudud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on retraction of confession in pure hudud and explain the proof based on shubha (doubt).

Core Idea
Retraction in pure hudud creates doubt because no one contradicts it, so the hadd is averted.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains a key principle in Hanafi criminal law: the acceptance of retraction of confession in hudud punishments that are purely the right of Allah. The ruling is based on the idea that a retraction, like the original confession, is a claim that could be true. Since there is no private party to dispute it, doubt arises and the harsh punishment is dropped. This lesson will walk you through the ruling, its proof, and its scope.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Determine what act is being discussed (retraction of confession in hudud) and the legal consequence (the person is released if retraction occurs before or during the hadd).
The ruling applies only to pure hudud (Allah's rights), not to qisas or qadhf.
2
Locate the proof (dalil)
Find the reasoning given: 'because retraction is a statement that may be true, like the confession, and there is no one to contradict it, so doubt is established.'
This is a rational proof based on the principle of shubha.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Understand how the proof leads to the ruling: the retraction introduces uncertainty (doubt) because it could be true and no one challenges it; in Hanafi law, hadd punishments are averted by doubts.
This is a manifestation of the maxim 'ad-dar'u bi sh-shubuhat' (hadd punishments are averted by doubts).
4
Contrast with qisas and qadhf
Note that the text differentiates pure hudud from cases involving rights of individuals, where there is a contradictor (victim or heirs) who can deny the retraction, so doubt is not created.
This explains why retraction is not accepted in qisas or qadhf.
5
Examine the scope of retraction
Identify what constitutes retraction: verbal retraction, denial of confession, and even fleeing (action) count as retraction, but only if the case is based on confession not testimony.
The text also confirms that retraction of confession of ihsan is valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (فإن رجع عن إقراره قبل الحد أو في وسطه خلى سبيله) لأن الرجوع خبر محتمل للصدق كالإقرار وليس أحد يكذبه فيه فتحقق الشبهة بالإقرار بخلاف ما فيه حق العبد وهو القصاص وحد القذف لوجود من يكذبه ولا كذلك ما هو خالص حق الشرع. أطلق في الرجوع فشمل الرجوع بالقول أو بالفعل كما إذا هرب كما في الحاوي . وقيد بالإقرار لأنه لو ثبت الزنا بالبينة فهرب في حال الرجم اتبع بالحجارة حتى يقضى عليه؛ في الحاوي. وإنكار الإقرار رجوع كإنكار الردة توبة قال في الخانية: رجل أقر عند القاضي بالزنا أربع مرات فأمر القاضي برجمه فقال والله ما أقررت بشيء يدرأ عند الحد اهـ . وكذا يصح الرجوع عن الإقرار بالإحصان لأنه لما صار شرطاً للحد صار حق الله تعالى فصح الرجوع عنه لعدم المكذب ؛ كذا في الكشف الكبير من بحث العلامة. وقد ظهر بما ذكرنا أنه يصح الرجوع عن الإقرار بالحدود الخالصة كحد الشرب والسرقة . فقد كذا
His saying: (If he retracts his confession before the hadd or during it, he is released) because retraction is a statement that may be true, like the confession, and there is no one to contradict it, so doubt is established by the confession, unlike what involves a right of a servant, i.e., qisas and hadd of qadhf, because there is someone who contradicts it. Retraction is general, including retraction by word or by action, like fleeing, as in al-Hawi. It is restricted to confession, because if zina is proven by testimony and he flees during stoning, he is pursued with stones until he dies; in al-Hawi. Denial of confession is retraction, like denial of apostasy is repentance. He said in al-Khaniyya: A man confessed before the judge to zina four times, and the judge ordered his stoning. He said, 'By Allah, I did not confess anything,' which averts the hadd. End. Similarly, retraction of confession of ihsan (marital status) is valid, because since it became a condition for the hadd, it became a right of Allah, so retraction is valid due to lack of a contradictor; as in al-Kashf al-Kabir from the research of the commentator. And it appears from what we have mentioned that retraction of confession in pure hudud, like the hadd for drinking and theft, is valid. End.
Source pages p. 12

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling on retracting a confession in hudud cases. The base text states that if a person retracts his confession before or during the execution of the hadd punishment, he is to be released. The reason given is that the retraction, like the original confession, is a statement that could be true, and there is no one who contradicts it (unlike in cases involving the rights of individuals, such as qisas or the hadd of qadhf, where the victim or claimant contradicts the retraction). Therefore, a doubt (shubha) arises and the hadd is averted. Retraction can be verbal or by action, such as fleeing. However, if the zina is proven by testimony (not confession), fleeing does not stop the punishment; he is pursued. Denial of the confession is considered a valid retraction. The text also mentions that retraction of the confession of ihsan (being in a valid marriage, which makes one eligible for stoning) is valid because it is a condition for the hadd and thus part of Allah's right. This confirms that retraction is accepted in all pure hudud (where only Allah's right is involved), such as the hadd for drinking and theft.

Key Terms
إقرار (iqrar): Confession of a crime, especially in hudud.
إحصان (ihsan): The state of being married (free, Muslim, adult) that makes one liable for stoning for zina.
شبهة (shubhah): Doubt that causes the hadd to be averted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is retraction of confession accepted in pure hudud (like hadd for drinking) but not in cases involving rights of individuals (like qisas)?
A) Because in pure hudud, there is no one to contradict the retraction, creating doubt.
B) Because pure hudud are less serious offenses.
C) Because the judge has the authority to pardon in pure hudud.
D) Because the confession in pure hudud is usually coerced.

Key Takeaway
Retraction of confession in pure hudud is valid and averts the punishment because it introduces doubt that no one contradicts.

The Wedding Procession as a Shubha Averting Hadd
Ruling with illustrative case on shubha in hudud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general rule that testimony on confession is not accepted, explain the exception of seven cases, and apply the concept of shubha to determine when hadd is averted in cases of mistaken intercourse.

Core Idea
A genuine external circumstance like a wedding procession creates a shubha that averts hadd; a bare claim of mistake does not.

This lesson examines a foundational rule in Hanafi testimony law: that testimony based on a confession is not accepted as evidence. The commentator then expands this with a concrete case from Kafi al-Hakim, contrasting two scenarios of mistaken intercourse. Understanding this distinction is crucial for applying the principle of shubha in hudud rulings, where doubts can avert severe penalties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Rule
Locate the base statement: testimony on confession is not accepted at all. Note that this is the default rule, and there are seven exceptions (not detailed here).
The exceptions are mentioned in al-Ashbah.
2
Parse the First Case (Wedding Procession)
Read the case: a man marries, but during the wedding another woman is brought to him and he has intercourse believing she is his wife. The ruling: no hadd on him, nor on his slanderer.
Focus on the external circumstance: the wedding procession (zufaf) is present.
3
Identify the Basis for Shubha
The text gives evidence: if a child is born, lineage is established from the man, showing that the intercourse was treated as valid in terms of lineage. This proves a strong doubt (shubha) that she was his wife.
The doubt is not just subjective but supported by a societal event.
4
Contrast with the Second Case (Bare Claim)
Read the second case: a man fornicates and then claims he thought she was his wife. The ruling: hadd is upon him. There is no external circumstance; his claim alone is insufficient.
The distinction is critical: shubha requires an objective basis.
5
Derive the Legal Principle
Conclude that averted hadd requires a plausible external situation that would make a reasonable person believe the woman was his wife. Mere after-the-fact excuses do not count.
This aligns with Hanafi reluctance to apply hadd in cases of genuine doubt.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وبهذا علم أن البينة على الإقرار لا تقبل أصلاً) أي إلا في سبع ذكرها في الأشباه. قوله: وبهذا علم الخ) في كافي الحاكم رجل تزوج فزفت له أخرى فوطئها قال : لا حد عليه ولا على قاذفه رجل فجر بامرأة ثم قال حسبتها امرأتي قال عليه الحد وليست هذه كالأولى لأن الزفاف شبهة ألا ترى أنها إن جاءت بولد ثبت نسبه منه، وإن جاءت هذه التي فجر بها بولد لم أثبت نسبه منه اهـ. ويمكن أن يفرق بين هذه وبين التي ذكرها المؤلف بأن التي ذكرها المؤلف هو جازم بأنها وطئت بشبهة
His saying: (And by this it is known that testimony on confession is not accepted at all) i.e., except in seven cases mentioned in al-Ashbah. His saying: (And by this it is known) in Kafi al-Hakim: A man married, and another woman was brought to him, and he had intercourse with her. He said: There is no hadd on him nor on his slanderer. A man fornicated with a woman and then said, 'I thought she was my wife.' He said: Hadd is upon him, and this is not like the first case because the wedding procession is a shubha. Do you not see that if she brings a child, his lineage is established from him? And if this woman with whom he fornicated brings a child, we do not establish his lineage from him. End. And one can distinguish between this case and the one mentioned by the author: that the one mentioned by the author is certain that he had intercourse with a shubha.
Source pages p. 12

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on testimony based on confession. The base text states that testimony on confession is not accepted at all, but the commentator adds that there are seven exceptional cases mentioned in al-Ashbah. Then it relates a case from Kafi al-Hakim: A man married, but during the wedding, another woman (not his wife) was brought to him and he had intercourse with her, mistakenly thinking she was his wife. The ruling is that there is no hadd (punishment) on him, nor on anyone who slanders him (accuses him of zina). In contrast, if a man fornicates with a woman and then claims he thought she was his wife, the hadd is imposed on him. The distinction is that in the first case, the wedding procession (zufaf) creates a strong doubt (shubha) that he believed the woman was his wife. Evidence for this doubt is that if she bears a child, the child's lineage is attributed to the man (i.e., paternity is established), whereas in the second case, lineage is not established. The commentator then notes that one can differentiate between this case and the one mentioned by the author: the author's case is where the man is certain that he had intercourse under a shubha (i.e., he was genuinely mistaken). This section highlights the principle that doubts (shubuhat) arising from circumstances can avert the hadd, but mere claims without context are insufficient.

Key Terms
شبهة (shubhah): A plausible doubt arising from circumstances that averts the hadd punishment.
زفاف (zufaf): Wedding procession; a specific event that can create a shubha of believing a woman is one's wife.
بينة على الإقرار (bayyinah 'ala al-iqrar): Testimony based on a confession; evidence that reports someone's confession.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case from Kafi al-Hakim, why is there no hadd on the man who had intercourse with the woman brought during his wedding?
A) Because he did not commit zina intentionally.
B) Because the wedding procession created a strong doubt that she was his wife.
C) Because his wife forgave him.
D) Because the woman was a slave.

Key Takeaway
A hadd punishment for zina is averted when the defendant's mistake is supported by an objective, credible external circumstance that would lead a reasonable person to the same belief.

The Obligation of Stoning the Muhsan and Its Proofs
Ruling on stoning the muhsan with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi obligation of stoning the muhsan, cite the proofs from Sunnah and ijma, and refute the Khawarij denial.

Core Idea
Stoning the muhsan is established by tawatur and ijma; denial is invalid.

The hadd for a muhsan (married, free Muslim) who commits zina is stoning to death. This lesson explores the ruling, its evidentiary basis, and the refutation of those who deny stoning. You will see how the Hanafi school grounds this ruling in the Prophet's practice, the consensus of the Companions, and the principle of tawatur in meaning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its conditions
Note that the ruling applies to a muhsan. The punishment is stoning in an open space until death.
The Hanafi definition of muhsan includes free, adult, Muslim, and having consummated a valid marriage.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The text cites the Prophet's stoning of Ma'iz and his statement 'zina after ihsan'. This is a mutawatir practice.
The asl is the act of the Prophet (peace be upon him), which is qat'i in thubut.
3
Confirm with ijma
The Companions unanimously agreed on stoning for the muhsan. This ijma is definitive.
Ijma of the Companions is a source of shar'i law.
4
Refute the Khawarij denial
The author argues that denying stoning stems from either rejecting ijma or rejecting ahad hadith, both invalid. Stoning is proven by tawatur in meaning.
Tawatur in meaning means the general concept is certain, even if specific details come through ahad.
5
Understand the place of stoning
The text mentions stoning in an open space, based on the practice of the Prophet at the Musalla.
Open space is to avoid damage to property and allow crowd control, but it's not a strict condition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن كان محصناً رجمه في فضاء حتى يموت يبدأ الشهود به فإن أبوا سقط قوله : (وندب تلقينه بلعلك قبلت أو لمست أو وطئت بشبهة الحديث ماعز في البخاري «لعلك قبلت أو غمزت أو نظرت. وقال في الأصل : ينبغي أن يقول له لعلك تزوجتها أو وطئتها بشبهة. والمقصود أن يلقنه بما يكون ذكره دارئاً ليذكره كائناً ما كان كما قال عليه السلام للسارق الذي جيء به إليه أسرقت وما أخاله سرق أي وما أظنه سرق تلقيناً له ليرجع. وبهذا علم أن الزاني لو ادعى أنها زوجته سقط الحد عنه وإن كانت زوجة للغير ولا يكلف إقامة البينة للشبهة كما لو ادعى السارق أن العين مملوكة له سقط القطع بمجرد دعواه . وفي المحيط : لو تزوج المزني بها أو اشتراها لا يسقط الحد في ظاهر الرواية لأنه لا شبهة له وقت الفعل قوله : (فإن كان محصناً رجمه في فضاء حتى يموت لأنه عليه السلام رجم ماعزاً وقد كان أحصن وقال في الحديث المعروف وزناً بعد إحصان». وعلى هذا إجماع الصحابة. وإنكار الخوارج الرجم باطل لأنهم إن أنكروا حجية إجماع الصحابة فجهل مركب بالدليل بل هو إجماع قطعي، وإن أنكروا وقوعه من رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم الإنكارهم حجية خبر الواحد فهو بعد بطلانه بالدليل ليس مما نحن فيه لأن ثبوت الرجم عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم متواتر المعنى كشجاعة علي وجود حاتم، والآحاد في تفاصيل صوره وخصوصياته؛ كذا في فتح القدير . وإنما يرجم في الفضاء لحديث البخاري أن ماعزا رجم بالمصلى وفي مسلم: فانطلقنا به إلى بقيع الغرقد فإن المصلي كان به وهو مصلي الجنائة في الحيط : المقضى برج إذا قتله انسان أو فقأ عينه لا شيء عليه ولو قتله قبل القضاء يحب القصاص إن كان عمداً والدية إن كان خطأ قوله : (يبدأ الشهود به أي بالرجم يعني على وجه الشرط ولو بحصاة صغيرة، هكذا روي عن علي رضي الله عنه، ولأن الشاهد قد يتجاسر على الأداء ثم يستعظم المباشرة فيرجع فكان في بدايته احتيال للدرء وقال الشافعي : لا يشترط بدايتهم اعتباراً بالجلد. قلنا : كل أحد لا يحسن الجلد فربما يقع مهلكاً والإهلاك غير مستحق ولا كذلك الرجم إتلاف قوله : (فإن أبو اسقط أي إن امتنع الشهود من الابتداء سقط الحد لأنه دلالة الرجوع، وكذا إذا ماتوا أو غابوا في ظاهر الرواية لفوات الشرط. ولا يجب الحد عليهم لو امتنعوا لأنه دلالة الرجوع لا صريحه وامتناع البعض أو غيبته كالكل، وكذا إذا خرج بعض الشهود عن الأهلية بارتداد أو عمى أو خرس أو فسق أو قذف سواء كان قبل القضاء أو بعده، لأن في الحدود، وأما قطع اليدين فإن كان بعد الشهادة امتنعت الإقامة، وإن القضاء الإمضاء من
If he is a muhsan (married), he is stoned in an open space until he dies. The witnesses begin the stoning; if they refuse, the punishment is dropped. His saying: (And it is recommended to prompt him with 'Perhaps you kissed, touched, or committed zina with a shubha'.) The hadith of Ma'iz in Bukhari: 'Perhaps you kissed, winked, or looked.' And he said in al-Asl: He should say to him: 'Perhaps you married her or committed zina with a shubha.' The purpose is to prompt him with something that will avert the punishment if he mentions it, whatever it may be, as the Prophet (peace be upon him) said to the thief who was brought to him: 'Did you steal? And I do not think you stole,' i.e., I do not suspect you stole, prompting him to retract. And by this it is known that if the adulterer claims that she is his wife, the hadd is dropped from him, even if she is the wife of another, and he is not required to produce evidence for the doubt, just as if the thief claims the object is his property, the cutting of the hand is dropped by his mere claim. In al-Muhit: If he marries the woman with whom he committed zina or buys her, the hadd is not dropped in the apparent narration because he had no doubt at the time of the act. His saying: (If he is a muhsan, he is stoned in an open space until he dies) because the Prophet (peace be upon him) stoned Ma'iz, who was muhsan, and said in the well-known hadith: 'He committed zina after ihsan.' And upon this there is consensus of the Companions. The denial of the Khawarij of stoning is invalid because if they deny the authority of consensus of the Companions, it is compounded ignorance of the evidence, rather it is definitive consensus; and if they deny its occurrence from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) due to their denial of the authority of ahad hadith, it is after its invalidation by evidence not relevant here because the establishment of stoning from the Messenger of Allah is tawatur in meaning, like the bravery of 'Ali and the generosity of Hatim, while ahad reports are in the details of its forms and specificities; as in Fath al-Qadir. He is only stoned in an open space due to the hadith of Bukhari that Ma'iz was stoned at the Musalla, and in Muslim: 'We took him to Baqi' al-Gharqad.' And the Musalla is for funeral prayer in the vicinity. The condemned to stoning: if a man kills him or gouges out his eye, there is no liability on him; but if he kills him before the judgment, qisas is required if intentional, and diyah if mistaken. His saying: (The witnesses begin the stoning) meaning, as a condition, even with a small pebble. Thus it is narrated from 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him), and because the witness may be bold in giving testimony but then find the act of stoning too severe and retract, so having them begin is a precaution to avert the punishment. Al-Shafi'i said: Their beginning is not a condition, by analogy with flogging. We say: Everyone is not skilled at flogging, so it might become lethal, and killing is not deserved, unlike stoning which is destruction. His saying: (If they refuse, it is dropped): If the witnesses refuse to begin, the hadd is dropped because it is an indication of retraction. Similarly, if they die or are absent, in the apparent narration, because the condition is lost. The hadd is not incumbent on them for their refusal, because it is an indication of retraction, not explicit retraction. The refusal or absence of some is like that of all. Similarly, if some witnesses lose their eligibility by apostasy, blindness, dumbness, sinfulness, or slander, whether before or after the judgment, because in hudud... As for cutting of the hands, if it occurs after testimony, the implementation is prevented, and the judgment is executed from...
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This passage deals with the stoning of a muhsan (a married, free Muslim who has consummated marriage) for zina. The ruling is that such a person is to be stoned in an open space until death. The text then discusses the recommended (mandub) prompting of the confessor to claim a doubt (shubha) to avert the punishment, citing the example of Ma'iz in Bukhari. If the accused claims she was his wife, the hadd is dropped without requiring evidence, analogous to a thief claiming ownership. However, if after the act he marries or buys the woman, the hadd is not dropped because no doubt existed at the time. The stoning of a muhsan is established by the Prophet's action (stoning Ma'iz), consensus of the Companions, and is a matter of tawatur in meaning; the denials of the Khawarij are refuted. The procedure requires that the witnesses begin the stoning, even with a small pebble; this is a condition (shart) because the witness may retract, thus averting the punishment. Imam al-Shafi'i disagreed, saying their starting is not a condition. The Hanafi response is that flogging (jild) is different because an unskilled flogger might kill, whereas stoning is intended to kill. If the witnesses refuse to start, the hadd is dropped as it indicates retraction. Similarly, if they die, become absent, or lose legal capacity, the hadd is not executed. The text ends with a partial discussion on cutting of hands, noting that after testimony, the punishment is not implemented if the witness becomes ineligible, but the judgment is executed.

Key Terms
محصن (muhsan): A person who is free, Muslim, adult, and has consummated a valid marriage; liable for stoning for zina.
رجم (rajm): Stoning to death as the hadd for zina committed by a muhsan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school consider stoning for the muhsan to be definitively established?
A) Because the Quran explicitly commands stoning.
B) Because of the mutawatir practice of the Prophet and consensus of the Companions.
C) Because only ahad hadith support it.
D) Because the Khawarij accept stoning.

Key Takeaway
Stoning the muhsan is wajib, proven by mutawatir sunnah and ijma; any denial is based on ignorance.

The Recommended Prompting (Talqin) to Avert Hadd
Recommended talqin and its effect on hadd

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi recommendation of talqin, apply it to a confession scenario, and identify when a claim of doubt drops the hadd.

Core Idea
Talqin is a mercy to avert hadd; a claim of doubt after prompting drops the punishment.

In hudud cases, the Hanafi school encourages the judge to prompt the confessor with a doubt that could avert the punishment. This lesson examines the evidence for talqin, its application to zina and theft, and the conditions under which a claim of doubt is accepted.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on talqin
The text states that talqin is recommended (mandub). It is not obligatory but encouraged to help the confessor retract.
Talqin is derived from the Prophet's example with Ma'iz and the thief.
2
Examine the examples
The Prophet said to Ma'iz: 'Perhaps you kissed, winked, or looked.' To the thief: 'Did you steal? I do not think you stole.'
This shows the goal is to give an opportunity to retract without lying.
3
Understand the effect of claiming doubt
If the accused claims a valid doubt (e.g., she was his wife), the hadd is dropped without requiring evidence.
This is analogous to a thief claiming ownership; the hadd is dropped.
4
Distinguish a post-act claim
If after the act he marries or buys the woman, the hadd is not dropped because no doubt existed at the time.
Timing is crucial: the doubt must be contemporary to the act.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن كان محصناً رجمه في فضاء حتى يموت يبدأ الشهود به فإن أبوا سقط قوله : (وندب تلقينه بلعلك قبلت أو لمست أو وطئت بشبهة الحديث ماعز في البخاري «لعلك قبلت أو غمزت أو نظرت. وقال في الأصل : ينبغي أن يقول له لعلك تزوجتها أو وطئتها بشبهة. والمقصود أن يلقنه بما يكون ذكره دارئاً ليذكره كائناً ما كان كما قال عليه السلام للسارق الذي جيء به إليه أسرقت وما أخاله سرق أي وما أظنه سرق تلقيناً له ليرجع. وبهذا علم أن الزاني لو ادعى أنها زوجته سقط الحد عنه وإن كانت زوجة للغير ولا يكلف إقامة البينة للشبهة كما لو ادعى السارق أن العين مملوكة له سقط القطع بمجرد دعواه . وفي المحيط : لو تزوج المزني بها أو اشتراها لا يسقط الحد في ظاهر الرواية لأنه لا شبهة له وقت الفعل قوله : (فإن كان محصناً رجمه في فضاء حتى يموت لأنه عليه السلام رجم ماعزاً وقد كان أحصن وقال في الحديث المعروف وزناً بعد إحصان». وعلى هذا إجماع الصحابة. وإنكار الخوارج الرجم باطل لأنهم إن أنكروا حجية إجماع الصحابة فجهل مركب بالدليل بل هو إجماع قطعي، وإن أنكروا وقوعه من رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم الإنكارهم حجية خبر الواحد فهو بعد بطلانه بالدليل ليس مما نحن فيه لأن ثبوت الرجم عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم متواتر المعنى كشجاعة علي وجود حاتم، والآحاد في تفاصيل صوره وخصوصياته؛ كذا في فتح القدير . وإنما يرجم في الفضاء لحديث البخاري أن ماعزا رجم بالمصلى وفي مسلم: فانطلقنا به إلى بقيع الغرقد فإن المصلي كان به وهو مصلي الجنائة في الحيط : المقضى برج إذا قتله انسان أو فقأ عينه لا شيء عليه ولو قتله قبل القضاء يحب القصاص إن كان عمداً والدية إن كان خطأ قوله : (يبدأ الشهود به أي بالرجم يعني على وجه الشرط ولو بحصاة صغيرة، هكذا روي عن علي رضي الله عنه، ولأن الشاهد قد يتجاسر على الأداء ثم يستعظم المباشرة فيرجع فكان في بدايته احتيال للدرء وقال الشافعي : لا يشترط بدايتهم اعتباراً بالجلد. قلنا : كل أحد لا يحسن الجلد فربما يقع مهلكاً والإهلاك غير مستحق ولا كذلك الرجم إتلاف قوله : (فإن أبو اسقط أي إن امتنع الشهود من الابتداء سقط الحد لأنه دلالة الرجوع، وكذا إذا ماتوا أو غابوا في ظاهر الرواية لفوات الشرط. ولا يجب الحد عليهم لو امتنعوا لأنه دلالة الرجوع لا صريحه وامتناع البعض أو غيبته كالكل، وكذا إذا خرج بعض الشهود عن الأهلية بارتداد أو عمى أو خرس أو فسق أو قذف سواء كان قبل القضاء أو بعده، لأن في الحدود، وأما قطع اليدين فإن كان بعد الشهادة امتنعت الإقامة، وإن القضاء الإمضاء من
If he is a muhsan (married), he is stoned in an open space until he dies. The witnesses begin the stoning; if they refuse, the punishment is dropped. His saying: (And it is recommended to prompt him with 'Perhaps you kissed, touched, or committed zina with a shubha'.) The hadith of Ma'iz in Bukhari: 'Perhaps you kissed, winked, or looked.' And he said in al-Asl: He should say to him: 'Perhaps you married her or committed zina with a shubha.' The purpose is to prompt him with something that will avert the punishment if he mentions it, whatever it may be, as the Prophet (peace be upon him) said to the thief who was brought to him: 'Did you steal? And I do not think you stole,' i.e., I do not suspect you stole, prompting him to retract. And by this it is known that if the adulterer claims that she is his wife, the hadd is dropped from him, even if she is the wife of another, and he is not required to produce evidence for the doubt, just as if the thief claims the object is his property, the cutting of the hand is dropped by his mere claim. In al-Muhit: If he marries the woman with whom he committed zina or buys her, the hadd is not dropped in the apparent narration because he had no doubt at the time of the act. His saying: (If he is a muhsan, he is stoned in an open space until he dies) because the Prophet (peace be upon him) stoned Ma'iz, who was muhsan, and said in the well-known hadith: 'He committed zina after ihsan.' And upon this there is consensus of the Companions. The denial of the Khawarij of stoning is invalid because if they deny the authority of consensus of the Companions, it is compounded ignorance of the evidence, rather it is definitive consensus; and if they deny its occurrence from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) due to their denial of the authority of ahad hadith, it is after its invalidation by evidence not relevant here because the establishment of stoning from the Messenger of Allah is tawatur in meaning, like the bravery of 'Ali and the generosity of Hatim, while ahad reports are in the details of its forms and specificities; as in Fath al-Qadir. He is only stoned in an open space due to the hadith of Bukhari that Ma'iz was stoned at the Musalla, and in Muslim: 'We took him to Baqi' al-Gharqad.' And the Musalla is for funeral prayer in the vicinity. The condemned to stoning: if a man kills him or gouges out his eye, there is no liability on him; but if he kills him before the judgment, qisas is required if intentional, and diyah if mistaken. His saying: (The witnesses begin the stoning) meaning, as a condition, even with a small pebble. Thus it is narrated from 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him), and because the witness may be bold in giving testimony but then find the act of stoning too severe and retract, so having them begin is a precaution to avert the punishment. Al-Shafi'i said: Their beginning is not a condition, by analogy with flogging. We say: Everyone is not skilled at flogging, so it might become lethal, and killing is not deserved, unlike stoning which is destruction. His saying: (If they refuse, it is dropped): If the witnesses refuse to begin, the hadd is dropped because it is an indication of retraction. Similarly, if they die or are absent, in the apparent narration, because the condition is lost. The hadd is not incumbent on them for their refusal, because it is an indication of retraction, not explicit retraction. The refusal or absence of some is like that of all. Similarly, if some witnesses lose their eligibility by apostasy, blindness, dumbness, sinfulness, or slander, whether before or after the judgment, because in hudud... As for cutting of the hands, if it occurs after testimony, the implementation is prevented, and the judgment is executed from...
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This passage deals with the stoning of a muhsan (a married, free Muslim who has consummated marriage) for zina. The ruling is that such a person is to be stoned in an open space until death. The text then discusses the recommended (mandub) prompting of the confessor to claim a doubt (shubha) to avert the punishment, citing the example of Ma'iz in Bukhari. If the accused claims she was his wife, the hadd is dropped without requiring evidence, analogous to a thief claiming ownership. However, if after the act he marries or buys the woman, the hadd is not dropped because no doubt existed at the time. The stoning of a muhsan is established by the Prophet's action (stoning Ma'iz), consensus of the Companions, and is a matter of tawatur in meaning; the denials of the Khawarij are refuted. The procedure requires that the witnesses begin the stoning, even with a small pebble; this is a condition (shart) because the witness may retract, thus averting the punishment. Imam al-Shafi'i disagreed, saying their starting is not a condition. The Hanafi response is that flogging (jild) is different because an unskilled flogger might kill, whereas stoning is intended to kill. If the witnesses refuse to start, the hadd is dropped as it indicates retraction. Similarly, if they die, become absent, or lose legal capacity, the hadd is not executed. The text ends with a partial discussion on cutting of hands, noting that after testimony, the punishment is not implemented if the witness becomes ineligible, but the judgment is executed.

Key Terms
تلقين (talqin): Prompting the confessor to mention a doubt that could avert the hadd.
شبهة (shubha): A doubt that can avert the hadd punishment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what happens if a confessing adulterer claims after talqin that the woman was his wife?
A) The hadd is still carried out because the claim is unsubstantiated.
B) The hadd is dropped without requiring evidence.
C) The hadd is delayed until proof is provided.
D) The hadd is changed to flogging.

Key Takeaway
Talqin is recommended to allow the accused to retract; a doubt claim drops the hadd even without proof.

The Condition of Witnesses Initiating Stoning and the Shafi'i Dispute
Condition of witnesses starting stoning and dispute with Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition that witnesses must start the stoning, explain the Shafi'i objection, and describe the consequences of witnesses refusing or losing capacity.

Core Idea
Witnesses must begin stoning as a condition; their refusal drops the hadd.

A key procedural point in the stoning of a muhsan is that the witnesses must initiate the stoning. The Hanafi school considers this a condition. In this lesson, we explore the evidence from 'Ali, the rationale, and the Shafi'i dispute based on analogy with flogging. We also see the effects of witnesses refusing, dying, or becoming incapacitated.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
The text states: 'the witnesses begin the stoning' – this is a condition (shart).
Even a small pebble suffices.
2
Understand the rationale
The witness may have been bold in testifying but then shrink from killing; allowing them to begin gives a chance to retract.
This is a precaution (ihtiyat) to avert punishment.
3
Analyze the Shafi'i counterargument
Al-Shafi'i analogizes to flogging, where the executioner starts, not the witnesses.
Flogging is a lesser punishment; unskilled execution may cause unintended death.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi response
Flogging and stoning differ: stoning is intentionally destructive, so witnesses begin to allow retraction; in flogging, the risk is unintended death.
Thus the condition is specific to stoning.
5
Explore consequences
If witnesses refuse, die, or become absent, the hadd is dropped because the condition is lost.
Also if they lose eligibility (apostasy, blindness, etc.) after testifying, the hadd is not executed.

Tazkir (Reminding) and Shubha in Hadd Cases: Averting Punishment
Commentary on recommending tazkir and rule of shubha

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommendation of tazkir, identify its evidence from the hadith of Ma'iz, and apply the rule that a claim of shubha at the time of the act drops the hadd.

Core Idea
Remind the confessor of excuses to give him a chance to retract; a mere claim of shubha drops the hadd.

In Hanafi fiqh, the hudud penalties are to be averted by any genuine doubt or excuse. This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq explains how a judge should gently remind a person who has confessed to zina of possible excuses, such as 'Perhaps you kissed her or thought she was your wife,' based on the Prophet's practice with Ma'iz. It then extends the principle: if the adulterer claims that the woman was his wife at the time of the act, the hadd falls even without proof, because the claim itself creates a shubha. However, marrying her after the act does not help, because the shubha must exist at the time of the act.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The text discusses 'tazkir' (reminding) of the confessor. Identify that this act is classified as 'mandub' or recommended (sunnah ghayr muakkadah) in Hanafi fiqh.
The ruling is not obligatory but highly encouraged.
2
Locate the dalil (evidence)
The author cites the hadith of Ma'iz in Sahih al-Bukhari: 'Perhaps you kissed, or gestured, or looked.' This shows the Prophet's practice of prompting excuses.
The word 'لعل' indicates a suggestive, non-coercive tone.
3
Understand the purpose and principle
The purpose is to give the confessor an opportunity to retract, thereby averting the hadd. This reflects the general principle of 'dar' al-hudud bi al-shubuhat' (avert penalties by doubts).
The same principle is applied to the thief analogy later.
4
Analyze the shubha rule and its condition
If the adulterer claims that the woman was his wife (or that he had a mistaken belief), the hadd is dropped by that claim alone, without requiring evidence. The condition is that the shubha existed at the time of the act, not afterwards (e.g., marrying her later does not help).
The thief analogy is used: if a thief claims ownership, amputation is dropped.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحدود
وطئت بشبهة فإن كان محصناً رجمه في فضاء حتى يموت يبدأ الشهود به فإن أبوا سقط قوله : (وندب تلقينه بلعلك قبلت أو لمست أو وطئت بشبهة الحديث ماعز في البخاري «لعلك قبلت أو غمزت أو نظرت. وقال في الأصل : ينبغي أن يقول له لعلك تزوجتها أو وطئتها بشبهة. والمقصود أن يلقنه بما يكون ذكره دارئاً ليذكره كائناً ما كان كما قال عليه السلام للسارق الذي جيء به إليه أسرقت وما أخاله سرق أي وما أظنه سرق تلقيناً له ليرجع. وبهذا علم أن الزاني لو ادعى أنها زوجته سقط الحد عنه وإن كانت زوجة للغير ولا يكلف إقامة البينة للشبهة كما لو ادعى السارق أن العين مملوكة له سقط القطع بمجرد دعواه . وفي المحيط : لو تزوج المزني بها أو اشتراها لا يسقط الحد في ظاهر الرواية لأنه لا شبهة له وقت الفعل
Book of Penalties. If one is stoned due to shubha, then if he is muhsan (married), he is stoned in an open space until death. The witnesses begin with him; if they refuse, it falls. He said: (And it is recommended to remind him, saying 'Perhaps you kissed, or touched, or stoned due to shubha' [citing] the hadith of Ma'iz in Bukhari: 'Perhaps you kissed, or gestured, or looked.' And in al-Asl: 'He should say to him: Perhaps you married her or stoned her due to shubha.' And the purpose is to remind him with what would be a preventative mention so that he may remember it, whatever it may be, just as the Prophet said to the thief who was brought to him: 'Did you steal? And I do not think he stole' — i.e., I do not suppose he stole — as a reminder for him to recant. And from this it is known that if the adulterer claims that she is his wife, the hadd (penalty) is dropped from him, even if she is the wife of another, and he is not required to bring proof because of shubha, just as if the thief claims that the item is his property, the amputation is dropped by his mere claim. And in al-Muhit: If he marries the woman with whom he committed zina or buys her, the hadd does not fall in the apparent narration because he has no shubha at the time of the act.
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn phrase 'واندب تلقينه' (and it is recommended to remind him). The author explains that the imam or judge should gently remind the person who has confessed to zina, by suggesting possible excuses such as 'Perhaps you kissed her, or touched her, or committed zina under shubha (mistaken belief)'. This is based on the Prophetic example with Ma'iz, where the Prophet asked him similar questions to give him a chance to retract. The wisdom is that the punishment should be averted as much as possible, in line with the principle of 'dar' al-hudud' (averting penalties with doubts). The passage then derives a general rule: if the person claims that he thought the woman was his wife (or his slave), the hadd falls based on that claim alone, without requiring evidence, because it creates a shubha. However, if he marries her after the act, it does not help, as the shubha must exist at the time of the act.

Key Terms
تلقين (talgīn): Reminding the confessor of possible excuses to encourage retraction, thereby averting the hadd.
شبهة (shubha): A doubt or mistaken belief that nullifies the hadd penalty.
درء الحدود (dar' al-hudūd): The principle of averting hudud penalties by any genuine doubt or excuse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the effect if an adulterer claims that the woman was his wife at the time of the act, even if she is actually the wife of another?
A) The hadd is still applied because he should have known better.
B) The hadd is dropped because the claim creates a shubha.
C) The hadd is dropped only if he can prove she is his wife.
D) The hadd is not dropped, but the imam may reduce it.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a judge should remind a confessor of excuses to avert the hadd, and a claim of shubha at the time of the act drops the punishment without evidence.

Ruling on Stoning the Muhsan and Its Proof
Commentary on the ruling that the muhsan adulterer is stoned to death in an open space

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the proof for rajm of the muhsan adulterer and explain why the Khawarij denial is invalid based on tawatur and ijma.

Core Idea
Rajm for muhsan is wajib by Sunnah and ijma; Khawarij denial is invalid because rajm is mutawatir in meaning.

Stoning for the married adulterer is a well-known ruling in Islam, but its proof is not explicitly in the Quran. This lesson examines the evidence: the Prophet's stoning of Ma'iz, the consensus of the Companions, and the refutation of those who deny this punishment. You will learn how the Hanafi school defends this ruling and why objections based on rejecting ahad reports or ijma are unfounded.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is stoning (rajm) of a muhsan (free, adult, married person who has had intercourse) for zina. The ruling is that it is wajib upon conviction by proper testimony or confession.
The text specifies 'in an open space' (fi fada').
2
Locate the primary dalil
The primary proof is the Prophet's action and statement in the case of Ma'iz, who was muhsan and was stoned. This is recorded in Bukhari and Muslim.
The hadith is cited in the source.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit action of the Prophet (stoning) and his statement 'and committed zina after ihsan' show that stoning is the prescribed punishment for the muhsan. This constitutes a binding Sunnah.
The text also invokes ijma of the Companions as additional evidence.
4
Analyze the refutation of Khawarij denial
The Khawarij reject rajm. The author argues that if they reject ijma, that is ignorance; if they reject ahad reports, rajm is actually established by tawatur (mass transmission) in meaning, even if details come from ahad.
This highlights the Hanafi principle of tawatur ma'nawi.
5
Note the practical detail on location
Stoning is to be performed in an open space (like the musalla) based on the practice with Ma'iz. Also, killing the condemned before the order is a crime; after the order, no liability.
This incidental ruling is from the commentary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (فإن كان محصناً رجمه في فضاء حتى يموت لأنه عليه السلام رجم ماعزاً وقد كان أحصن وقال في الحديث المعروف وزناً بعد إحصان». وعلى هذا إجماع الصحابة. وإنكار الخوارج الرجم باطل لأنهم إن أنكروا حجية إجماع الصحابة فجهل مركب بالدليل بل هو إجماع قطعي، وإن أنكروا وقوعه من رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم الإنكارهم حجية خبر الواحد فهو بعد بطلانه بالدليل ليس مما نحن فيه لأن ثبوت الرجم عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم متواتر المعنى كشجاعة علي وجود حاتم، والآحاد في تفاصيل صوره وخصوصياته؛ كذا في فتح القدير . وإنما يرجم في الفضاء لحديث البخاري أن ماعزا رجم بالمصلى وفي مسلم: فانطلقنا به إلى بقيع الغرقد فإن المصلي كان به وهو مصلي الجنائة في الحيط : المقضى برج إذا قتله انسان أو فقأ عينه لا شيء عليه ولو قتله قبل القضاء يحب القصاص إن كان عمداً والدية إن كان خطأ
His statement: (Then if he is muhsan, he is stoned in an open space until death) because the Prophet stoned Ma'iz and he was muhsan, and said in the well-known hadith 'and committed zina after ihsan (marriage).' And upon this is the ijma of the Companions. And the denial of the Khawarij of rajm is invalid because if they deny the authority of ijma of the Companions, it is compounded ignorance contrary to evidence; rather it is definitive ijma. And if they deny its occurrence from the Messenger of Allah, their denial of the authority of khabar al-wahid — it is after its invalidity by evidence not part of our discussion, because the establishment of rajm from the Messenger of Allah is mutawatir in meaning like the bravery of Ali and the generosity of Hatim, while the ahad reports are in the details of its forms and specifics; as in Fath al-Qadir. And he is only stoned in an open space due to the hadith of Bukhari that Ma'iz was stoned in the musalla, and in Muslim: 'So we set out with him to Baqi' al-Gharqad' because the musalla was there, and it was the place of funeral prayer. (Commentary): 'The one ordered to be stoned if a person kills him or gouges out his eye, there is nothing upon him, and if he kills him before the order, qisas is required if intentional, and diyah if accidental.'
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn phrase 'فإن كان محصناً رجمه في فضاء حتى يموت' (if he is muhsan, he is stoned in an open space until death). The author provides the proof: the Prophet stoned Ma'iz, who was muhsan (married), and this is established by authentic hadith. Moreover, it is a matter of consensus (ijma) of the Companions. The author refutes the Khawarij who deny rajm, arguing that their rejection is based either on denying the authority of ijma or on denying the reliability of ahad reports, but the fact of rajm is established by tawatur (mass transmission) in meaning, even if details are from ahad reports. The location of stoning should be an open space, based on the practice of the Prophet with Ma'iz at the musalla (prayer ground). An incidental ruling is added: if someone kills the condemned person before the execution order, it is murder requiring qisas; after the order, it is not penalized.

Key Terms
محصن (muhsan): A person who has had valid sexual intercourse in marriage (free and adult).
رجم (rajm): Stoning to death as punishment for zina committed by a muhsan.
إجماع الصحابة (ijma' al-sahabah): Consensus of the Companions of the Prophet, considered a definitive proof.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because all Companions practiced rajm without dispute.
D) Because the Khawarij are not qualified to interpret the Shari'ah.

Key Takeaway
Rajm for the muhsan is wajib by Sunnah and ijma; denial based on rejection of ahad reports is refuted by tawatur ma'nawi.
