Condition of Witnesses Starting the Stoning and Consequences of Refusal
Commentary on the requirement that witnesses initiate stoning and what happens if they refuse or are unable

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi condition for executing rajm (witnesses must start stoning) and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument based on qiyas.

Core Idea
Witnesses must throw the first stone—a condition that allows retraction and averts the hadd.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses a unique Hanafi condition for the punishment of stoning: the four witnesses must physically begin the stoning. This condition, rooted in a narration from Ali and the principle of dar' al-hudud bi al-shubhat, is a point of ikhtilaf with the Shafi'i school. Understanding this dispute reveals how procedural safeguards shape criminal law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi condition
The text states that witnesses must begin stoning even with a small pebble. This is based on a narration from Ali and the wisdom of allowing retraction.
This condition is for rajm only.
2
Understand the Shafi'i objection
Al-Shafi'i rejects the condition, analogizing to flogging where witnesses do not start.
Qiyas to jald is the basis.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The text argues flogging is not analogous because untrained floggers may cause accidental death, while stoning is intentionally lethal. The condition serves to avert punishment.
This reflects the maxim dar' al-hudud bi al-shubhat.
4
Examine consequences of refusal or incapacity
If witnesses refuse, die, go absent, or lose capacity (apostasy, blindness, etc.), the hadd falls because the condition is lost. Refusal is treated as an indication of retraction.
Even if only some witnesses become unable, the hadd drops.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf holds that rajm is carried out even if witnesses do not begin; the Imam and people proceed. However, the mufta bihi is the condition's effectiveness.
This shows even within the school there is debate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (يبدأ الشهود به أي بالرجم يعني على وجه الشرط ولو بحصاة صغيرة، هكذا روي عن علي رضي الله عنه، ولأن الشاهد قد يتجاسر على الأداء ثم يستعظم المباشرة فيرجع فكان في بدايته احتيال للدرء وقال الشافعي : لا يشترط بدايتهم اعتباراً بالجلد. قلنا : كل أحد لا يحسن الجلد فربما يقع مهلكاً والإهلاك غير مستحق ولا كذلك الرجم إتلاف قوله : (فإن أبو اسقط أي إن امتنع الشهود من الابتداء سقط الحد لأنه دلالة الرجوع، وكذا إذا ماتوا أو غابوا في ظاهر الرواية لفوات الشرط. ولا يجب الحد عليهم لو امتنعوا لأنه دلالة الرجوع لا صريحه وامتناع البعض أو غيبته كالكل، وكذا إذا خرج بعض الشهود عن الأهلية بارتداد أو عمى أو خرس أو فسق أو قذف سواء كان قبل القضاء أو بعده، لأن في الحدود، وأما قطع اليدين فإن كان بعد الشهادة امتنعت الإقامة، وإن القضاء الإمضاء من لأنه امرأته إلى الآن بخلاف قوله حسبتها امرأتي فإنه يفيد أنه الآن مقر بأنها ليست امرأته وإنما ظنها وقت الفعل فليتأمل. ثم رأيت في التتارخانية عن شرح الطحاوي : لو شهد عليه أربعة بالزنا ثم ادعى شبهة فقال ظننت أنها امرأتي لا يسقط الحد، ولو قال هي امرأتي أو أمتي لا حد عليه ولا على الشهود
الرجم من من كان منهم ذا عند وقد كان القطع قبلها رمى القاضي بحضرتهم لأنهم إذا كانوا مقطوعي الأيدي لم تستحق البداءة بهم، وإن قطعوا بعدها فقد استحقت وهذا يفيد أن كون الابتداء شرطاً إنما هو بهم قدرتهم على الرجم وفي الظهيرية وإن كان الشهود مرضى لا يستطيعون الرمي حضروا رمي القاضي ثم رمي الناس. وقال أبو يوسف : يقام عليه الرجم وإن لم يحضر الشهود وإن حضروا ولم يرجموا رجم الإمام ثم الناس. وقيد المصنف بالرجم لأن ما سوى الحدود لا يجب الابتداء لا من الشهود ولا من الإمام وكذا في الظهيرية
His statement: (The witnesses begin with him) meaning with the stoning, that is, as a condition, even with a small pebble. This is narrated from Ali, and because the witness may be bold in testifying but then find the direct action great and retract, so in his beginning there is a stratagem for averting (the hadd). Al-Shafi'i said: Their beginning is not a condition, analogizing to flogging. We said: Not everyone knows how to flog, so it may become lethal and killing is not deserved, unlike stoning which is destruction. His statement: (If they refuse, it falls) meaning if the witnesses refrain from beginning, the hadd falls because it is an indication of retraction. Likewise if they die or are absent, in the apparent narration, because the condition is lost. The hadd is not obligatory upon them if they refrain, because it is an indication of retraction, not explicit. The refusal or absence of some is like all. Likewise if some witnesses lose capacity due to apostasy, blindness, muteness, transgression, or qadhf (false accusation), whether before judgment or after, because in hudud... And as for cutting off hands, if it is after testimony, enforcement is prevented. And if the judgment is executed from... because she is his wife until now, unlike his statement 'I thought she was my wife' because it indicates that now he admits she is not his wife, but he thought so at the time of the act, so consider. Then I saw in al-Tatarkhaniyya from Sharh al-Tahawi: If four testify against him for zina, then he claims shubha saying 'I thought she was my wife', the hadd does not fall; but if he says 'she is my wife' or 'my slave', no hadd upon him nor upon the witnesses. (Page 14) The stoning from whoever among them had... and if the amputation was before, the judge throws in their presence, because if they have amputated hands, they do not deserve to begin; but if amputated after, they have deserved it. This indicates that the condition of beginning is only with their ability to stone. And in al-Zahiriyya: If the witnesses are sick and unable to throw, they attend, the judge throws, then the people. Abu Yusuf said: The stoning is carried out even if the witnesses are not present, and if they are present but do not stone, the Imam stones then the people. The author restricted (the condition) to stoning because in other hadd punishments, beginning is not required from witnesses nor from Imam, and likewise in al-Zahiriyya.
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn phrases 'يبدأ الشهود به' (the witnesses begin with him) and 'فإن أبو اسقط' (if they refuse, it falls). The author explains that it is a condition (shart) for the execution of rajm that the four witnesses themselves initiate the stoning by throwing the first stones, even if they are small pebbles. This is based on a narration from Ali and the wisdom that a witness may be bold in testifying but then hesitate when it comes to actual killing; by requiring them to begin, it gives them a chance to retract, thus averting the hadd. Al-Shafi'i disagrees, analogizing to flogging (jald) where the witnesses do not have to start. The Hanafi response is that flogging is less severe and untrained floggers might kill accidentally, whereas stoning is intended to kill, so the analogy is imperfect. If the witnesses refuse to stone, the hadd falls because it indicates they may have retracted their testimony. This applies even if they die, go absent, or lose capacity (apostasy, blindness, muteness, transgression, qadhf). The same applies if only some of the witnesses become unable. For amputation (cutting of hands), the condition applies similarly: if the witnesses have missing hands, they are not required to begin. If they are sick but able to attend, they can be present while others stone. Abu Yusuf holds a different view: rajm is carried out even if the witnesses are absent or do not stone, and the Imam and people proceed. The condition is specifically for rajm, not other hudud.

Key Terms
شرط (shart): A condition; here, the act of witnesses beginning to stone is a condition for enforcing the hadd of rajm.
درء الحدود بالشبهات (dar' al-hudud bi al-shubuhāt): The principle of averting hadd punishments by any doubt; here, the condition serves to create a chance for retraction.
دلالة الرجوع (dalalat al-ruju'): An indication of retraction of testimony; refusal to stone is treated as such.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens in Hanafi fiqh if the witnesses refuse to begin the stoning?
A) The hadd is implemented by the Imam and the people anyway.
B) The hadd is dropped because their refusal indicates possible retraction.
C) The witnesses are punished for refusing.
D) The hadd is postponed until they agree.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires the witnesses of zina to personally start the stoning, and their refusal or inability drops the hadd, embodying the principle of averting punishment.

Order of Stoning and Ruling for Close Relatives
Commentary on the order of stoning and the ruling for close relatives

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the order of stoning in Hanafi fiqh (witnesses, Imam, people) and distinguish the ruling for close relatives regarding participation and intent.

Core Idea
A close relative may stone but must not aim to kill; the hadd is valid even if they do, but it is disliked.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the procedure of stoning for zina. It addresses two key issues: the sequence of stoners (witnesses, Imam, then people) and the special rule for close relatives. Understanding these details ensures correct application of hadd without violating the spirit of mercy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prescribed order of stoning
From the narration of Ali, when hadd is proven by testimony, the witnesses begin, then the Imam, then the people. When proven by confession, the Imam begins, then the people.
This order is sunnah, not wajib.
2
Analyze the ruling for close relatives (mahram)
The text presents two views: (1) mahram may stone but should not intend to kill; (2) mahram should not stone at all. The author leans toward the first, with karaha tanzihiyya.
The difference stems from whether the mahram's participation is necessary.
3
Apply the dalil from the Ghāmidiyyah
The Prophet's stoning of the Ghāmidiyyah woman after her confession establishes that the Imam begins, then the people. This hadith is zanni in both thubut and dalala.
The hadith supports the order for confession cases.
4
Note the condition for stoning without witnessing testimony
If the qadi is a just jurist (adil faqih), the people may stone even if they did not witness the testimony. Otherwise, they must witness it themselves.
This protects against unjust execution.
5
Evaluate the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on mahram stoning
Some Hanafi sources (al-Muhit) forbid mahram from executing the hadd entirely, while others (al-Tabyin) allow it with the condition of not aiming to kill. The mufta bihi is the latter.
The hadd is valid in both cases, but the intent affects the sin.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ثم الإمام ثم الناس هكذا روي عن علي رضي الله عنه وأرضاه . ويقصدون بذلك مقتله إلا رحم محرم منه فإنه لا يقصد مقتله فإن بغيره كفاية كذا في التبيين وغيره. وظاهره أنه يرجمه ولا يقصد مقتله مع أن ظاهر ما في المحيط أنه لا يرجمه أصلاً فإنه قال : ويكره لذي الرحم المحرم أن يلي إقامة الحد والرجم ا هـ . ولم يذكر المصنف أن الإمام إذا امتنع من الرجم بعد الشهود أنه يسقط الحد وقياسه السقوط . قال في فتح القدير : واعلم أن مقتضى ما ذكر أنه لو بدأ الشهود فيما إذا ثبت بالشهادة يجب أن يثني الإمام فلو لم يثن الإمام يسقط الحد لاتحاد المأخذ فيهما .اهـ. وفي الظهيرية والقاضي إذا أمر الناس برجم الزاني وسعهم أن يرجموه وإن لم يعاينوا أداء الشهادة. وروى ابن سماعة عن محمد أنه قال : هذا إذا كان القاضي فقيهاً عدلاً، أما إذا كان فقيهاً غير عدل أو كان عدلاً غير فقيه فلا يسعهم يرجموه حتى يعاينوا أداء الشهادة اهـ.
أن قوله : (ويبدأ الإمام لو مقراً ثم الناس كذا روي عن علي رضي الله عنه ورمى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم الغامدية بحصاة مثل الحمصة وكانت قد اعترفت بالزنا، ولم يذكر المصنف أن الإمام لو لم يبدأ هل يحل للناس الرمي. قال في فتح القدير واعلم أن مقتضى هذا أنه لو
:
اهـ. قوله : (فإنه قال ويكره لذي الرحم المحرم (الخ الظاهر أن الكراهة تنزيهية ثم إن محل كراهة رجمه مطلقاً إذا لم يكن المحرم شاهداً. قال في الجوهرة: وإن شهد أربعة على أبيهم بالزنا وجب عليهم أن يبتدؤا بالرجم وكذا الأخوة وذوو الرحم، ويستحب أن لا يتعمدوا مقتلاً، وكذا ذوو الرحم المحرم. وأما ابن العم فلا بأس أن يتعمد قتله لأن رحمه لم يكمل فأشبه الأجنبي وقد قالوا إن الابن إذا شهد على أبيه بالزنا لم يحرم الميراث بهذه الشهادة لأن الميراث يجب بالموت والشهادة إنما وقعت على الزنا وذلك غير الموت، وكذا إذا شهد عليه بالقصاص فقتل لم يحرم الميراث لهذه العلة قوله : (فلو لم يثن الإمام سقط الحد) نقل في النهر عن إيضاح الإصلاح أن حضوره غير لازم ثم قال : إن ما في الفتح إنما يتم لو سلم وجوب حضوره كالشهود قال : وفي الدراية ويستحب للإمام أن يأمر طائفة من المسلمين أن يحضروا لإقامة الحدود. واختلفوا في عددها فعن ابن عباس واحد، وقال عطاء اثنان، والزهري ثلاثة، والحسن البصري عشرة .اهـ. وهذا صريح في أن حضورهم ليس شرطاً فرميهم
His statement: (Then the Imam, then the people) is thus narrated from Ali. And they aim thereby to kill him, except for a close relative (dhī rahm mahram) who should not aim to kill him, because someone else suffices. As in al-Tabyīn and others. And the apparent meaning is that he stones him but does not intend his death, although the apparent meaning in al-Muhīt is that he does not stone him at all, for he said: 'It is disliked for a close relative to undertake the execution of hadd and stoning.' And the author did not mention that if the Imam refrains from stoning after the witnesses, the hadd falls, but analogically it should fall. In Fath al-Qadir: 'Know that the consequence of what was mentioned is that if the witnesses began when it is proven by testimony, the Imam must follow; if he does not, the hadd falls because the basis is the same.' In al-Zahiriyya: If the qadi orders the people to stone the adulterer, it is permissible for them to stone even if they did not witness the testimony. Ibn Sama'a narrated from Muhammad that he said: 'This is when the qadi is a just jurist; but if he is a jurist but not just, or just but not a jurist, it is not permissible for them to stone until they witness the testimony.' His statement: (And the Imam begins if he is confessing, then the people) is thus narrated from Ali, and the Messenger of Allah stoned the Ghāmidiyyah woman with a pebble like a chickpea, and she had confessed to zina. The author did not mention that if the Imam does not begin, whether it is permissible for the people to stone. In Fath al-Qadir: 'Know that the consequence of this is that if...' His statement: (For he said: It is disliked for a close relative...) The apparent meaning is that the dislike is tanzīhī (reprehensible but not sinful). Then the place of dislike of his stoning absolutely is when the relative is not a witness. In al-Jawhara: If four testify against their father for zina, they must begin the stoning, likewise brothers and close relatives, and it is recommended that they do not intentionally kill. And for the cousin, there is no harm in intentionally killing him because his relationship is not complete, so he resembles a stranger. And they said: If the son testifies against his father for zina, he is not deprived of inheritance by this testimony, because inheritance is due upon death, and the testimony is only about zina which is not death. Similarly, if he testifies against him for qisas and he is killed, he is not deprived of inheritance for this reason. His statement: (If the Imam does not follow, the hadd falls) is transmitted in al-Nahr from Idah al-Islah that his presence is not necessary. Then he said: What is in Fath al-Qadir only holds if his presence is obligatory like the witnesses. In al-Diraya: It is recommended for the Imam to order a group of Muslims to attend for the execution of the hadd. They differed on its number: from Ibn Abbas: one, from Ata': two, from al-Zuhri: three, from Hasan al-Basri: ten. This clearly indicates that their presence is not a condition, so their stoning (is valid).
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on the procedure of stoning. After the witnesses begin, the Imam then stones, followed by the people. This is from a narration of Ali. The text addresses a key point: close relatives (mahram such as father, son, brother) should not aim to kill the offender, but may still stone without intending death. There is a difference: in al-Muhit, it is disliked (makruh) for a mahram to undertake the hadd execution entirely. The author notes that if the Imam refrains after the witnesses, the hadd should fall analogically, but this is not explicit. The passage also discusses the case of a confessing offender: the Imam begins, then the people, as with the Ghāmidiyyah woman. There is a condition for people to stone without seeing testimony: if the qadi is a just jurist, they can obey; otherwise they must witness the testimony themselves. Regarding close relatives who are witnesses (e.g., sons testifying against father), they must begin the stoning, but it is recommended they do not intend to kill. This does not affect inheritance. Finally, the presence of a group for stoning is recommended but not a condition; the number varies among the Salaf.

Key Terms
رحم محرم (rahm mahram): A close blood relative within the prohibited degrees of marriage (e.g., father, son, brother).
مقر (muqirr): Someone who confesses; here, the offender who admits to zina without witnesses.
كراهة تنزيهية (karaha tanzihiyya): A disliked but not sinful action; here, for a mahram to execute the hadd.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling regarding a son who testified against his father for zina?
A) He should not participate in the stoning.
B) He must begin the stoning but should not intentionally kill his father.
C) He is disqualified from testifying.
D) He inherits despite the testimony.

Key Takeaway
The order of stoning is sunnah, and close relatives may participate but must avoid intentionally killing the offender.

Hudud — Fixed Penalties
intermediate
10 min
Initiation of Stoning: Witnesses, Imam, and the Condition of Ibtida'
Intra-Hanafi dispute on stoning initiation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the initiation roles of witnesses (shahada) and Imam (iqrar) in stoning and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether initiation is a condition for the hadd.

Core Idea
Initiation of stoning by witnesses is a condition for hadd validity; without it, the punishment falls.

In Hanafi law, the procedure for the stoning punishment (rajm) for the muhsan fornicator follows a specific order, but the sequence differs depending on how the zina is proven. This passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqaiq unpacks the ruling from the matn, addressing who must throw the first stone and whether that initiation is an indispensable condition. It also presents an important internal debate within the Hanafi school between Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad on one side, and Imam Abu Yusuf on the other.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two modes of proof
The ruling on who initiates stoning depends on whether the zina is proven by testimony (shahada) or by confession (iqrar). Determine which mode each part of the passage addresses.
Shahada: witnesses begin; Iqrar: Imam begins.
2
State the majority Hanafi position on initiation
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani, when zina is proven by four witnesses, those witnesses must initiate the stoning. If they refuse or cannot, the hadd is not carried out.
The passage cites a narration from Ali (RA) and the practice of the Prophet with al-Ghamidiyyah.
3
Understand the opposing view of Abu Yusuf
Abu Yusuf holds that the stoning proceeds even if the witnesses do not initiate; the Imam or the people may start.
His dalil is that the hadd is established and should not be suspended due to witnesses' refusal.
4
Examine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
Under the majority view, if witnesses refuse to stone, the punishment is waived. Under Abu Yusuf's view, it is still carried out by others.
This has implications for the enforcement of hudud.
5
Identify the mufta bihi (operative position)
The text and later authorities (e.g., Fath al-Qadir) confirm that the majority view requiring initiation is relied upon for fatwa.
Thus, a mufti today would require witnesses to begin, or else the hadd is not enforced.

Source Text

كتاب الحدود ثم الإمام ثم الناس ويبدأ الإمام به لو مقراً ثم الناس ولو غير محصن جلده مائة الرجم من كان منهم ذا عند وقد كان القطع قبلها رمى القاضي بحضرتهم لأنهم إذا كانوا مقطوعي الأيدي لم تستحق البداءة وروى ابن سماعة عن محمد أنه قال : هذا إذا كان القاضي فقيهاً عدلاً، أما إذا كان فقيهاً غير عدل أو كان عدلاً غير فقيه فلا يسعهم يرجموه حتى يعاينوا أداء الشهادة اهـ. أن قوله : (ويبدأ الإمام لو مقراً ثم أن مقتضى هذا أنه لو : اهـ. قوله : (فإنه قال ويكره لذي الرحم المحرم (الخ الظاهر أن الكراهة تنزيهية ثم إن محل كراهة رجمه مطلقاً إذا لم يكن المحرم شاهداً. قال في الجوهرة: وإن شهد أربعة على أبيهم بالزنا وجب عليهم أن يبتدؤا بالرجم وكذا الأخوة وذوو الرحم، ويستحب أن لا يتعمدوا مقتلاً، وكذا ذوو الرحم المحرم. وأما ابن العم فلا بأس أن يتعمد قتله لأن رحمه لم يكمل فأشبه الأجنبي وقد قالوا إن الابن إذا شهد على أبيه بالزنا لم يحرم الميراث بهذه الشهادة لأن الميراث يجب بالموت والشهادة إنما وقعت على الزنا وذلك غير الموت، وكذا إذا شهد عليه بالقصاص فقتل لم يحرم الميراث لهذه العلة قوله : (فلو لم يثن الإمام سقط واختلفوا في عددها فعن ابن عباس واحد، وقال عطاء اثنان، والزهري ثلاثة، والحسن البصري عشرة .اهـ. وهذا صريح في أن حضورهم ليس شرطاً فرميهم امتنع الإمام لا يحل للقوم رجمه ولو أمرهم لعلمهم بفوات شرط الرجم وهو منتف برجم ماعز فإن القطع بأنه عليه السلام لم يحضره بل رجمه الناس بأمره عليه السلام. ويمكن الجواب بأن حقيقة ما دل عليه قول علي رضي الله عنه أنه يجب على الإمام أن يأمرهم بالابتداء اختياراً لثبوت دلالة الرجوع ،وعدمه وأن يبتدئ هو في الإقرار لينكشف للناس أنه لم يقصر في أمر القضاء بأن لم يتساهل في بعض شروط القضاء بالحد، فإذا امتنع حينئذ ظهرت أمارة الرجوع. وفي الحاوي: وينبغي للناس أن يصفوا عند الرجم كصفوف الصلاة وكلما رجم تأخروا وتقدم غيرهم فرجموا اهـ
Book of Hudud: Then the Imam, then the people. And the Imam begins if [the person] is a confessor, then the people. And if he is not muhsan, he is flogged one hundred [lashes]. The stoning is from those who have [attended]? And the cutting before it: the judge throws in their presence because if they are without hands, they do not deserve to begin with them; if they are cut after, it is deserved. This indicates that the condition of initiation is only with their ability to stone. In al-Zahiriya: if the witnesses are sick and cannot throw, the judge throws, then the people. Abu Yusuf said: The stoning is established even if the witnesses do not attend; if they attend and do not stone, the Imam stones then the people. The author restricted to stoning because other than hudud do not require initiation from witnesses nor from Imam. Similarly in al-Zahiriya. He said: (Then the Imam, then the people) – thus narrated from Ali (رضي الله عنه). They intend by that his killing except a mahram relative, he does not intend his killing. If others suffice, as in al-Tabyin etc. Its apparent meaning is that he stones him and does not intend his death, while what is in al-Muhit says he does not stone at all; he said: It is disliked for a mahram relative to carry out the hadd and stoning. The author did not mention that if the Imam refrains from stoning after the witnesses, the hadd falls; by analogy it falls. In Fath al-Qadir: Know that the implication of what was mentioned is that if the witnesses begin in a case established by testimony, the Imam must second, and if the Imam does not second, the hadd falls because the same basis applies. In al-Zahiriya: If the judge orders the people to stone the fornicator, they may stone even if they did not witness the testimony. Ibn Sama'ah narrated from Muhammad that he said: This is if the judge is a jurist and just; but if he is a jurist but unjust, or just but not a jurist, they may not stone until they witness the testimony. He said: (And the Imam begins if [the person] is a confessor, then the people) – thus narrated from Ali (رضي الله عنه). The Messenger of Allah (صلى الله عليه وسلم) threw at al-Ghamidiyyah a pebble like a chickpea, and she had confessed to zina. The author did not mention whether if the Imam does not begin, it is permissible for the people to stone. In Fath al-Qadir: Know that the implication of this is that if he does not... He said: (For he said: It is disliked for a mahram relative...) – apparently the karahah is tanzihiyyah. Then the place of dislike of his stoning absolutely if the relative is not a witness. In al-Jawharah: If four testify against their father for zina, it is obligatory for them to begin stoning; likewise brothers and relatives. It is recommended that they do not intentionally kill him; likewise mahram relatives. As for a cousin, there is no harm if he intentionally kills him because his kinship is not complete, so he is like a stranger. They said: If a son testifies against his father for zina, he does not lose inheritance due to this testimony because inheritance depends on death, and the testimony is about zina, not death. Likewise if he testifies against him for qisas and he is killed, he does not lose inheritance for this reason. He said: (If the Imam does not second, the hadd falls.) It is narrated in al-Nahr from Idah al-Islah that his presence is not necessary. Then he said: What is in al-Fath is only valid if his presence is obligatory like the witnesses. He said: In al-Dirayah, it is recommended for the Imam to order a group of Muslims to attend for the establishment of hudud. They differed on its number: from Ibn Abbas: one, Ata: two, al-Zuhri: three, al-Hasan al-Basri: ten. This is explicit that their presence is not a condition, so their stoning if the Imam refrains, it is not lawful for the people to stone him, even if he orders them, because they know that the condition of stoning is missing. That is negated by the stoning of Ma'iz, for it is certain that the Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم) did not attend but the people stoned him by his order. The answer is that the truth indicated by Ali's statement is that the Imam must order them to begin by choice, to confirm the indication of retraction and its absence, and he should begin in the case of confession to reveal to the people that he did not neglect in the matter of judgment, not being careless in some conditions of judgment by hadd. So if he refrains, then a sign of retraction appears. In al-Hawi: The people should line up at stoning like the rows of prayer, and whenever they throw, they step back and others come forward and throw.
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq regarding the procedure of stoning (rajm) for the hadd of zina. It begins by stating the general order: the Imam, then the people. However, when the zina is proven by testimony (shahada), the witnesses should initiate the stoning. The commentator explains that if the witnesses have been maimed (hands cut off) before the stoning, they do not have the ability to throw stones, so they are not expected to begin; but if the cutting occurs after they have thrown, it is permissible. The condition of initiation is only with their ability to stone. A ruling from al-Zahiriya is cited: if the witnesses are sick and cannot throw, the judge throws first, then the people. Then the view of Abu Yusuf is presented: he holds that the stoning is carried out even if the witnesses do not attend; if they attend but do not throw, the Imam throws first then the people. The author restricted this ruling to stoning because for other hadd punishments, initiation by witnesses or Imam is not required. The commentary then discusses the narration from Ali that the order is Imam then people, but with the nuance that the stoner should not intentionally aim for a lethal spot unless the stoner is not a mahram relative. There is a difference: some sources say a mahram relative should not stone at all, while others say it is only disliked. The issue of whether the Imam's participation is a condition is debated: if the Imam refrains after the witnesses have started, the hadd falls by analogy. Fath al-Qadir affirms this. However, other scholars like the author of al-Nahr hold that the Imam's presence is not a condition. A narration from Ibn Sama'ah adds a condition: if the judge is knowledgeable and just, the people may stone without witnessing the testimony; otherwise, they must witness it. The passage also covers the case of iqrar (confession): the Imam must begin, and then the people. The example of al-Ghamidiyyah is cited, where the Prophet himself threw a small pebble. If the Imam does not begin, is it permissible for the people? The text mentions that according to Fath al-Qadir, the implication is that it is not permissible because the condition is missing. However, the case of Ma'iz is cited where the Prophet did not attend but the people stoned by his order, so the condition is not absolute; rather, the Imam's initiation is to indicate that he has not neglected his duty. The passage concludes with a recommendation from al-Hawi that the people should line up in rows like prayer and take turns throwing. Throughout, the madhhab maintains that the order is a recommended condition for the validity of stoning, but if all responsible parties fulfill their roles, the hadd is carried out.

Key Terms
الرجم (al-rajm): Stoning to death as the hadd punishment for muhsan fornicators.
الابتداء (al-ibtida'): The initiation of throwing the first stones at the convict, performed by witnesses or Imam before the general public.
المقرّ (al-muqirr): A person who confesses (iqrar) to zina, in which case the Imam begins the stoning.
المحصن (al-muhsan): A person who is free, adult, Muslim, and has had valid consummated marriage; their zina punishment is stoning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If zina is proven by the testimony of four witnesses, who should initiate the stoning according to the relied-upon Hanafi position?
A) The Imam
B) The witnesses
C) Any adult Muslim
D) The judge first, then the people

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position requires witnesses to initiate stoning in shahada cases; if they refuse, the hadd falls, but Abu Yusuf dissents.

Hudud — Fixed Penalties
beginner
6 min
Hadd of Flogging for the Unmarried Fornicator
Establishes flogging for ghayr muhsan from Quran and its abrogation for muhsan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Quranic basis for flogging the ghayr muhsan fornicator and explain how the ruling is abrogated for the muhsan via mutawatir sunna in Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
The 100-lash flogging is qat'i for ghayr muhsan; abrogated only for muhsan by stoning sunna.

This lesson examines the foundational text for the hadd of zina for the unmarried offender. The Quranic verse from Surah al-Nur commands flogging, yet this punishment is not universal—it applies only to those who are not muhsan. Understanding the abrogation mechanism (naskh) is key to correctly applying the hudud in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage rules on flogging for the ghayr muhsan fornicator. State the punishment and the category of person it applies to.
Ghayr muhsan means not meeting conditions of ihsan (free, adult, Muslim, valid consummated marriage).
2
Locate the primary dalil
The Quranic verse (24:2) is cited as the direct proof. Note that it commands flogging of 100 lashes.
The imperative 'fajlidu' indicates obligation (wujub) in Hanafi usul.
3
Trace the naskh (abrogation) operation
The passage explains that this verse is abrogated for the muhsan by the mutawatir sunna of the Prophet's stoning. Identify the abrogating evidence.
Hanafi school accepts that a qat'i sunna can abrogate a Quranic verse.
4
Determine the remaining operative scope
Since the abrogation is specific to muhsan, the verse continues to apply to ghayr muhsan. Confirm that the ruling is not completely repealed.
Common error: thinking the verse is entirely abrogated.
5
Note the usul principle demonstrated
This is a case of naskh al-Quran bi al-sunnah al-mutawatirah. Recognize the principle and its acceptance in Hanafi usul.
This principle is accepted because the sunna is qat'i in transmission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ولو غير محصن جلده مائة) لقوله تعالى الزانية والزاني فاجلدوا كل واحد منهما مائة جلدة [النور: ۲] إلا أنه انتسخ في حق المحصن فبقي في حق غيره معمولاً به، ويكفينا في تعيين الناسخ القطع برجم النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فيكون من نسخ الكتاب بالسنة القطعية
He said: (And if he is not muhsan, flog him one hundred [lashes]) – due to the saying of Allah: 'The fornicatress and the fornicator, flog each one of them one hundred lashes' [Surah al-Nur: 2] except that it is abrogated (naskh) in the case of the muhsan, so it remains operative for others. It suffices for us in specifying the abrogating [text] the certain (qat'i) [practice] of the Prophet's stoning, so this is abrogation of the Book by a mutawatir sunna.
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. The author comments on the matn phrase 'and if he is not muhsan, flog him one hundred.' The primary dalil is the Quranic verse from Surah al-Nur (24:2) which commands flogging for both male and female fornicators. However, this ruling is abrogated (mansukh) for the muhsan fornicator, whose punishment is stoning to death. The abrogation is established by the mutawatir sunna (the consistent practice of the Prophet, peace be upon him, in stoning muhsan offenders). This is a case of naskh al-Quran bi al-sunnah al-mutawatirah, which is accepted in Hanafi usul because the sunna is qat'i in transmission. For the non-muhsan (ghayr muhsan), the original Quranic ruling remains operative: 100 lashes.

Key Terms
الغير محصن (al-ghayr muhsan): A person who does not meet the conditions of ihsan (free, adult, Muslim, valid consummated marriage); their hadd is 100 lashes.
النسخ (al-naskh): Abrogation of a legal ruling by a later revelation or sunna. Here, the flogging verse is abrogated for muhsan by the mutawatir sunna of stoning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) All fornicators
B) Non-muhsan fornicators
C) Muhsan fornicators
D) Slaves

Key Takeaway
The 100-lash flogging for zina is the hadd for ghayr muhsan, established by a definitive Quranic text that is abrogated via mutawatir sunna only for muhsan.

Flogging of Slaves: Ruling, Proof, and Procedure
Details the reduced flogging for slaves and the physical procedure of flogging

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a slave fornicator (50 lashes), identify the Quranic proof and the qiyas extension to male slaves, and explain the procedural requirements for flogging (whip, stripping, distribution).

Core Idea
A slave fornicator receives 50 lashes by qiyas from the Quranic half-punishment for slave women.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the Hanafi ruling on flogging slaves for zina. We will see how the Quranic verse for slave women is extended to male slaves via qiyas, and then examine the detailed procedure for carrying out the punishment — the type of whip, removal of clothes, and distribution of lashes. Understanding these rules is essential for implementing hadd punishments correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? What is the hukm (number of lashes)?
The act is zina by a slave; the ruling is 50 lashes.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof does the author cite? Identify the Quranic verse and its relevance.
Quran 4:25 specifies half punishment for slave women.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the dalil prove the ruling for male slaves? What is the legal link?
The illa is slavery; by qiyas, the half-punishment applies to male slaves as well.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Is there a difference of opinion within the Hanafi school? What is the counter-argument?
Some argued the verse includes males by predominance; the author rejects this on usul grounds.
5
Evaluate the method of flogging
What are the procedural requirements? What must be avoided?
Whip must be moderate, convict stripped except awrah, lashes distributed avoiding head/face/private parts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( ونصف للعبد) أي نصف جلد المائة للعبد الزاني فيجلد خمسين سوطاً لقوله تعالى فإن أتين بفاحشة فعليهن نصف ما على المحصنات من العذاب [النساء : ٢٥] والمراد به الجلد لأن الرجم لا يتنصف وإذا ثبت التنصيف في الإماء لوجود الرق ثبت في العبيد دلالة. وما في التبيين من أن العبيد دخلوا في اللفظ وأنث للتغليب مخالف لما في الأصول من أن الذكور لا تتبع الإناث حتى لو قال أمنوني على بناتي لا تدخل الذكور بخلاف أمنوني على بني عم الذكور والإناث . قوله : (بسوط لا تمرة له متوسطاً) أي لا عقدة له لأن علياً رضي الله عنه لما أراد أن يقيم الحد كسر تمرته والمتوسط بين المبرح وهو الجارح وغيره المؤلم لإفضاء الأول إلى الهلاك وخلو الثاني عن المقصود وهو الانزجار ؛ كذا في الهداية وحاصله أنه المؤلم غير الجارح قوله : ( ونزع ثيابه وفرق على بدنه إلا رأسه ووجهه وفرجه أي ونزع عنه ثيابه إلا ما يستر عورته لأن علياً رضي الله عنه كان يأمر بالتجريد في الحدود لأن التجريد أبلغ في إيصال الألم إليه، وهذا الحد مبناه على الشدة في الضرب، وفي نزع الإزار كشف العورة فيتوقاه. وإنما يفرق الضرب على أعضائه لأن الجمع في عضو واحد قد يفضي إلى التلف والحد زاجر لا متلف. وإنما يتقي الأعضاء الثلاثة لقوله عليه السلام للذي أمره بضرب الحد «اتق الوجه
He said: (And half for the slave) – meaning half of the hundred lashes for the slave fornicator, so he is flogged fifty lashes, due to His saying: 'But if they commit a lewdness, then on them half the punishment of free women' [Surah al-Nisa: 25]. By it is meant flogging because stoning cannot be halved. When half is established for slave women due to slavery, it is established for male slaves by implication. What is in al-Tabyin that male slaves are included in the wording and the feminine is used for predominance contradicts what is in the principles that males do not follow females; if one says 'give me protection for my daughters,' males do not enter, unlike 'give me protection for the sons of my uncle, males and females.' He said: (With a whip that has no node, moderate) – meaning no knot, because Ali (رضي الله عنه) when he wanted to execute the hadd, he broke its node. The moderate is between the severe (which wounds) and the painful (which does not); the first leads to destruction, the second lacks the purpose of deterrence. As in al-Hidayah. Its essence is that it is painful but not injurious. He said: (And remove his clothes and distribute [the lashes] over his body, except his head, face, and private parts) – meaning remove his clothes except what covers his private parts, because Ali (رضي الله عنه) used to order stripping in hudud because stripping is more effective in conveying pain. This hadd is based on severity in beating. And in removing the waist-wrapper is exposure of the private parts, so he avoids that. The lashes are distributed over his limbs because concentrating on one limb may lead to destruction, and the hadd is a deterrent, not a destroyer. The three parts are avoided because the Prophet said to the one he ordered to execute the hadd: 'Avoid the face.'
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage covers three rulings: (1) the flogging of slaves, (2) the description of the whip, and (3) the method of flogging. For the slave fornicator, his punishment is half that of a free person: 50 lashes. The proof is from Surah al-Nisa (4:25), which mentions half punishment for slave women. Since stoning cannot be halved, the half applies to flogging. The Hanafi position uses qiyas to extend this to male slaves, as the effective cause ('illa) is slavery. There is a contrary view in al-Tabyin that the verse's wording includes male slaves by predominance, but the author rejects this, citing the usul principle that masculine does not follow feminine in such contexts. For the whip, it must be moderate (not severe and not too light), without knots, so that it causes pain but does not wound. The narration of Ali breaking the node of his whip is cited. For the method, the convict's clothes are removed except those covering the private parts (awrah). The lashes are distributed over the body, avoiding the head, face, and private parts, to prevent killing or injury. This is based on the Prophet's instruction to 'avoid the face.' The aim is deterrence, not destruction.

Key Terms
التمرة (al-tamrah): The knot or node of a whip; the text says a whip 'la tamrata lahu' meaning no knot, to avoid causing injury.
المبرح (al-mubarrih): A severe beating that wounds or kills; contrasted with moderate beating that is painful but not injurious.
التجريد (al-tajrid): The act of stripping the convict's clothes (except covering the awrah) before flogging.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how many lashes does a male slave receive for zina?
A) 100
B) 25
C) 50
D) 80

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling for a slave fornicator is 50 lashes, derived by qiyas from the Quranic half-punishment for slave women, and must be executed with a moderate whip, stripping the convict, and distributing lashes while avoiding the face and private parts.

Flogging for Non-Muhsan and Slave: Proofs from Quran and Sunnah
Explanation of flogging ruling with Quranic proofs and rebuttal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on flogging for non-muhsan and slave fornicators, cite the Quranic verses, and explain the abrogation of the verse for muhsan.

Core Idea
The Quranic 100 lashes apply to non-muhsan only; slaves receive half; abrogation by definite sunnah.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on the hadd punishment for zina for non-muhsan free persons and slaves. The author of Kanz al-Daqaiq states the ruling, and the commentary provides the Quranic proofs and addresses an usul issue regarding the inclusion of male slaves.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is zina by a non-muhsan free person (unmarried, never consummated marriage) – ruling is 100 lashes. For a slave (male or female), the ruling is 50 lashes.
Non-muhsan here means free, adult, and not muhsan (i.e., no valid marriage consummated).
2
Locate the dalil for the non-muhsan
The primary evidence is Quran 24:2: 'The fornicatress and the fornicator, flog each one of them with a hundred lashes.' However, this verse is abrogated for the muhsan by the Prophet's stoning (definite sunnah).
Abrogation by mutawatir sunnah is valid in Hanafi usul.
3
Determine the abrogation mechanism
The verse remains operative for non-muhsan. The abrogator is the definite sunnah (the Prophet stoned Ma'iz and others), which has certain transmission and thus can abrogate a Quranic verse.
Hanafi school holds that sunnah can abrogate Quran if both are qat'i.
4
Find the dalil for the slave
Quran 4:25 for female slaves: 'their punishment is half of that prescribed for free women'. Since stoning cannot be halved, it must refer to flogging. This ruling is extended to male slaves by qiyas (implied analogy).
The halving is due to slavery, not gender.
5
Address the usul objection
Some (as in al-Tabyin) argued that male slaves are included by the feminine wording due to ghaleba (overwhelming majority). The Hanafi rebuttal: in usul, masculine and feminine are not interchangeable; males are not included unless context indicates.
This objection is overturned by the principle that females do not imply males.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ولو غير محصن جلده مائة) لقوله تعالى الزانية والزاني فاجلدوا كل واحد منهما مائة جلدة [النور: ۲] إلا أنه انتسخ في حق المحصن فبقي في حق غيره معمولاً به، ويكفينا في تعيين الناسخ القطع برجم النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فيكون من نسخ الكتاب بالسنة القطعية قوله : ( ونصف للعبد) أي نصف جلد المائة للعبد الزاني فيجلد خمسين سوطاً لقوله تعالى فإن أتين بفاحشة فعليهن نصف ما على المحصنات من العذاب [النساء : ٢٥] والمراد به الجلد لأن الرجم لا يتنصف وإذا ثبت التنصيف في الإماء لوجود الرق ثبت في العبيد دلالة. وما في التبيين من أن العبيد دخلوا في اللفظ وأنث للتغليب مخالف لما في الأصول من أن الذكور لا تتبع الإناث حتى لو قال أمنوني على بناتي لا تدخل الذكور بخلاف أمنوني على بني عم الذكور والإناث .
He said: (And for the non-muhsan, flog him with a hundred lashes) because of the saying of the Most High: 'The fornicatress and the fornicator, flog each one of them with a hundred lashes' [Quran 24:2] except that this was abrogated with respect to the muhsan, so it remains operative for others. And it suffices for us in determining the abrogator the certainty that the Prophet (peace be upon him) stoned, so it is abrogation of the Book by definite sunnah. He said: (And half for the slave) meaning half of the hundred lashes for the slave who commits zina, so he is flogged with fifty lashes because of the saying of the Most High: 'Then if they commit a lewd act, their punishment is half of that prescribed for free women' [Quran 4:25]. And what is meant by it is flogging because stoning cannot be halved. And when the halving is established for female slaves due to the presence of slavery, it is established for male slaves by implication. And what is in al-Tabyin that male slaves are included in the wording and the feminine is used for overwhelming majority contradicts what is in the principles that males do not follow females, so that if one said 'Seek refuge for my daughters', males are not included, unlike if one said 'Seek refuge for my male cousins' which includes males and females.
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq, explaining the ruling for flogging the non-muhsan fornicator and the slave. The author begins by citing the Quranic verse (Surah Nur, 24:2) which commands flogging with 100 lashes. He notes that this verse is abrogated with respect to the muhsan (who receives stoning) as established by the definite sunnah (the Prophet's stoning of Ma'iz and others). Therefore, the 100 lashes apply only to the non-muhsan. Then he explains the matn's phrase 'half for the slave' meaning the slave receives 50 lashes, citing the verse from Surah Nisa (4:25) which mentions half the punishment for female slaves. Since stoning cannot be halved, the verse refers to flogging. This ruling is extended to male slaves by analogy (dilālah). Finally, he addresses an objection from al-Tabyin that the wording uses feminine for inclusion of males, refuting it based on usul al-fiqh principles that masculine and feminine are not interchangeable in such contexts.

Key Terms
غير محصن (ghayr muhsan): A free person who is not muhsan, i.e., has never been married or has not consummated a valid marriage.
نصف للعبد (nisf li al-'abd): Half of the hundred lashes for a slave, i.e., fifty lashes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Quranic 100 lashes apply only to the non-muhsan; the muhsan is stoned; slaves receive half (50 lashes) by explicit verse and analogy.

The Imam's Order: A Condition for Stoning
Ruling that Imam must order stoning; Ma'iz case explained

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that stoning requires the Imam's order and identify the proof from the Ma'iz case.

Core Idea
Stoning cannot be carried out without the Imam's order; his refusal indicates possible retraction.

This lesson examines a crucial procedural safeguard in the implementation of the hadd punishment for zina. The Hanafi school firmly holds that the Imam (or judge) must order the stoning; the people cannot proceed on their own. The case of Ma'iz is analyzed to illustrate how the Prophet's order was sufficient even though he was not physically present. We will also see how the Imam's hesitation serves as a sign of retraction, protecting the accused.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central ruling
The passage begins with a clear ruling: if the Imam refrains from ordering stoning, it is not permissible for the people to stone. This establishes the Imam's order as a necessary condition.
2
Examine the proof from Ma'iz
The text invokes the incident of Ma'iz as evidence: the Prophet ordered stoning but was not present. This shows that the order itself is what matters, not the physical presence of the Imam.
The Prophet's order sufficed, so too an Imam's order.
3
Understand the wisdom behind the Imam's role
The Imam's refusal to order is a sign of possible retraction (imarat al-ruju'). This procedural pause ensures that the punishment is not carried out hastily and that the accused's confession is re-evaluated.
Ali's saying is cited to support this interpretation.
4
Note the recommended practice
The passage ends with a recommendation: those involved in stoning should form rows like prayer rows, stepping back after each throw to avoid injury.
This is a procedural detail for safety.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
امتنع الإمام لا يحل للقوم رجمه ولو أمرهم لعلمهم بفوات شرط الرجم وهو منتف برجم ماعز فإن القطع بأنه عليه السلام لم يحضره بل رجمه الناس بأمره عليه السلام. ويمكن الجواب بأن حقيقة ما دل عليه قول علي رضي الله عنه أنه يجب على الإمام أن يأمرهم بالابتداء اختياراً لثبوت دلالة الرجوع ،وعدمه وأن يبتدئ هو في الإقرار لينكشف للناس أنه لم يقصر في أمر القضاء بأن لم يتساهل في بعض شروط القضاء بالحد، فإذا امتنع حينئذ ظهرت أمارة الرجوع. وفي الحاوي: وينبغي للناس أن يصفوا عند الرجم كصفوف الصلاة وكلما رجم تأخروا وتقدم غيرهم فرجموا اهـ
If the Imam refrains, it is not permissible for the people to stone him. And if he ordered them, they would know that the condition for stoning is lost, and it is negated by the stoning of Ma'iz because it is established that the Prophet (peace be upon him) was not present, rather people stoned him by his order. And it is possible to answer that the reality of what the saying of Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) indicates is that the Imam must order them to start, optionally, for the establishment of the indication of retraction, and that he should start in the confession so that it becomes clear to the people that he did not fall short in the matter of judgment by not being lax in some conditions of judgment by hadd. Then if he refuses at that point, a sign of retraction appears. And in al-Hawi: It is commendable for the people to form rows for stoning like rows of prayer, and whenever they stone, they step back and others come forward and stone.
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage discusses a procedural issue in stoning. If the Imam (or judge) refrains from ordering the stoning, the people cannot proceed with it. The example of Ma'iz is given: the Prophet did not personally stone him but ordered the people to do so, and they did. The commentary then addresses an objection: how can we reconcile the requirement of the Imam's command with the fact that the Prophet was not present during Ma'iz's stoning? The answer is that the Imam must order the people to start (in the case of witnesses) or start himself in the case of confession, to allow the possibility of retraction. If the Imam refrains during the stoning, it is a sign that the person may have retracted. The practice of forming rows for stoning like prayer rows is recommended to avoid hitting each other.

Key Terms
امتنع الإمام (imtana'a al-imam): If the Imam refrains from ordering the stoning.
إمارة الرجوع (imarat al-ruju'): A sign of retraction by the person who confessed.
الرجم (al-rajm): Stoning to death as a hadd punishment for zina.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Imam's order is a necessary condition for the implementation of stoning in the Hanafi school.

The Proper Method of Flogging in Hudud
Explanation of physical method of flogging in hudud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi guidelines for flogging (whip condition, stripping, lash distribution, and areas to avoid) and explain the reasoning behind each rule.

Core Idea
Hadd flogging must deter without destroying: moderate whip, distributed lashes, avoid head, face, and private parts.

Flogging as a hadd punishment is prescribed by Shari'ah for certain offenses. The Hanafi school, drawing from the practice of the Companions and prophetic instructions, has detailed the method of flogging to ensure it serves as a deterrent without causing death or permanent harm. This lesson examines the key rules: the whip must be moderate and knot-free, the offender must be stripped except for covering the private parts, the lashes must be spread over the body, and the head, face, and private parts must be avoided. We also discuss a brief intra-Hanafi difference regarding striking the head.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four key rulings
Extract from the text: (1) the whip must be without a knot (tamrah) and moderate (between harsh and not painful), (2) remove outer clothes but cover the private parts, (3) distribute lashes over the body, (4) avoid the head, face, and private parts.
These are recommended practices, not strict conditions for validity.
2
Understand the rationale for each ruling
The whip without a knot prevents excessive injury; the moderate level ensures pain but not wounding. Stripping increases deterrence. Distribution prevents concentration of strikes that could kill. Avoiding the three areas protects vital senses and beauty, as per the hadith 'Avoid the face and the testicles.'
The underlying principle: hadd is a deterrent, not a killer (zajir, not mutlif).
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on striking the head
The text mentions that Abu Yusuf initially agreed not to strike the head, then later changed to allow it based on a statement of Abu Bakr. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) Hanafi position is to avoid the head, as per al-Hidayah.
The commentator refutes Abu Yusuf by explaining that Abu Bakr's statement referred to enemies in battle, not to hudud.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (بسوط لا تمرة له متوسطاً) أي لا عقدة له لأن علياً رضي الله عنه لما أراد أن يقيم الحد كسر تمرته والمتوسط بين المبرح وهو الجارح وغيره المؤلم لإفضاء الأول إلى الهلاك وخلو الثاني عن المقصود وهو الانزجار؛ كذا في الهداية وحاصله أنه المؤلم غير الجارح قوله : ( ونزع ثيابه وفرق على بدنه إلا رأسه ووجهه وفرجه أي ونزع عنه ثيابه إلا ما يستر عورته لأن علياً رضي الله عنه كان يأمر بالتجريد في الحدود لأن التجريد أبلغ في إيصال الألم إليه، وهذا الحد مبناه على الشدة في الضرب، وفي نزع الإزار كشف العورة فيتوقاه. وإنما يفرق الضرب على أعضائه لأن الجمع في عضو واحد قد يفضي إلى التلف والحد زاجر لا متلف. وإنما يتقي الأعضاء الثلاثة لقوله عليه السلام للذي أمره بضرب الحد «اتق الوجه والمذاكير» ولأن الفرج مقتل والرأس مجمع الحواس وكذا الوجه وهو مجمع المحاسن أيضاً فلا يؤمن من فوات شيء منها بالضرب وذلك إهلاك معنى فلا يشرع حداً. وقال أبو يوسف: يضرب الرأس أيضاً رجع إليه بعد أن كان أولاً يقول لا يضرب كما هو المذهب وإنما يضرب سوطاً لقول أبي بكر رضي الله عنه : اضربوا الرأس فإن فيه شيطاناً. قلنا: تأويله أنه قال ذلك فيمن أبيح قتله ونقل أنه ورد في حربي كان دعاة من الكفرة والإهلاك فيه مستحق
He said: (With a whip that has no knot, moderate) meaning no knot in it, because when Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) wanted to implement the hadd, he broke its knot. And moderate is between harsh, which wounds, and other painful, because the former leads to death and the latter lacks the intended purpose which is deterrence. Thus in al-Hidayah, its gist is that it is painful but not wounding. He said: (And he removes his clothes and distributes [lashes] over his body except his head, face, and private parts) meaning he removes his clothes except what covers his private parts because Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) used to order stripping in hudud because stripping is more effective in causing him pain, and this hadd is based on severity in striking. And removing the lower garment exposes the private parts, so it is avoided. And he distributes the strikes over his limbs because concentrating on one limb may lead to destruction, and the hadd is a deterrent, not a destroyer. And he avoids the three organs because of the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him) to the one he ordered to strike the hadd: 'Avoid the face and the testicles.' And because the private part is fatal, the head is the center of senses, and the face is the center of beauty, so it is not safe from loss of something from them by striking, and that is destruction in meaning, so it is not prescribed as a hadd. And Abu Yusuf said: The head should also be struck, then he retracted after he used to say it should not be struck, as is the madhhab, and he struck with a whip because of the saying of Abu Bakr (may Allah be pleased with him): 'Strike the head because there is a devil in it.' We say: Its interpretation is that he said that regarding one whose killing is permissible, and it is reported that it was about a polytheist who was calling people from the disbelievers, and destruction is deserved in that case.
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage explains the physical method of flogging in hudud. The whip should be free of knots (not harsh) and moderate in strength—painful but not wounding. The person being flogged is stripped of outer clothes but the private parts must remain covered. The lashes are distributed over the body to avoid concentrating on one spot which could cause death. Three areas are specifically avoided: the head, face, and private parts. The head and face are avoided because of potential loss of senses or beauty; private parts are avoided due to risk of death. The Prophet's instruction 'Avoid the face and testicles' is cited. Additionally, the opinion of Abu Yusuf is mentioned: initially he agreed to avoid the head, but later he changed to allow hitting the head based on a statement of Abu Bakr. The commentator refutes this by explaining that Abu Bakr's statement referred to enemies in battle, not to hudud.

Key Terms
سوط (sawt): Whip used for flogging; must be moderate, without knots.
تمرته (tamratahu): The knot at the end of a whip.
مبرح (mubarrih): Harsh or wounding flogging that may lead to death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which parts of the body are avoided during flogging according to the Hanafi school?
A) Head and face
B) Head, face, and private parts
C) Only head
D) Only private parts

Key Takeaway
Hadd flogging must be carried out with a moderate whip, stripping the offender, distributing lashes, and avoiding the head, face, and private parts to ensure it deters without destroying.

Rulings on Flogging Posture and Stoning Pit
Rulings on posture of flogging, stripping for women, and digging pit for stoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on the posture of flogging for men and women, the garments removed from women, and the digging of a pit for stoning, and explain the evidence from the practice of Ali and the Prophet.

Core Idea
Men stand, women sit: flogging posture protects modesty and maximizes deterrent effect.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq details three procedural rules for administering hudud punishments. These rules are based on the practice of the early Muslims and aim to balance the goals of deterrence and modesty. Understanding them clarifies how Hanafi law implements fixed punishments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three rulings
Read the passage and list the three distinct rulings: (1) man flogged standing, not stretched; (2) woman flogged sitting, only fur and padding removed; (3) pit dug for woman in stoning, not for man.
2
Examine the evidence for each
Note the proofs: the saying of Ali (radiAllahu anhu) for flogging postures, and the practice of the Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wa sallam) with Ma'iz and al-Ghamidiyya for the stoning pit.
Hanafi school relies on these as strong precedents.
3
Understand the rationale (hikmah)
Consider why each rule exists: standing for men increases public deterrent effect; sitting for women prevents exposure of 'awrah; removing fur/padding allows pain to reach the body while preserving modesty; digging a pit for women in stoning conceals the body, while men do not require it.
4
Determine the legal nature (hukm)
These rules are sunnah (recommended), not obligatory. If the flogging is done differently (e.g., woman standing), the hadd is still valid but the act is makruh tanzihan.
The Hanafi position box indicates sunnah level.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ويضرب الرجل قائماً في الحدود وغير ممدود) لقول علي رضي الله عنه : تضرب الرجال في الحدود قياماً والنساء قعوداً ولأن مبنى إقامة الحد على التشهير والقيام أبلغ فيه. ثم قوله «غير ممدود» فقد قيل المد أن يلقى على الأرض ويمد كما يفعل في زماننا وقيل أن . السوط فيرفعه الضارب فوق رأسه، وقيل أن يمد بعد الضرب وذلك كله لا يفعل لأنه زيادة على المستحق قوله : (ولا ينزع ثيابها إلا الفرو والحشو) لأن في تجريدها كشف العورة والفرو والحشو يمنعان وصول الألم إلى الجسد والستر حاصل بدونهما فلا حاجة إليهما فينزعان ليصل الألم إلى البدن قوله : وتضرب جالسة لأثر علي رضي الله عنه ولأنها عورة فلو ضربت قائمة لا يؤمن كشف عورتها قوله : ويحفر لها في الرجم (لا له لأن ماعزاً لم يحفر له وحفر للغامدية وهو بيان للجواز وإلا فلا بأس بترك الحفر لها لأنه عليه السلام لم يأمر بذلك والإمساك غير مشروع في المرجوم
He said: (And the man is struck standing in hudud and not stretched out) because of the saying of Ali (may Allah be pleased with him): 'Men are struck in hudud standing, and women sitting.' And because the basis of establishing the hadd is public display, and standing is more effective in that. Then his saying 'not stretched out' — it is said that 'stretched out' means to be thrown on the ground and stretched as is done in our time, and it is said that the whip is raised above the head, and it is said that he is stretched after striking; all that is not done because it is an increase over what is due. He said: (And her clothes are not removed except the fur and padding) because stripping her exposes her private parts, and the fur and padding prevent the pain from reaching the body, and covering is achieved without them, so they are not needed, so they are removed so that the pain reaches the body. He said: (And she is struck sitting) due to the athar from Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) and because she is an 'awrah, so if she were struck standing, it would not be safe from exposure of her private parts. He said: (And a pit is dug for her in stoning, not for him) because Ma'iz was not dug a pit for, and a pit was dug for al-Ghamidiyya, and that indicates permissibility; otherwise there is no harm in leaving digging for her because the Prophet (peace be upon him) did not order it, and restraint is not legislated for the one being stoned.
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage provides several rulings related to the implementation of hadd punishments. Firstly, men are flogged in a standing position, not lying down or stretched, because standing increases notoriety and is more effective as a deterrent. Ali's statement is cited as evidence. Secondly, for women undergoing flogging, only the outer fur and inner padding garments are removed, to allow the pain to reach the body while preserving modesty. Women are flogged sitting to avoid exposure of their private parts. Thirdly, regarding stoning, a pit is dug for the woman being stoned (so her body is partially buried) but not for the man, following the practice of the Prophet with Ma'iz (no pit) and al-Ghamidiyya (pit). This shows that digging is permissible but not obligatory.

Key Terms
ممدود (mamdood): Stretched out; the person is not to be laid flat on the ground during flogging.
فرو (farw): Fur garment worn by women; removed during flogging to allow pain to reach the body.
حشو (hashw): Inner padding in clothing; removed along with the fur during flogging to let pain reach the body.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What garment(s) are removed from a woman during flogging according to Hanafi law?
A) All outer clothes
B) Only the fur and padding
C) Nothing is removed
D) The head covering is removed

Key Takeaway
Hanafi law mandates sitting for women and standing for men during flogging, with minimal garment removal, to balance deterrence and modesty.

Master's Authority to Flog His Slave: Hadd vs Ta'zir
Ruling that master cannot implement hadd without Imam but may administer ta'zir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between hadd and ta'zir in the context of a master's authority over his slave, and state the evidence for each ruling.

Core Idea
The master cannot execute hadd without the Imam's permission, but may administer ta'zir for discipline.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies a critical distinction between two types of punishment: hadd (fixed Shari'ah penalties) and ta'zir (discretionary discipline). While a master has authority over his slave, that authority does not extend to implementing hudud, which are divine rights reserved for the state. However, the master retains the right to discipline his slave through ta'zir. Let us examine the proofs and rationale behind this distinction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what the matn is ruling on: the act of a master flogging his slave. The ruling is that he cannot flog for hadd without the Imam's permission, but he can for ta'zir.
Distinguish between the two types of punishment from the outset.
2
Locate the primary dalil
Find the proof cited: the hadith 'أربع إلى الولاة' in which the Prophet assigned hudud to the rulers. This indicates that hudud are not left to individuals.
The hadith is a hadith ahad, but it is relied upon in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Trace the rational proof
The passage also gives a reason: hadd is a right of Allah because its purpose is to purify society from corruption. Therefore, it must be executed by the one who represents the Shari'ah, i.e., the Imam or his deputy.
This rational argument (talil) supports the textual evidence.
4
Contrast with ta'zir
The text contrasts hadd with ta'zir, which is a right of the slave (or master) and aims at discipline. Hence, the master can administer ta'zir without the Imam's permission.
The distinction is evident in that ta'zir applies even to children and animals, while hadd is restricted.
5
Evaluate the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf is clear: the master must seek the Imam for hadd, but can discipline for lesser matters. This prevents encroachment on state authority and ensures proper execution of divine punishments.
Understanding this helps apply the ruling correctly in real life.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولا يحد عبده إلا بإذن إمامه) لقوله عليه السلام أربع إلى الولاة وذكر منها الحدود ولأن الحد حق الله تعالى لأن المقصود منه إخلاء العالم الفساد ولهذا لا يسقط بإسقاط العبد فيستوفيه من هو نائب عن الشرع وهو الإمام أو نائبه بخلاف التعزير لأنه حق العبد، ولهذا يعزر الصبي وحق الشرع موضوع عنه. قيد بالحد لأن المولى يعزر عبده بلا إذن الإمام لأنه حق العبد وهو المالك والمقصود منه التأديب ولهذا يعزر الصبي والدابة وتقبل فيه الشهادة على الشهادة وشهادة النساء مع الرجال ويصح فيه العفو
He said: (And he does not flog his slave except with the permission of his Imam) because of the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Four things are for the rulers,' and he mentioned among them the hudud. And because the hadd is a right of Allah Almighty, for its purpose is to rid the world of corruption, and therefore it is not dropped by the slave's dropping of it, so it is exacted by the one who represents the Shari'ah, which is the Imam or his deputy, unlike ta'zir because it is a right of the slave. For this reason, a child is disciplined with ta'zir, and the right of the Shari'ah is waived regarding him. It is restricted to hadd because the master administers ta'zir to his slave without the Imam's permission because it is the right of the slave and he is the owner, and its purpose is discipline. For this reason, a child and an animal are disciplined with ta'zir, and testimony upon testimony and testimony of women with men are accepted in it, and pardon is valid in it.
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage discusses the authority to flog a slave. The matn states that a master cannot implement the hadd punishment (such as flogging for zina, qadhf, etc.) on his slave without the permission of the Imam. The proof is the hadith that four matters (including hudud) belong to the rulers. The rationale is that hadd is a right of Allah intended to purify society, so it does not belong to the master and cannot be waived by the slave. It must be executed by the Imam or his deputy. In contrast, ta'zir (discretionary punishment) is a right of the slave (or master) because its purpose is discipline. Therefore, the master can administer ta'zir without Imam's permission. This distinction is further supported by the fact that ta'zir can be applied to children and even animals, and different rules of evidence apply.

Key Terms
حد (hadd): Fixed punishment prescribed by Shari'ah for specific crimes, a right of Allah.
تعزير (ta'zir): Discretionary punishment left to the judge or master; a right of the individual.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Can a master flog his slave for zina without the Imam's permission?
A) Yes, absolute
B) No, unless it is ta'zir
C) Yes, with condition
D) No, never

Key Takeaway
A master cannot execute hadd punishments on his slave without the Imam's permission; only ta'zir remains within his authority.

Conditions of Ihsan for Stoning
Definition and conditions of ihsan for stoning in Hanafi fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five conditions of ihsan and identify which persons qualify as muhsan for stoning according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Ihsan requires freedom, accountability (adulthood + sanity), Islam, and valid marriage with consummation — missing any one prevents stoning.

In the Hanafi law of hudud, the hadd of stoning (rajm) applies only to a person who is muhsan. The term ihsan has a precise technical meaning. This lesson parses the conditions laid out in Kanz al-Daqaiq and explains why a slave, child, insane person, or disbeliever cannot be muhsan.

Guided Path
1
Identify the list of conditions
Read the matn and note the five components listed as conditions for ihsan: freedom (hurriyah), accountability (taklif = adulthood and sanity), Islam (islam), and valid marriage with consummation (wath' fi nikah sahih).
The matn explicitly states 'freedom, accountability, Islam, and intercourse in a valid marriage'.
2
Examine the rationale for each condition
The commentary explains why each missing condition prevents ihsan: slave cannot marry independently, child/insane lack legal capacity for the act to be zina, disbeliever is excluded by hadith.
The hadith 'Whoever associates partners with Allah is not muhsan' is cited.
3
Distinguish conditions of ihsan from conditions for zina
Note that accountability (taklif) is a condition for both the act of zina and for ihsan. The child or insane person's act is not legally considered zina, so they cannot be muhsan.
The text says 'otherwise, the act of a child or insane person is not zina at all'.
4
Apply the conditions to hypothetical cases
Test each condition on a person to determine if they are muhsan. For example, a free adult Muslim who has never married is not muhsan because the marriage condition is missing.
This step consolidates understanding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وإحصان الرجم والحرية والتكليف والإسلام والوطء بنكاح صحيح وهما بصفة الإحصان) فالعبد ليس محصناً لأنه غير متمكن بنفسه من النكاح الصحيح المغني عن الزنا، ولا الصبي والمجنون لعدم أهلية العقوبة والتكليف شرط لكون الفعل زنا وإنما جعله شرط الإحصان لأجل قوله وهما بصفة «الإحصان وإلا ففعل الصبي والمجنون ليس بزنا أصلاً. ولا الكافر للحديث من أشرك بالله فليس بمحصن ورجمه عليه السلام اليهوديين إنما كان
He said: (And the ihsan for stoning: freedom, accountability, Islam, and intercourse in a valid marriage, and they both have the description of ihsan.) So the slave is not muhsan because he is not able by himself to have a valid marriage that would suffice against zina. Nor is the child or insane person because they lack the capacity for punishment, and accountability is a condition for the act to be zina; and he only made it a condition of ihsan because of his saying 'and they both have the description of ihsan'; otherwise, the act of a child or insane person is not zina at all. Nor is the disbeliever, because of the hadith: 'Whoever associates partners with Allah is not muhsan,' and the Prophet's stoning of the two Jews was only...
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage defines the conditions of ihsan that make a person subject to stoning for zina. The matn lists five conditions: freedom, accountability (taklif: sanity and adulthood), Islam, and valid sexual intercourse in a valid marriage. The commentary explains that slaves are not muhsan because they lack the ability to enter a valid marriage independently (they need master's permission). A minor or insane person is not muhsan because their act is not zina in the first place (they are not legally accountable). A disbeliever is not muhsan based on the hadith that shirk negates ihsan. The reference to the Prophet stoning the Jews is mentioned, but the passage is incomplete; it likely explains that stoning the Jews was due to their own law, not because they were muhsan in Islam.

Key Terms
إحصان (ihsan): The state of being muhsan, which makes stoning applicable for zina.
محصن (muhsan): A person who meets all conditions of ihsan and is subject to stoning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which condition of ihsan excludes a non-Muslim who commits zina from being stoned?
A) Freedom
B) Adulthood
C) Islam
D) Valid marriage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school defines ihsan with five specific conditions; any missing condition changes the punishment from stoning to flogging.
