Avoiding Head and Private Parts in Hadd Flogging
Prohibition of striking head, face, and private parts in hadd

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on avoiding the head, face, and private parts during hadd flogging and explain the reasoning and response to the opposing proof.

Core Idea
Striking head, face, and private parts in hadd is prohibited—they are fatal or sensitive areas whose injury amounts to extra-legal destruction.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on which body parts must be avoided when administering hadd flogging. The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents the ruling from Kanz al-Daqa'iq, provides the rationale, and addresses an objection attributed to Abu Yusuf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is striking specific body parts during hadd flogging. The ruling is prohibition (haram); the text says it is 'not legislated'.
The default ruling for any act not authorized by the Lawgiver is prohibition when it entails harm.
2
Locate the dalil for the prohibition
The dalil is rational (qiyas): the private part is a fatal spot, the head is the center of senses, and the face is the center of beauties. Striking them risks destruction (itlaf) which is not the purpose of hadd.
No explicit Qur'an or hadith is cited for this specific prohibition; it is derived from the general principle of preventing destruction.
3
Trace the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Yusuf initially held that the head may be struck, citing the hadith of Abu Bakr: 'Strike the head for therein is a shaytan.' He later retracted to the majority position.
The text says 'raja'a ilayhi' indicating he returned to the madhhab.
4
Analyze the response to the opposing dalil
The Hanafi response interprets Abu Bakr's hadith as specific to war captives whose killing is permitted, not to hudud offenders. Thus, it does not override the prohibition.
This is an example of takhsis (specification) of a general text by context.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon ruling is to avoid the head, face, and private parts. Abu Yusuf's initial view is not acted upon.
The text confirms this as the madhhab.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحدود يمد وفرجه ويضرب الرجل قائماً في الحدود وغير ممدود ولا ينزع ثيابها إلا الفرو والحشو وتضرب جالسة ويحفر لها في الرجم لا له ولا يحد عبده إلا بإذن إمامه وأحصان الرجم الحرية والتكليف والإسلام والوطء بنكاح صحيح وهما بصفة الإحصان ولا والمذاكير» ولأن الفرج مقتل والرأس مجمع الحواس وكذا الوجه وهو مجمع المحاسن أيضاً فلا يؤمن من فوات شيء منها بالضرب وذلك إهلاك معنى فلا يشرع حداً. وقال أبو يوسف: يضرب الرأس أيضاً رجع إليه بعد أن كان أولاً يقول لا يضرب كما هو المذهب وإنما يضرب سوطاً لقول أبي بكر رضي الله عنه : اضربوا الرأس فإن فيه شيطاناً. قلنا: تأويله أنه قال ذلك فيمن أبيح قتله ونقل أنه ورد في حربي كان دعاة من الكفرة والإهلاك فيه مستحق
Book of Hudud: He is stretched and his private part [avoided], and the man is struck standing in hudud and not stretched out, and her clothes are not removed except the fur and stuffing, and she is struck sitting, and a pit is dug for her in stoning not for him, and he does not execute hadd on his slave except with permission of his imam, and the ihsan of stoning is freedom, legal responsibility, Islam, and intercourse with a valid marriage, and both are with the description of ihsan, and the testicles? Because the private part is a fatal spot, and the head is the center of senses, and likewise the face which is the center of beauties also, so it is not safe from loss of something from them by striking, and that is destruction in meaning, so it is not legislated as a hadd. And Abu Yusuf said: The head is also struck; he returned to it after he first said it is not struck as is the madhhab, and rather he strikes with a whip due to the saying of Abu Bakr may Allah be pleased with him: Strike the head for therein is a shaytan. We said: Its interpretation is that he said that regarding one whose killing is permitted, and it is transmitted that it occurred regarding a war captive who was a caller from the disbelievers, and destruction therein is warranted.
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This is a ruling-with-proof passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. The author first quotes the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq listing several rulings on hadd execution, then focuses on the prohibition of striking the head, face, and private parts. The rationale is that these areas are fatal or may cause loss of senses or beauty, which would amount to extra-legal destruction. Abu Yusuf's opinion that the head should be struck is then refuted by interpreting Abu Bakr's statement as applying to those already condemned to death, not to hudud. The relied-upon position (al-mu'tamad) is to avoid these areas.

Key Terms
الفرج (al-farj): Private parts; in context, the genital area which is a fatal spot if struck hard.
المذاكير (al-madhākīr): Testicles; specifically prohibited to strike due to extreme sensitivity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is striking the head prohibited in hadd flogging according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because the head is the seat of the shaytan.
B) Because the head is a fatal spot.
C) Because the head is the center of senses.
D) Both A and C.

Key Takeaway
Striking the head, face, and private parts in hadd flogging is prohibited because it risks destruction that is not part of the legislated punishment.

Posture During Hadd Flogging for Men
Ruling on posture during hadd flogging

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the posture of a man during hadd flogging, identify its proof (dalil), and explain the prohibition of stretching and its rationale.

Core Idea
A man must stand during hadd flogging for maximum public deterrence; any stretching is excess.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the precise physical method of flogging for men in hudud punishments. The matn is concise but the commentary unpacks three specific prohibitions related to stretching. Understanding this ruling requires grasping both the proof from the Sahaba and the underlying objective of tashhir (public deterrence).

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its hukm level
The matn states the man is struck standing and not stretched out. The hukm is wajib: standing is required and stretching is prohibited.
This is a condition of the flogging, not a recommended practice.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the saying of Ali (رضي الله عنه): 'Men are struck in hudud standing and women sitting.' This is a Qawl Sahabi, accepted as evidence in Hanafi usul.
The thubut is zanni, but the dalalah is qat'i according to the commentary.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The rationale is that hadd is based on tashhir (public deterrence), and standing is more effective for that purpose. The command from Ali directly establishes the ruling, and the rationale strengthens it.
This shows the Hanafi method of combining naql and ma'qul.
4
List the three interpretations of 'not stretched'
The commentary mentions three meanings: (1) not thrown on the ground and stretched, (2) not raising the whip above the head, (3) not stretching after the blow. All are prohibited as additions beyond the prescribed punishment.
These are derived from the term 'mamdud' and its common usage.
5
Understand why all stretching is prohibited
Stretching in any form is an excess (ziyadah) beyond what is legally required, thus it invalidates the hadd or makes the striker liable.
This principle prevents escalation of punishment beyond the shari'ah limits.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ويضرب الرجل قائماً في الحدود وغير ممدود) لقول علي رضي الله عنه : تضرب الرجال في الحدود قياماً والنساء قعوداً ولأن مبنى إقامة الحد على التشهير والقيام أبلغ فيه. ثم قوله «غير ممدود» فقد قيل المد أن يلقى على الأرض ويمد كما يفعل في زماننا وقيل أن السوط يرفعه الضارب فوق رأسه، وقيل أن يمد بعد الضرب وذلك كله لا يفعل لأنه زيادة على المستحق
His saying: (And the man is struck standing in hudud and not stretched out) due to the saying of Ali may Allah be pleased with him: Men are struck in hudud standing and women sitting, and because the foundation of establishing the hadd is on publicizing, and standing is more effective in that. Then his saying 'not stretched out': It has been said that 'madd' is that he is thrown on the ground and stretched as is done in our time, and it is said that the whip is raised above his head by the striker, and it is said that he is stretched after the striking. All of that is not done because it is an addition beyond what is deserved.
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the manner of flogging for men. The matn states the man is struck standing and not stretched out. The author provides the proof from Ali's instruction. The rationale is that hadd is meant to be a public deterrent, and standing enhances publicity. Then three interpretations of 'not stretched out' are given: (1) not thrown on the ground and stretched, (2) not raising the whip above the head, (3) not stretching after the blow. All are prohibited as exceeding the prescribed punishment.

Key Terms
ممدود (mamdūd): Stretched out on the ground; prohibited in hadd flogging.
تشهير (tashhīr): Public exposure/deterrence; purpose of hadd.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentary, why is the man struck standing and not stretched?
A) To increase the pain.
B) For better publicity and deterrence.
C) Because Ali said so without reason.
D) To avoid injury to the back.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires a man to stand upright during hadd flogging, and prohibits any form of stretching, to maximize public deterrence.

Clothing of Woman During Flogging: Removal of Fur and Stuffing
Ruling on removing woman's clothes except fur and stuffing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on which clothes are removed from a woman during hadd flogging and explain the rationale (talil) that balances modesty and pain delivery.

Core Idea
Remove only the fur and stuffing: modesty preserved, pain delivered.

In hadd punishments, a woman's modesty must be maintained even during flogging. The Hanafi school specifies that only two types of garments are removed: the outer fur coat and any inner padded clothing. This ruling ensures that the lash reaches the body effectively without exposing the 'awrah unnecessarily.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the passage and note that it states: 'Her clothes are not removed except the fur and stuffing.'
The phrase 'لا ينزع ثيابها إلا الفرو والحشو' is the core ruling.
2
Understand the rationale (talil)
The text gives two reasons: (1) stripping all clothes would uncover the private parts (calling for modesty), and (2) fur and stuffing prevent the pain from reaching the body (defeating the purpose of flogging).
The word 'لأن' introduces the cause: 'because in stripping her there is uncovering of the private parts, and the fur and stuffing prevent the arrival of pain to the body.'
3
Contrast with what is not removed
Note that ordinary clothes (e.g., a dress, shirt) are left on. Only items that block pain (thick fur or padding) are removed.
The text says 'فرو وحشو' are removed; other garments remain to preserve modesty.
4
Extract the legal principle
The ruling is not arbitrary; it balances two competing objectives: avoiding harm (uncovering 'awrah) and achieving the purpose of punishment (pain). The Hanafi principle here is that a wajib (obligatory) action must be carried out in a way that minimizes unnecessary harm.
This is an example of applying the maxim 'الضرر يزال' (harm must be removed) and 'الضرورات تبيح المحظورات' (necessities permit prohibitions), but only to the extent needed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولا ينزع ثيابها إلا الفرو والحشو) لأن في تجريدها كشف العورة والفرو والحشو يمنعان وصول الألم إلى الجسد والستر حاصل بدونهما فلا حاجة إليهما فينزعان ليصل الألم إلى البدن
His saying: (And her clothes are not removed except the fur and stuffing) because in stripping her there is uncovering of the private parts, and the fur and stuffing prevent the arrival of pain to the body, while covering is achieved without them, so there is no need for them, so they are removed so that pain may reach the body.
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling on a woman's clothing during hadd flogging. Only two items are removed: the fur (outer garment) and the stuffing (inner padding). Reason: removing all clothes would expose her private parts, which is prohibited. The fur and stuffing block pain, so they are removed to ensure the flogging is effective, while modesty is maintained with the remaining clothes.

Key Terms
الفرو (al-farw): Fur garment worn over clothes; removed to allow pain.
الحشو (al-ḥashw): Stuffing or padding worn under clothes; removed to allow pain.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why are the fur and stuffing removed from a woman during flogging?
A) To humiliate her.
B) Because they block pain; without them pain reaches the body.
C) Because they are impure.
D) Because the Prophet ordered their removal.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school mandates removal of only the fur and stuffing to balance effective punishment with modesty.

Posture of Woman During Hadd Flogging
Ruling on posture of woman during hadd flogging

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that a woman must be flogged sitting during hadd and explain the proof from the tradition of Ali (RA) and the rational basis of covering 'awrah.

Core Idea
A woman must be flogged sitting to preserve modesty; standing risks exposing her ‘awrah.

In this lesson, we examine a specific ruling within hudud: the posture of a woman when she receives the flogging punishment. The matn states clearly that she is struck sitting, and the commentary provides both a textual proof from the companion Ali ibn Abi Talib (RA) and a rational argument based on modesty. Understanding this ruling highlights how Hanafi fiqh integrates textual evidence with the principle of covering ‘awrah (satr al-‘awrah), even in the context of punishment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is flogging a woman as a hadd punishment. The ruling is that she must be struck sitting (qa‘idatan). This is stated in the matn: 'wa tudrabu jalisatan'.
The ruling is specific to women; men are flogged standing.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is an athar (tradition) from Ali ibn Abi Talib (RA), reported as: 'Men are struck standing and women sitting.' This is a qawl sahabi (saying of a companion).
This athar is considered zanni al-thubut (single transmission) but its meaning is clear.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'tudrabu' (she is struck) in the passive imperative implies obligation (wujub). The differentiation by gender makes sitting an explicit required element for women.
In Hanafi usul, the command (amr) indicates obligation unless there is a qarinah to the contrary.
4
Note the rational argument
The text also gives a rational reason: 'li-annahā ‘awrah' (because she is a private part). If she stands, her ‘awrah might become uncovered during the flogging. This is a ma‘qūl (intellectual) proof that supports the textual one.
This demonstrates istihsan or istidlal bil-ma‘na, not contradictory to the text.
5
Evaluate the cross-madhhab status
While the Hanafi school holds that sitting is wajib, other schools (e.g., Shafi‘is) may not differentiate posture by gender. The practical consequence is that in a Hanafi context, the flogger must seat the woman; otherwise, he sins.
The authority weight here is from al-Bahr al-Ra’iq, upholding the position as mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وتضرب جالسة) لأثر علي رضي الله عنه ولأنها عورة فلو ضربت قائمة لا يؤمن كشف عورتها
His saying: (And she is struck sitting) due to the tradition of Ali may Allah be pleased with him, and because she is a private part, so if she were struck standing, it is not safe from uncovering of her private parts.
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling that a woman must be flogged sitting down. The proof is from Ali's instruction, and the rationale is that a woman's body is considered 'awrah (to be covered). If she stands, her private parts may become exposed during the flogging. Therefore, sitting is obligatory to maintain modesty.

Key Terms
عورة (‘awrah): Area that must be covered; here the woman's entire body is considered 'awrah in public flogging.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is a woman struck sitting during hadd?
A) Because standing is more painful.
B) To avoid uncovering her private parts.
C) Because the Quran commands it.
D) Because it is easier for the executioner.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi hadd flogging, a woman must be struck sitting to preserve her modesty, based on the tradition of Ali and the principle of covering 'awrah.

Digging a Pit for Stoning: Woman Only
Ruling on digging a pit for the woman in stoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on digging a pit for stoning, identify the prophetic evidence, and distinguish the rulings for men and women.

Core Idea
A pit is dug for the woman in stoning, not for the man—following the Prophet's practice, not a command.

In the procedure of stoning for zinā, a practical question arises: should a pit be dug for the offender? This passage from al-Bahr al-Rā’iq clarifies the Hanafi position: a pit is dug for the woman but not for the man. The evidence comes from the Prophet's treatment of Ma'iz (no pit) and al-Ghamidiyyah (pit). The author emphasizes that this is a matter of permissibility, not obligation, and that restraint (imsāk) is not legislated—the condemned may flee.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and Its Scope
The ruling is that a pit should be dug for a woman sentenced to stoning, but not for a man. Identify the act (digging) and the legal category (mubah/permissible, or sunnah as some later authorities hold).
2
Locate the Prophetic Evidence
The proof is the practice of the Prophet: for Ma'iz (male) no pit was dug; for al-Ghamidiyyah (female) a pit was dug. This is a sunnah fi'liyyah (prophetic action).
The evidence is zannī in both transmission and indication.
3
Understand the Nature of the Evidence
The action is a clarification of permissibility (bayān al-jawāz), not a command. The Prophet did not order digging; he simply did it for the woman and omitted it for the man. Thus, digging is not obligatory and omitting it is not sinful.
The phrase 'wa huwa bayān li’l-jawāz' is key.
4
Note the Related Rule on Restraint
The passage ends with 'al-imsāk ghayr mashrū‘' – restraining the condemned is not legislated. This means the person may run; if they escape, they are not to be chased or held back. This is a separate but related procedural point.
This is based on another hadith not quoted here.
5
Contrast with Other Schools
Some other schools require digging for both genders or consider it obligatory. Identify the practical difference (thamarah) in implementation.
Hanafis differentiate based on the prophetic example.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ويحفر لها في الرجم لا له) لأن ماعزاً لم يحفر له وحفر للغامدية وهو بيان للجواز وإلا فلا بأس بترك الحفر لها لأنه عليه السلام لم يأمر بذلك والإمساك غير مشروع في المرجوم
His saying: (And a pit is dug for her in stoning, not for him) because Ma'iz was not dug for him, and it was dug for al-Ghamidiyyah, and this is a clarification of permissibility, otherwise there is no harm in leaving digging for her because the Prophet peace be upon him did not command that, and restraint (holding back) is not legislated for the one being stoned.
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage addresses the stoning procedure. A pit is dug for the woman to sit in so her 'awrah is covered, but not for the man. The proof is from the practice of the Prophet: Ma'iz (a male) was not dug for, while al-Ghamidiyyah (a female) was. The author clarifies that digging is permissible but not obligatory; if it is not dug, there is no sin, as it is not a command. The statement about 'imsaak' (restraint) means that the person being stoned should not be held back; they are allowed to run if they can escape, per other hadiths not quoted here.

Key Terms
الإمساك (al-imsāk): Holding back or restraining the person being stoned; not legislated in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why do Hanafis rule a pit should be dug for a woman but not for a man in stoning?
A) Because women are weaker and need to be contained.
B) Because the Prophet did not dig for Mā‘iz and dug for al-Ghāmidiyyah.
C) Because a Quranic verse commands it.
D) Because the man's ʿawrah is more exposed.

Key Takeaway
Digging a pit for stoning is a permissive sunnah for women only, based on the prophetic precedent, and is not obligatory.

Conditions of Ihsan for Stoning
Definition and conditions of ihsan required for stoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the four conditions of ihsan and identify which individuals are not considered muhsan according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Ihsan requires freedom, sanity, Islam, and consummated valid marriage; without these, stoning does not apply.

The hadd penalty for zina (unlawful sexual intercourse) is not uniform; it depends on the offender's legal status. The most severe form, stoning, applies only to a muhsan—a person who has enjoyed the full pleasure of a valid marriage. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq parses the precise conditions that constitute ihsan, clarifying who is excluded and why. By mastering these conditions, you will be able to apply the correct hadd in cases of zina.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four pillars of ihsan
The text opens by listing four conditions: freedom, legal responsibility (taklif: adulthood and sanity), Islam, and valid marital intercourse with a muhsan partner. Note that both the man and the woman must be muhsan for stoning to apply to each.
2
Recognize those who are categorically not muhsan
The author enumerates specific categories: slaves, children, insane persons, disbelievers (with a note that the Prophet's stoning of Jews was abrogated), unmarried persons, married but not consummated, and those who consummated with a non-muhsan (e.g., dhimmi, slave, minor).
The hadith 'al-thayyib bi al-thayyib' shows that thayyib (non-virgin) status requires consummation.
3
Understand the definition of consummation (dukhul)
Consummation is defined as insertion of the glans (or its equivalent); ejaculation is not required. This follows the same standard as for ghusl (ritual bath).
The absence of ejaculation does not negate ihsan because satisfaction is assumed from insertion.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on return of ihsan after insanity
The majority holds that if one loses ihsan due to insanity, it returns upon recovery without requiring new consummation. Abu Yusuf disagrees, requiring re-consummation with the spouse.
The mufta bihi is the majority view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وإحصان الرجم الحرية والتكليف والإسلام والوطء بنكاح صحيح وهما بصفة الإحصان) فالعبد ليس محصناً لأنه غير متمكن بنفسه من النكاح الصحيح المغني عن الزنا، ولا الصبي والمجنون لعدم أهلية العقوبة والتكليف شرط لكون الفعل زنا وإنما جعله شرط الإحصان لأجل قوله وهما بصفة «الإحصان وإلا ففعل الصبي والمجنون ليس بزنا أصلاً. ولا الكافر للحديث من أشرك بالله فليس بمحصن ورجمه عليه السلام اليهوديين إنما كان بحكم التوراة قبل نزول آية الرجم ثم نسخ ولا من لم يتزوج لعدم تمكنه من الوطء الحلال، ولا من تزوج ولم يدخل بها للحديث الثيب بالثيب ) والثيابة لا تكون بغير دخول، ولأنه لم يستغن عن الزنا والدخول إيلاج الحشفة أو قدرها ولا يشترط الإنزال كما في الغسل لأنه شبع. ولا من دخل بغير المحصنة كمن دخل بذمية أو أمة أو صغيرة أو مجنونة لوجود النفرة عن نكاح هؤلاء لعدم تكامل النعمة ولا من دخل بامرأة محصنة ولم يكن محصناً وقته وصار محصناً وقت الزنا لما ذكرنا من عدم تكامل النعمة. ولو زال الإحصان بعد ثبوته بالجنون أو العته يعود محصناً إذا أفاق، وعند أبي يوسف لا يعود حتى يدخل بامرأته بعد الإفاقة.
His saying: (And the ihsan for stoning is freedom, legal responsibility, Islam, and intercourse by valid marriage, and both are with the description of ihsan.) So the slave is not muhsan because he is not able by himself to have a valid marriage that suffices him from zina; nor the child or insane due to lack of capacity for punishment, and legal responsibility is a condition for the act to be zina, but it is made a condition of ihsan for the sake of his saying 'both are with the description of ihsan', otherwise the act of a child or insane is not zina at all. Nor the disbeliever due to the hadith: 'Whoever associates partners with Allah is not muhsan', and his stoning of the two Jews was by the ruling of the Torah before the revelation of the verse of stoning, then abrogated. Nor one who has not married due to lack of ability for lawful intercourse; nor one who married but did not consummate, due to the hadith 'the thayyib with the thayyib', and thayyib cannot be without consummation, and because he has not been free from need of zina; and consummation is insertion of the glans or its equivalent, and ejaculation is not required as in ghusl because it is [a sign of] satisfaction. Nor one who consummated with a non-muhsan, like one who consummated with a dhimmiyya, a slave girl, a minor, or an insane woman, due to the aversion to marriage with these due to lack of complete pleasure. Nor one who consummated with a muhsana woman but he was not muhsan at the time and became muhsan at the time of zina, due to what we mentioned of lack of complete pleasure. And if ihsan is removed after being established by insanity or imbecility, he returns to being muhsan when he regains sanity; according to Abu Yusuf, he does not return until he consummates with his wife after recovery.
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This is a detailed parsing of the conditions of ihsan (the state that makes stoning obligatory for adultery). Ihsan requires four conditions: freedom (not a slave), legal responsibility (adulthood and sanity), Islam, and valid marital intercourse with a muhsan partner. The author then lists who is not muhsan: slaves, children, insane, disbelievers (the hadith of stoning Jews is abrogated), unmarried, married without consummation, and those who consummated with a non-muhsan. The definition of consummation is insertion of the glans; ejaculation is not required. If ihsan is lost due to insanity, it returns upon recovery according to the majority; Abu Yusuf requires re-consummation.

Key Terms
الإحصان (al-iḥṣān): The legal state making stoning obligatory; requires freedom, sanity, Islam, and previous valid marital intercourse.
الثيب (al-thayyib): A non-virgin; one who has had valid marital intercourse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a condition for ihsan according to the passage?
A) Freedom.
B) Legal responsibility.
C) Having children.
D) Valid marital intercourse.

Key Takeaway
Ihsan for stoning requires four conditions: freedom, legal responsibility, Islam, and consummated valid marriage with a muhsan partner; the absence of any condition reduces the penalty to flogging.

Hadd for a Dhimmi Who Converts: Evidence and Ihsan
Fatwa on hadd for dhimmi after conversion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions under which hadd is applied or dropped for a dhimmi who converts after committing zina, and explain how ihsan can be proven for stoning.

Core Idea
Conversion does not automatically drop hadd; it depends on how the crime was proven.

This passage from the Fatawa of Qari' al-Hidayah and al-Hawi al-Qudsi clarifies a critical nuance in hudud: the fate of a dhimmi who commits zina (or theft) and then embraces Islam. The ruling hinges on the type of evidence that established the crime. Additionally, it addresses how ihsan (marital status) can be proven to justify stoning, even if the accused denies it. These distinctions are essential for understanding the Hanafi approach to evidence and punishment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is zina (or theft) by a dhimmi who later converts. The ruling is that hadd may be applied or dropped based on the evidence.
Focus on the two scenarios: Muslim testimony/confession vs. dhimmi testimony.
2
Determine the condition for hadd to be applied
If the crime was proven by the dhimmi's own confession or by the testimony of Muslims, hadd is still executed after conversion.
Conversion does not erase the established crime in these cases.
3
Determine the condition for hadd to be dropped
If the crime was proven only by dhimmi witnesses, then conversion causes the hadd to be dropped.
Dhimmi testimony is considered less reliable in such cases, and conversion is seen as a new status.
4
Analyse the second fatwa on ihsan
Al-Hawi al-Qudsi discusses how ihsan can be proven for stoning: either by the accused having a child from his wife (indicating consummation) or by testimony of two men or a man and two women.
Denial of ihsan does not block stoning if these proofs exist.
5
Apply the ruling to practical scenarios
Consider various combinations of evidence and conversion timing to determine when hadd is enforced.
The key is the source of evidence, not the timing of conversion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي فتاوى قارئ الهداية المسماة بالسراجية : إذا سرق الذمي أو زنى ثم أسلم إن ثبت ذلك عليه بإقراره أو بشهادة المسلمين لا يدرأ عنه الحد، وإن ثبت بشهادة أهل الذمة فأسلم لا يقام عليه الحد وسقط عنه وفي الحاوي القدسي : وإن شهد عليه أربعة بالزنا فأنكر الإحصان وله امرأة قد ولدت منه فإنه يرجم وإن لم تكن ولدت منه وشهد بالإحصان رجلان أو رجل وامرأتان رجم اهـ .
And in the Fatawa of Qari' al-Hidayah called al-Sirajiyyah: If a dhimmi stole or committed zina and then became Muslim, if that is established against him by his confession or by the testimony of Muslims, the hadd is not repelled from him; and if it is established by the testimony of dhimmis and he becomes Muslim, the hadd is not executed on him and it is dropped. And in al-Hawi al-Qudsi: And if four testify against him for zina and he denies ihsan but he has a wife who has given birth to a child from him, then he is stoned; and if she has not given birth and two men or a man and two women testify to his ihsan, he is stoned.
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage cites two fatwa sources. The first, from Qari' al-Hidayah, states that if a dhimmi commits zina or theft and then converts to Islam, the hadd is enforced if proven by Muslim testimony or confession, but dropped if proven only by dhimmi witnesses. The second, from al-Hawi al-Qudsi, discusses a case where four witnesses testify to zina but the accused denies ihsan. If his wife has given birth to a child from him, that serves as evidence of consummation, and he is stoned. Otherwise, testimony of two men or a man and two women to his ihsan is sufficient for stoning.

Key Terms
الذمي (al-dhimmī): A non-Muslim living under Muslim protection with a covenant.
الإحصان (al-iḥṣān): Legal status of being married and having consummated the marriage, which makes a convicted adulterer liable to stoning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is the hadd dropped for a dhimmi who converts to Islam after committing zina?
A) If he confessed before conversion.
B) If the crime was proven by dhimmi witnesses only.
C) If he converts before the trial.
D) If he was never muhsan.

Key Takeaway
A dhimmi's conversion drops hadd only when the crime was proven by dhimmi witnesses; if proven by confession or Muslim testimony, hadd is enforced.
